~
眼熟
Often used with the verb 看 (kàn), as in 看眼熟 (kàn yǎnshu).

~
档
The meaning "crosspiece" is only used for furniture like tables, shelves, etc. meaning the horizontal crosspieces. Don't use it for something like the crosspiece of a crucifix. When used to mean "vendor's open-air stall," it is usually reduplicated as 档档 (dàngdàng).


~
屏幕
No special notes.

~
过于
Be careful about word order.  过于 always comes *before* the adjective or adverb it modifies. For example, “too expensive” is  过于昂贵 (guòyú ánguì), *not* 昂贵过于 (ánguì guòyú).

~
成员
No special notes.

~
当中
Can function as a noun, meaning "the middle."  In this context, it's often used with the preposition 在 (zài) to create the phrase 在…当中 (zài... dāngzhōng).  For example, 在人群当中 (zài rénqún dāngzhōng) means "in the middle of the crowd."

~
就算
就算 is stronger than 即使 (jíshǐ) or 哪怕 (nǎpà).  It conveys a feeling of concession, as if the speaker is reluctantly admitting something to be true for the sake of argument.


~
男
Can be used as a prefix before other words to form compounds that specifically refer to men's fashion, restrooms, and so on.

~
含义
No special notes.

~
收益
No special notes.

~
建成
The resultative complement 成 (chéng) emphasizes completion of the construction project.

~
火箭
No special notes.

~
外交官
No special notes.

~
动人
Can be used more broadly than "moving" or "touching" in English.  It can also describe something beautiful or captivating.

~
收费
Can also be used as a noun, meaning "fee" or "charge."

~
食堂
No special notes.

~
连续剧
No special notes.

~
边
When used as a suffix for locations, it adds a sense of vagueness or approximation, like "nearby" or "around." For example, "outside" can be 外边 (wàibian), with 边 having this nuance.

~
资产
No special notes.

~
赶忙
Implies a sense of urgency, suggesting that something needs to be done quickly because of a pressing situation.

~
战场
Figuratively, it can refer to any fiercely competitive or challenging environment, such as a "commercial battlefield" (商业战场 shāngyè zhànchǎng).

~
祖母
No special notes.

~
富有
Can describe not only material wealth but also abundance in abstract qualities.

~
雨衣
No special notes.

~
上下
In the sense of "about" or "approximately," 上下 is placed *after* the number it modifies.

~
职责
A more formal and stronger term than 责任 (zérèn), implying a sense of assigned duty and accountability, often in a professional or official context.

~
用法
No special notes.

~
语音
When referring to the act of sending a voice message, the term 语音 is often combined with the verb 发 (fā) to form the phrase 发语音 (fā yǔyīn), which means "to send a voice message."

~
精
Has many specific meanings depending on context.

~
冲击
Implies a sudden and powerful force, often causing significant disturbance or change.

~
包装
Can also refer to the way something is presented or marketed, especially the visual aspects like design and labeling.

~
铜牌
No special notes.

~
膜
Can refer to a variety of thin, flexible materials, not just biological membranes.

~
指出
Often used in formal contexts, such as academic discussions or official reports, to highlight a specific fact, error, or issue.

~
全身
No special notes.

~
妙
Can be used as an exclamation of admiration or appreciation, similar to "Wonderful!" or "Brilliant!" in English.

~
系列
Often used with the measure word 个 (gè).

~
猴
Can be used figuratively to describe someone who is mischievous or restless.

~
超出
Implies exceeding a limit or boundary, often with negative connotations, suggesting something is beyond what's allowed or expected.

~
杀毒
Often used together with the word 软件 (ruǎnjiàn), which means "software," to form the term 杀毒软件 (shādú ruǎnjiàn), which means "antivirus software."

~
散文
Formal written style essays are typically referred to as 散文.  More informal essays, such as those written by students, are called 作文 (zuòwén).

~
全
This can be tricky to use correctly. When referring to all of a group of people, 全 should be placed *before* the measure word, e.g. 全家人 (quánjiārén), 全班同学 (quánbān tóngxué). However, if there is no measure word, 全 should be placed *after* the noun. For example, we say "the whole world" as 全世界 (quánshìjiè).

~
好人
In addition to meaning "a good person", 好人 can also have a sarcastic meaning, referring to someone who is too afraid of offending others to act according to their principles.

~
快点儿
儿 (er) is a retroflex suffix which makes the tone gentler and more urging.

~
共有
共有 is most often used in the written language.

~
至
至 is a more formal way of saying 到 (dào).

~
此次
此次 is more formal than 这次 (zhè cì).

~
登山
登山 is the act of climbing a mountain as a sport or leisure activity. For ascending a mountain as a means of transport, use 上山 (shàngshān).

~
请进
Only used to invite someone *in*. To invite someone to go first, use 您先 (nín xiān).

~
遇
遇 has the nuance of something happening unexpectedly.

~
宇航员
This word is mostly used in a scientific context.  In more informal settings, 太空人 (tàikōngrén) is preferred.

~
常年
常年 can refer to all seasons of the year, or it can refer to the average value of something over many years.

~
沟
沟 is somewhat formal.  More informal synonyms include 水沟 (shuǐgōu) and 水渠 (shuǐqú).

~
替
替 means to replace someone, implying they are not present.  If someone is present and you're doing their work for them, use 帮 (bāng) instead.

~
回国
回国 is used only for returning to one's *own* country.  To go back to any other country, use 回 (huí).

~
徒弟
A related word is 学生 (xuéshēng). In general, 徒弟 (túdì) emphasizes the master-apprentice relationship, where skills and knowledge are passed down through personal training and mentorship. It carries a sense of tradition and lineage. On the other hand, 学生 (xuéshēng) emphasizes the teacher-student relationship, which can be more formal and institutionalized. A 徒弟 (túdì) is often seen as a successor or inheritor of the master's craft, whereas a 学生 (xuéshēng) is primarily a learner.

~
欢乐
欢乐 is usually used for large-scale celebrations.

~
整治
整治 is most often used in the context of solving problems or making changes.

~
猜测
The result of 猜测 is not necessarily accurate.  For a guess that might be accurate, use 推测 (tuīcè).

~
祝
祝 is mostly used in formal settings.  In informal settings, use 希望 (xīwàng).

~
肩
The most common word using 肩 is 肩膀 (jiānbǎng), shoulder.

~
油
油 has many meanings depending on context. Most often it means either cooking oil or petroleum.

~
男生
男生 is exclusively used for boys enrolled in school.  For adult men, use 男人 (nánrén).

~
攻击
攻击 has the meaning of proactively harming someone, whether physically or otherwise.  For harm inflicted passively, use 伤害 (shānghài).

~
送礼
送礼 can have a negative meaning, suggesting bribery.

~
开夜车
The origin of this word comes from working very late, with the only cars on the road being night buses.

~
全体
全体 is a formal way of saying 全部 (quánbù).

~
高于
高于 suggests that the value of something has surpassed a certain benchmark, but the values can still be compared side by side.  高出 (gāochū) is used for values that are clearly incomparable.

~
握
握 usually implies a tight grip.  For holding something gently, use 拿 (ná).

~
储存
储存 refers to long-term storage.  For short-term storage, use 存放 (cúnfàng).

~
车
车 can refer to any wheeled vehicle, not just cars.

~
引
引 has the nuance of bringing something from one place to another.

~
初期
初期 is usually immediately followed by a noun.

~
揭
揭 is usually used for something that has previously been hidden, such as a conspiracy.  For taking off the lid of a container, use 打开 (dǎkāi).

~
还有
还有 can be tricky for English speakers to use correctly.  It can be used either at the beginning of a phrase or in the middle, but these correspond to quite different meanings.

~
将要
将要 is mostly used in written language.

~
显出
显出 emphasizes that something hidden has now been revealed.

~
属
属 can be used in many ways and is therefore quite difficult to master.

~
答复
答复 is more formal than 回答 (huídá).

~
原始
原始 describes something unchanged since the beginning of time, while 原来 (yuánlái) describes something unchanged since a more recent point in time.

~
作 (zuō, high-maintenance)
This slang usage of 作 (zuō) is particularly common online and among younger speakers.  It describes someone who is overly dramatic, attention-seeking, or creates unnecessary drama.  Think of the English slang terms "extra," "high-maintenance," or "drama queen/king."

~
围 (wéi, to wear by wrapping around)
This meaning usually applies to items like scarves, shawls, or sashes that are draped or wrapped around the neck or shoulders.

~
相互 vs 互相
While often interchangeable, 相互 emphasizes a two-way interaction, while 互相 is more general and can involve multiple parties.  相互 also has a slightly more formal tone.

~
愁 (chóu)
愁 often implies a deeper, more lingering worry or anxiety compared to 担心 (dānxīn), which is more about concern or being worried.

~
侧 (cè, incline/lean)
This meaning is more figurative, referring to favoring one side in an argument or tending towards a particular viewpoint.

~
昏 (hūn, dull/muddle-headed)
This can describe a person's mental state, suggesting they are slow-witted, confused, or not thinking clearly.

~
配套 (pèitào)
This word emphasizes the completeness and compatibility of a set of items, often used for equipment, facilities, or services designed to work together.

~
号召 (hàozhào)
This implies a more formal and public call to action, often by a leader or organization, urging people to participate in a cause or movement.

~
埋 (mái, used in 埋怨)
This word is almost exclusively used in the compound 埋怨 (mányuàn), meaning "to complain" or "to blame."

~
那边 (nàbiān)
Besides its literal meaning, 那边 can also be used figuratively to refer to a different perspective or standpoint in a discussion.

~
打官司 (dǎ guānsi)
This term generally refers to civil lawsuits, not criminal cases.  For criminal cases, terms like 提起公诉 (tíqǐ gōngsù - to initiate public prosecution) are used.

~
间 (jiān, measure word)
As a measure word for rooms, 间 counts the enclosed spaces within a building, not necessarily the function of the room.

~
线 (xiàn, tier)
This slang usage categorizes cities based on their economic development and importance, with "first-tier" cities being the most developed.

~
地板 (dìbǎn)
Specifically refers to the finished flooring surface, not the subfloor.

~
节假日 (jiéjiàrì)
This refers to official public holidays, including traditional festivals and national holidays.

~
外科 (wàikē)
This refers to the surgical department or the field of surgery in general.  Specific surgical specialties have their own terms, e.g., 心脏外科 (xīnzàng wàikē - cardiac surgery).

~
开机 (kāijī)
In computing contexts, this can refer to both starting up a computer and restarting a computer that's already on (similar to "reboot").

~
不幸 (bùxìng)
This word carries a more formal and serious tone than simply saying "unfortunate."

~
不顾 (bùgù)
This emphasizes a deliberate disregard for something, often despite potential negative consequences.

~
族 (zú, social group)
This extended usage often appears in compounds like 上班族 (shàngbānzú - office workers) or 月光族 (yuèguāngzú - people who spend their entire monthly salary).

~
胆小 (dǎnxiǎo)
Often used to describe children or someone's personality in general, not necessarily a specific instance of fear.

~
对付 (dùfu, to get by with)
This usage often implies using something as a makeshift solution or managing with limited resources.

~
指着 (zhǐzhe)
This can also mean "to rely on" or "to depend on," especially when referring to a source of income or support.

~
做饭 (zuòfàn)
This refers to cooking a meal, not just individual dishes.

~
先锋 (xiānfēng)
This also carries a connotation of innovation and pushing boundaries, particularly in art, culture, or social movements.

~
偏 (piān, stubbornly/contrary to expectations)
This usage implies that something happens despite efforts to prevent it or goes against what is expected.

~
下去 (xiàqù)
This can also be used to encourage someone to continue doing something or to signal that an activity should proceed.

~
扇 (shàn, classifier)
As a classifier, 扇 is used for doors, windows, and other objects with flat, hinged or detachable parts.

~
别的 (biéde)
别的 usually follows a noun or pronoun, while 其他 (qítā) can stand alone.

~
据 (jù, according to)
Often used to introduce information from a source or authority, similar to "according to reports" or "based on evidence."

~
想不到 (xiǎngbudào)
Can also express surprise or disbelief at something unexpected.

~
低于 (dīyú)
Specifically refers to a numerical value being lower than another.

~
指示 (zhǐshì)
Often used in formal contexts for official directives or instructions from superiors.

~
盒 (hé)
Generally refers to a small container, often for gifts or small items.

~
男孩儿 (nánháir)
The 儿 (er) suffix adds a colloquial and affectionate tone.

~
吉祥 (jíxiáng)
Often used for traditional Chinese symbols and decorations associated with good luck and fortune.

~
出汗 (chūhàn)
Specifically refers to the act of sweating, while 汗 (hàn) refers to the sweat itself.

~
预备 (yùbèi)
Implies making preparations in advance for a future event or action.

~
值班 (zhíbān)
Refers to being on duty for a specific period, often in a work or professional context.

~
站住
This word is usually used as a command, like "Halt!" or "Stop right there!".

~
大妈
Although 大妈 technically means "aunt," it's often used colloquially to refer to any middle-aged or elderly woman, similar to how "auntie" is used in some English-speaking cultures.  It can be considered slightly informal and sometimes carries a stereotypical connotation of being gossipy or meddlesome.

~
热点
While 热点 can refer to a physical hot spot, it's more commonly used figuratively to mean a trending topic or a focal point of public attention, like a "hot topic" in English.

~
十足
十足 can mean "100 percent" or "completely," but it's often used to emphasize the degree of something, similar to "fully" or "utterly" in English. For example, 十足的傻瓜 (shízú de shǎguā) means "a complete fool."  When referring to colors, it implies a pure, unmixed shade.

~
娃娃
娃娃 can refer to both a doll and a baby/young child. The context usually makes it clear which meaning is intended.

~
好转
好转 implies a positive change in a situation that was previously negative or unfavorable, like a recovery from illness or an improvement in economic conditions.

~
密
密 has several meanings, including "thick," "dense," "secret," and "close." The intended meaning depends on the context.  For example, 密林 (mìlín) means "dense forest," while 秘密 (mìmì) means "secret."

~
制约
制约 implies mutual restriction or limitation, where one factor influences and controls another, and vice versa.  It's often used in discussions of checks and balances or constraints on power.

~
身高
身高 specifically refers to a person's height.

~
征服
征服 implies a complete and decisive victory or subjugation, often through force or struggle.  It carries a stronger connotation than simply "winning" or "overcoming."

~
从没
从没 emphasizes that something has *never* happened in the past. It's stronger than simply saying 没 or 没有.

~
慰问
慰问 refers to expressing sympathy, concern, or support, often in times of difficulty or hardship. It can involve visiting someone, sending a message, or offering practical assistance.

~
倒闭
倒闭 specifically refers to a business going bankrupt or closing down.

~
联盟
联盟 implies a formal agreement or partnership between groups or individuals for a common purpose, often political or economic.

~
病
病 can refer to both a specific illness or disease and the general state of being sick.

~
面条儿
面条儿 is the colloquial term for noodles, especially in northern China.  面条 (miàntiáo) is the more standard term.  The "儿" (er) suffix adds a colloquial touch.

~
自杀
自杀 specifically means to take one's own life.

~
但
但 is a conjunction meaning "but" or "however." It introduces a contrast or exception to the preceding clause.

~
渡
渡 has multiple meanings related to crossing or getting through something. It can refer to crossing a river, overcoming a difficulty, or ferrying something across.

~
渴望
渴望 implies a strong, intense desire or longing for something, often something difficult to attain.

~
注射
注射 specifically refers to administering a substance through injection.

~
就是说
就是说 is used to clarify or rephrase something that has just been said. It's similar to "in other words" or "that is to say."

~
奶牛
奶牛 specifically refers to a cow raised for milk production, a dairy cow.

~
父母
父母 refers to both parents, mother and father.

~
如下
如下 introduces a list or explanation that follows. It means "as follows" or "as below."

~
在内
在内 means "including" or "within," indicating that something is included in a larger group or set.

~
窗子
窗子 is a more colloquial term for window, while 窗户 (chuānghu) is more formal.

~
器官
器官 refers to a bodily organ, a specialized part of the body with a specific function.

~
相比
相比 introduces a comparison between two things. It's similar to "compared to" or "in comparison with."

~
一贯
一贯 implies consistency and unchanging behavior or policy over a long period.

~
不错
不错 means "not bad" or "pretty good." It can also mean "correct" or "right."

~
寺
寺 generally refers to a Buddhist temple.

~
兴趣
兴趣 refers to interest in something, either as a general curiosity or a specific hobby.

~
言语
言语 refers to spoken words or language. It can also mean "to speak" or "to tell."

~
网上
网上 means "online" or "on the internet."

~
想法
想法 refers to an idea, opinion, or way of thinking.

~
巧
巧 has multiple meanings, including "skillful," "coincidental," and "opportune."

~
中年
中年 refers to middle age, typically the period between 40 and 60 years old.

~
败
败 has multiple meanings related to failure, defeat, or decay. It can mean "to defeat," "to lose," "to fail," or "to wither."

~
写字台
写字台 refers specifically to a writing desk, a desk designed for writing.

~
口试
There is no difference between the use of 口试 in Chinese and "oral exam" in English.

~
一部分
There is no difference between the use of 一部分 in Chinese and "a part" in English.

~
梦见
There is no difference between the use of 梦见 in Chinese and "dream of" or "dream about" in English.

~
为止
This word is usually used with 到 or 至. Note that sometimes 为止 can be omitted.

~
进去
The opposite of this word is 出来 (chūlái).

~
户外
There is no difference between the use of 户外 in Chinese and "outdoors" in English.

~
招生
There is no difference between the use of 招生 in Chinese and to "enroll students" or "recruit students" in English.


~
奏
When 奏 means "to play music," it is usually used for classical or traditional music. For pop music, one would usually just use 弹 (tán) or 唱 (chàng).


~
晚会
There is no difference between the use of 晚会 in Chinese and "evening party" in English.

~
板
There are many meanings of this word.  Be sure to consider the context.

~
轮
Be careful to differentiate between this character and 论 (lùn, theory; discuss).

~
过后
There is no difference between the use of 过后 in Chinese and "afterwards" or "after" in English.


~
台上
There is no difference between the use of 台上 in Chinese and "on stage" or "on the stage" in English.

~
当年
当年 can also mean "that very same year."

~
图片
There is no difference between the use of 图片 in Chinese and "picture" or "photograph" in English.

~
步
步 can also mean "stage" (as in a stage of a process), or "situation."

~
次数
There is no difference between the use of 次数 in Chinese and "number of times" or "frequency" in English.

~
首席
There is no difference between the use of 首席 in Chinese and "chief" in English.

~
退票
退票 can also mean for the ticket to "bounce," as in a check.


~
女
This character is also used as a radical for other characters, such as 妈 (mā, mother).

~
装备
There is no difference between the use of 装备 in Chinese and "equipment" or "to equip" in English.

~
跌
跌 (diē) is usually for physical falls, whereas 倒 (dǎo) can be more abstract.


~
误
There is no difference between the use of 误 (wù) in Chinese and "mistake," "error," or "to miss" in English.

~
玩儿
There is no difference between the use of 玩儿 (wánr) in Chinese and "to play" or "to have fun" in English.

~
外卖
外卖 can also refer to the takeout business itself, or a takeout meal.

~
赢得
There is no difference between the use of 赢得 (yíngdé) in Chinese and "to win" or "to gain" in English.

~
撑
撑 has many meanings, such as "to support," "to prop up," "to push or move with a pole," "to maintain," "to open or unfurl," and "to fill to bursting point." It is usually better translated based on context than by memorizing every meaning.

~
公鸡
There is no difference between the use of 公鸡 (gōngjī) and "rooster" or "cock" in English.

~
可
可 (kě) has many functions, including but not limited to:
* Can; may
* (prefix) -able
* certainly; very (for emphasis)

~
只管
只管 (zhǐguǎn) means "just (one thing, no need to worry about the rest)." There is no single perfect equivalent in English.  It can often be translated as "by all means," "please feel free," "do not hesitate," etc.

~
来到
来到 (láidào) is more literary than the more common 到 (dào).

~
整
整 (zhěng) has several meanings and usages.  Its basic meaning is "whole" or "complete." But before a measure word, it can also mean "whole." And before *or* after a number plus a measure word, it means "exactly."  It can also mean "to put in order," "to repair," or even (colloquially) "to mess with."

~
文娱 (wényú)
There is no difference between the use of 文娱 in Chinese and "cultural recreation" or "entertainment" in English.

~
箱子
There is no difference between the use of 箱子 (xiāngzi) in Chinese and "chest," "bin," "box," "case," "trunk," or "suitcase" in English.

~
体检 (tǐjiǎn)
This word is an abbreviation for 体格检查 (tǐgé jiǎnchá).

~
眼泪
There is no difference between the use of 眼泪 (yǎnlèi) in Chinese and "tear" or "tears" in English.

~
加速
There is no difference between the use of 加速 (jiāsù) in Chinese and "speed up," "accelerate," or "quicken" in English.

~
石油
There is no difference between the use of 石油 (shíyóu) in Chinese and "oil" or "petroleum" in English.

~
遍地
There is no difference between the use of 遍地 (biàndì) and "everywhere" or "all around" in English.

~
大于
There is no difference between the use of 大于 (dàyú) in Chinese and "greater than" or "more than" in English.

~
窗口 (chuāngkǒu) - While 窗口 can refer to a physical window, it's also frequently used in a more abstract sense to mean "a point of contact or access," such as a customer service window or a specific time slot.  In computing, it refers to a window in a graphical user interface.

~
一口气 (yīkǒuqì) -  This can mean "in one breath," implying something is done quickly or without interruption. It can also express doing something in one go, like finishing a task or eating something all at once.  It often carries a connotation of effort or exertion.

~
宝石 (bǎoshí) -  宝石 generally refers to precious stones used in jewelry. While it can encompass a broader range of stones than just gems, it usually implies some degree of value and beauty.

~
虎 (hǔ) -  Besides meaning "tiger," 虎 can also be used figuratively to describe someone fierce, brave, or powerful.  It's a common component in idioms and sayings.

~
干涉 (gānshè) -  干涉 carries a stronger negative connotation than simply "interfering." It implies meddling in something that isn't one's business and often suggests an unwelcome or forceful intrusion.

~
不久 (bùjiǔ) -  Be mindful of the context. 不久 can mean both "soon" (in the future) and "not long ago" (in the past). The surrounding words will clarify the intended meaning.

~
焦点 (jiāodiǎn) -  焦点 can refer to both the literal focal point of a lens and the figurative focus of attention or discussion.

~
旅店 (lǚdiàn) -  旅店 generally refers to a smaller, more basic hotel or inn.  It often implies a budget-friendly option.

~
签字 (qiānzì) -  签字 specifically means to sign one's name, as opposed to just any mark.

~
完了 (wánle) - This word has two very distinct meanings: (1) something is finished/completed. (2) Something is ruined/the person is in trouble.  The context is critical.  The tone also plays a crucial role.  A neutral tone usually indicates completion, while a distressed or exasperated tone indicates ruin.

~
赛场 (sàichǎng) -  赛场 refers specifically to the venue or location of a competition, not just any field or track.

~
食品 (shípǐn) -  食品 refers to processed or prepared food items, rather than raw ingredients.

~
卷 (juǎn) -  卷 has many meanings, be sure to use the correct measure word.  For books, paintings and scrolls, use 本 (běn).  For other rolled items, use 卷 (juǎn).

~
相声 (xiàngsheng) - 相声 is a traditional Chinese comedic performance involving witty banter, puns, and humorous storytelling, usually performed by two people.

~
中等 (zhōngděng) -  中等 means "medium" or "average" and often implies being in the middle of a range or ranking.

~
杰出 (jiéchū) -  杰出 implies a high degree of excellence or distinction, often in a specific field or area.

~
评 (píng) -  评 can encompass a range of evaluative actions, from commenting and reviewing to criticizing and judging.

~
直升机 (zhíshēngjī) - 直升机 is a helicopter.

~
有用 (yǒuyòng) -  有用 simply means "useful" or "helpful."

~
品 (pǐn) -  品 has a wide range of meanings. As a verb, it emphasizes careful appreciation or savoring, often related to taste, art, or character. As a noun, it can refer to quality, grade, or category.

~
体积 (tǐjī) - 体积 specifically refers to the three-dimensional space occupied by an object, its volume.

~
排行榜 (páihángbǎng) - 排行榜 refers to a ranked list, often used for things like best-selling items, top-rated movies, or popular music.

~
修复 (xiūfù) - 修复 implies restoring something to its original state or repairing something that has been damaged.

~
内地 (nèidì) - 内地 has different meanings depending on the context. In mainland China, it typically refers to the mainland area excluding Hong Kong, Macau, and Taiwan.  In other contexts, it can simply mean "inland" or "interior."  In Taiwan, it used to refer to Japan during their colonization of Taiwan.

~
请教 (qǐngjiào) - 请教 is a polite and respectful way to ask for advice or guidance from someone with more knowledge or experience.

~
一点点 (yìdiǎndiǎn) - This emphasizes a very small amount, a little bit.

~
柜子 (guìzi) -  柜子 refers to a cupboard, cabinet, or similar storage furniture.

~
看出 (kànchū) -  看出 means to discern or perceive something that might not be immediately obvious, to "see through" a situation or person.

~
真相 (zhēnxiàng) - 真相 refers to the true facts of a situation, often implying that they were previously hidden or obscured.

~
夺取 (duóqǔ) - 夺取 implies forcefully seizing or taking something, often through struggle or competition.

~
铁路 (tiělù) -  铁路 refers specifically to a railway system or network of tracks, rather than just a single rail.

~
读书 (dúshū) -  读书 can mean both "to read" and "to study," often in a formal academic setting.

~
皮包 (píbāo) -  皮包 generally refers to a leather bag, often a purse, briefcase, or handbag.

~
军人 (jūnrén) -  军人 refers to military personnel in general, encompassing soldiers, officers, and other members of the armed forces.

~
短片 (duǎnpiàn) -  短片 refers to a short film or video clip.

~
混合 (hùnhé) - 混合 implies a thorough blending or mixing of different elements or substances.

~
保密 (bǎomì) -  保密 means to keep something confidential or secret.

~
绝 (jué) -  绝 has several meanings, ranging from "absolutely" and "extremely" to "cut off" and "extinct." Pay close attention to the context.

~
小孩儿 (xiǎoháir) -  小孩儿 is a common and informal term for "child."

~
生活费 (shēnghuófèi) -  生活费 refers specifically to money allocated for living expenses, such as food, rent, and utilities.

~
慢热
Can be used to describe people, products, or sports performance.  For people, it suggests someone who takes time to open up in relationships. For products, it refers to things that gain popularity gradually. In sports, it describes athletes who take a while to reach peak performance in a game or match.

~
冷水
Figuratively, 冷水 can be used to describe plans that are not yet ready or finalized.  It implies that the plans are still in their early stages and need further development.

~
话
The many meanings of 话 can be difficult. Note the specific measure words for 话.

~
衣架
This refers to any kind of clothes hanger, including those made of wood, plastic, or metal. It can also refer to a clothes stand or rack.

~
总
总 has many meanings, but they are all related to the idea of "all" or "every".

~
话剧
This specifically refers to modern drama, as opposed to traditional Chinese opera (戏曲 - xìqǔ).

~
领带
No special notes.

~
门诊
This refers specifically to outpatient services at a hospital or clinic, as opposed to inpatient services (住院 - zhùyuàn).

~
列
列 can refer to both columns and rows (in Taiwan). However, in mainland China, it typically refers to columns. 行 (háng) is used for rows.

~
登
登 has a literal meaning of ascending or climbing. It can also mean to publish or record something, or to enter information into a register. In some dialects, it can also mean to put on shoes or trousers.

~
铺
铺 has several meanings, including to spread or display something, to set up a bed or shop, and even to refer to a shop or store itself.

~
愤怒
This describes a stronger emotion than just being annoyed or upset. It implies a sense of injustice or outrage.

~
地面
This refers to the surface of the ground or floor, not the earth itself.

~
期
期 is used both for general lengths of time as well as specific, enumerated instances of a periodical publication or installment.

~
创立
This emphasizes the act of establishing something new, like a company, organization, or theory.  It implies originality and innovation.

~
拉开
This signifies pulling something open with a distinct separation, like opening curtains, a drawer, or a zipper.  It also means to increase a gap or distance.

~
人间
This term often carries a poetic or philosophical connotation, referring to the world of human experience and emotions.

~
逼
Be careful using this character. Aside from its usual meaning, it is also a euphemistic variant of a vulgar word.

~
不便
This word expresses a sense of difficulty or awkwardness in a situation. It can also refer to being short of cash.

~
那么
那么 can be used to emphasize the degree of something, meaning "so" or "so very much."  It can also be used in a conditional sense, meaning "in that case."

~
地带
This refers to a specific area or region with distinct characteristics, often geographic or functional.

~
办事处
This term denotes a smaller office or branch of a larger organization, typically located in a different city or region.

~
高尚
This describes a person's moral character, indicating nobility, integrity, and refined qualities.

~
海边
This refers specifically to the area along the coast, including the beach and nearby land.

~
低温
In a medical context, 低温 can refer to hypothermia.

~
风度
This term usually applies to men and describes a refined and elegant demeanor, encompassing grace, charm, and composure.

~
强大
This emphasizes both physical and non-physical strength, such as military power, economic influence, or a robust spirit.

~
不免
This conveys a sense of inevitability or unavoidability, often due to external circumstances.

~
山谷
This refers specifically to a valley between mountains or hills.

~
高度
高度 can refer to physical height, altitude, or a high degree of something abstract, like importance or achievement.

~
凉水
This refers to water that is cool or cold, but not necessarily chilled or iced.  It also implies unboiled water.

~
学年
This specifically refers to the academic year, typically from September to June or July.

~
声
声 can refer to both the physical sound and its quality, as well as a person's reputation or the tone of their speech.

~
一流
This signifies the highest level of quality or excellence, often used to describe people, products, or services.

~
分解
This can refer to both physical and abstract decomposition, such as breaking down a substance chemically or analyzing a complex problem into smaller parts.

~
悲惨
This describes a situation of extreme suffering and misfortune, often evoking feelings of pity and sadness.

~
诚信
This combines the concepts of honesty and trustworthiness, emphasizing sincerity and integrity in one's actions and words.

~
横
横 has several meanings related to horizontal and unreasonable/violent, but these are all separate concepts.

~
增强
This signifies an increase in strength, power, or intensity, often through deliberate effort or improvement.

~
清洁
This describes something that is clean and free from dirt or impurities. It can also refer to the act of cleaning.

~
无限
Can be used as an adjective before a noun, or as an adverb before a verb.  When used as an adjective, it can mean "infinite", "limitless", "unlimited", or "unbounded". When used as an adverb, it means "infinitely", "limitlessly", "unlimitedly", or "unboundedly".

~
合并
This word can be used to describe the merging of two or more things into one, such as companies, departments, or territories. It can also be used to describe the act of combining two or more things together.

~
学者
This word refers to someone who is highly educated and knowledgeable in a particular field of study. It can also refer to someone who is actively engaged in research and scholarship.

~
火车
Measure word is 列 (liè).  Other measure words such as 节 (jié), 班 (bān), and 趟 (tàng) can be used in certain contexts, but 列 is the most common and general measure word for 火车.

~
响声
响声 (xiǎngshēng) refers to any sound, noise, or din. It can be used to describe both pleasant and unpleasant sounds.

~
凶
凶 (xiōng) is a multipurpose character that primarily signifies "fierce," "ominous," "terrible," or "vicious." It can also pertain to "murder," "famine," or be a variant of another character with the same pronunciation.

~
援助
This can be a noun or a verb.

~
物业
While 物业 (wùyè) generally translates to "property" or "real estate," it often specifically refers to property management services in a residential or commercial complex.  It encompasses tasks like maintenance, security, and administrative duties within the property.

~
争
While commonly meaning "contend," "dispute," or "fight," 争 (zhēng) also carries the sense of striving or vying for something, as in 竞争 (jìngzhēng) - to compete. It less commonly implies a deficiency or asks "how" or "what" in certain dialects or literary contexts.

~
拥有
拥有 (yōngyǒu) specifically emphasizes possession and ownership, unlike other verbs for "to have" like 有 (yǒu). It signifies having control, rights, or enjoyment of something.

~
康复
康复 (kāngfù) denotes the process of regaining health and strength after illness or injury.  It implies a return to a normal or improved physical and mental state.

~
查
查 (chá) carries a broader meaning than simply "check". It encompasses investigating, examining, and looking up information. It implies a more thorough and detailed examination than a simple check.

~
动物园
No additional notes.

~
坡
The measure word for 坡 (pō) is 个 (gè), which might seem unusual for a physical feature.

~
薄弱 (bóweak ruò)
No additional notes.

~
等候 (děnghòu)
No additional notes.

~
补习 (bǔxí)
No additional notes.

~
住房 (zhùfáng)
No additional notes.

~
场面 (chǎngmiàn)
No additional notes.

~
难看 (nánkàn)
No additional notes.

~
个体 (gètǐ)
No additional notes.

~
刷子 (shuāzi)
No additional notes.

~
就是 (jiùshì)
就是 (jiùshì) has multiple uses.  When used for emphasis, it means "precisely" or "exactly." It can also mean "just" or "simply" and functions as "only" in certain situations.  In correlation with 也 (yě), it becomes "even" or "even if."

~
想到 (xiǎngdào)
想到 (xiǎngdào) implies the act of something coming to mind or being recalled, rather than active contemplation.  It also carries the nuance of anticipating something.

~
大爷 (dàyé)
大爷 (dàyé) has several meanings. Besides referring to one's father's elder brother or a respectful term for an older man, it can also denote an arrogant idler or self-centered show-off, particularly in Beijing dialect.

~
船只 (chuánzhī)
No additional notes.

~
开幕 (kāimù)
Primarily used for events, rather than physical openings.

~
气温 (qìwēn)
No additional notes.

~
转动 (zhuàndòng)
转动 (zhuàndòng) emphasizes rotational movement, turning around an axis or revolving, distinct from other movement verbs.

~
迷信 (míxìn)
迷信 (míxìn) doesn't merely refer to superstitions; it also denotes the act of blindly believing in them, often with negative connotations.

~
从不 (cóngbù)
从不 (cóngbù) is a strong and absolute term for "never," conveying a complete lack of occurrence throughout a period.

~
晚点 (wǎndiǎn)
Specifically used in the context of transportation being delayed or behind schedule.

~
签名 (qiānmíng)
No additional notes.

~
不成 (bùchéng)
不成 (bùchéng) has varied uses. It expresses disapproval or failure ("won't do").  It signifies inability and can form rhetorical questions at the end of sentences.

~
心里 (xīnlǐ)
Refers to thoughts and feelings, not literal heart.

~
职工 (zhígōng)
Refers to both staff and workers within an organization.

~
有害 (yǒuhài)
No additional notes.

~
西北 (xīběi)
Can refer to both a direction and a geographical region in China.

~
悲伤 (bēishāng)
No additional notes.

~
银牌 (yínpái)
No additional notes.

~
周
Can mean "all over" (e.g., 全世界都周游了一遍 - travelled all over the world). This meaning is less common now though.

~
北部
A more colloquial way to say 北部 is simply 北边.

~
好多
As well as meaning "many", this can also mean "much better" when referring to one's health.

~
边境
边境 is usually used to refer to land borders. If you want to talk about maritime borders, you should use 海疆.

~
挣钱
A more colloquial way to say 挣钱 is simply 赚钱.

~
吊
Can mean "to lament" or "to condole with" (e.g., 吊唁 - to offer one's condolences). It can also be used to mean "terrible" or "bad" (e.g., 这电影真吊 - this film is terrible).


~
行李
行李 is more formal than 行李箱 (suitcase).

~
地下
地下 can refer to the subway (e.g., 我们坐地下 - let's take the subway). This meaning is specific to Northern China.

~
节奏
节奏 can be used figuratively to mean "pace" (e.g., 我们加快节奏 - let's pick up the pace).

~
葡萄酒
A shorter and more colloquial word for this is simply 酒.

~
藏
As well as "to hide," this can also mean "to harbor" (e.g., 藏污纳垢 - to harbor filth).

~
稿子
Can refer to any type of written work, not just a manuscript (e.g., 发言稿 - speaking notes).

~
药水
This is also used in online gaming slang to refer to "potion".

~
心
This can also mean "intention" or "the core of something" (e.g.,  良苦用心 - good intentions).

~
风暴
Often used metaphorically (e.g.,  金融风暴 - financial crisis).

~
国外
More formal than 海外.  Both mean "abroad" or "overseas."

~
在家
Can also be used as a noun, meaning "householder" or "layman" (as opposed to a monk or a nun).

~
早晨
More formal than 早上.

~
前景
前景 usually carries a positive connotation.

~
称为
More formal than 叫 or 叫做.

~
战略
A common collocation is 战略伙伴 (strategic partner).

~
前提
Often used with the preposition 以…为前提 (on the premise of…).

~
祖国
祖国 is a more emotive and patriotic word than 国家.

~
付
Can also classify sets or pairs of things (e.g., 一付手套 - a pair of gloves).


~
研究所
Can also mean "graduate school".

~
高层
Can refer to literal height (e.g., 高层建筑 - high-rise building), or metaphorically to high-ranking officials (e.g., 高层领导 - high-level leaders).

~
登录
Besides online login, it can also mean "to board" (e.g.,  飞机 - board a plane).

~
那里
Can be used figuratively to mean "that sort of thing" (e.g.,  我不是那样的人 - I'm not that kind of person).

~
听众
Refers specifically to radio listeners.  For a general audience, use 观众.

~
从小
Implies something began in childhood and continues to the present.

~
开通
Can refer to the opening of a transportation route (e.g.,  开通地铁 - open a subway line). Can also mean "open-minded".

~
异常
Can mean "extremely" or "exceptionally", in addition to "abnormal" (e.g., 异常美丽 - exceptionally beautiful).

~
疗养
Implies a longer period of rest and recuperation than simply 休息.

~
哈哈
This is an onomatopoeia for laughter.  Be careful not to overuse it in writing, as it can seem informal.

~
长度
Can also refer to duration of time.

~
唱片
Now refers to CDs and digital albums as well as vinyl records.

~
教育部
This refers specifically to the Ministry of Education of the People's Republic of China.

~
争议
This word implies a more formal or public dispute than simple disagreement.

~
传出
Can mean "to leak out," particularly of rumors or news (e.g.,  消息传出 - news leaked out).

~
变形
Can be used metaphorically (e.g.,  政策变形 - policy distortion).

~
下班
Can be used as a noun ("after work") or a verb ("to get off work").


~
离不开
The literal translation is "cannot leave". It emphasizes dependence or necessity, not just fondness or attachment.  Think of it as "can't live without", "can't function without", "absolutely need", "essential to," "inextricably linked to."


~
乡
While 乡 can technically mean "country," it usually refers to a smaller administrative unit, like a township or village, especially in official contexts. For "country" in the general sense, use 国家 (guójiā).


~
炒作
Often carries a negative connotation, implying artificial or manipulative promotion.  It's similar to "hype" or "sensationalize" in English.  A more neutral term would be 宣传 (xuānchuán), meaning "to publicize" or "to promote".


~
胜负
Encompasses both victory and defeat, often referring to the uncertain outcome of a competition.  It's not just about winning or losing, but the overall contest itself.


~
带有
Indicates something has a certain characteristic, often an unintended or secondary one. It's not the primary defining feature but rather a nuance.  "Tinged with" or "having a trace of" might be good translations in some cases.


~
慢车
Specifically refers to a train or bus that makes frequent stops, hence its slow speed. It's not just any slow-moving vehicle.


~
学时
Refers to a period of academic instruction, similar to "credit hour" or "contact hour".  It's a unit of educational measurement.


~
多次
Indicates an action repeated many times, usually unspecified but more than a few.  It stresses repetition more than a precise number.


~
拐
Has various meanings depending on context. Pay attention to the specific meaning being used. For the meaning related to kidnapping, note that it's written the same way for both simplified and traditional.


~
倒是
Used to express a mild surprise or contrast. Often translates to "actually," "on the contrary," or "unexpectedly."  It shifts the direction of the conversation or introduces a slightly different perspective.


~
贺卡
Generally used for congratulatory or celebratory occasions. For condolences or sympathy, use 慰问卡 (wèiwèn kǎ).


~
队伍
Refers to an organized group of people, often in a line or formation.  It can refer to queues, processions, troops, or even teams in a broader sense.  Choose the appropriate measure word depending on the context: 个 (gè) is general, 支 (zhī) is for organized groups like branches or detachments, and 条 (tiáo) is for lines or processions.


~
停下
Indicates a complete cessation of movement or activity.  It emphasizes the state of being stopped rather than the process of stopping.


~
车主
Specifically refers to the legal owner of a vehicle. It doesn't necessarily mean the person currently driving.


~
科研
Short for 科学研究 (kēxué yánjiū), always refers to scientific research.  For more general research, use 研究 (yánjiū).


~
大使
Specifically an ambassador, the highest-ranking diplomatic representative of a country.  Don't confuse with other diplomatic titles.


~
公共
Means "public" in the sense of shared or accessible to all.  It highlights communal use or ownership.


~
配
Has multiple meanings related to matching, combining, or fitting.  Pay close attention to context to determine the correct interpretation.


~
山
Can refer to either a mountain or a hill.  座 (zuò) is the most common measure word.


~
大多数
Refers to a significant majority, usually well over half. It emphasizes the preponderance of a certain group or characteristic.


~
降温
Can refer to a decrease in temperature or a cooling down of a situation, such as declining enthusiasm or economic activity.


~
取款
Specifically means withdrawing money.  For depositing money, use 存钱 (cún qián).


~
收取
Implies collecting or receiving something, often with an element of formality or official process.  It's not just casually taking something.


~
干什么
Can be a question ("what are you doing?") or part of a rhetorical question implying disapproval or disbelief ("what do you think you're doing?").


~
水分
Can literally mean moisture content, but also figuratively refers to exaggeration or inflated figures. It suggests something is not as substantial as it appears.


~
电视台
Specifically a television station, not a TV channel or program.


~
再也
Used with negative verbs to indicate something will no longer happen. It emphasizes the finality of the action.


~
战斗
Implies active fighting or struggle, often involving conflict or confrontation. It's more intense than just competition or disagreement.


~
养老
Encompasses both providing for the elderly and enjoying retirement.  Context will determine the specific meaning.


~
强度
Refers to the degree or level of something, often related to strength, intensity, or concentration. It's a measure of how powerful or potent something is.


~
恩人
Specifically refers to someone who has done a significant favor or kindness that warrants deep gratitude.  It's a stronger term than just a helpful person.


~
图
Can refer to a visual representation (picture, chart, diagram) or a plan or scheme.  The context determines the meaning.


~
渐渐
Indicates a gradual change or process over time. It emphasizes the slow and steady nature of the transition.


~
零｜〇
Both represent zero, but 零 is generally used for numbers while 〇 is for dates or filling in forms.


~
晚饭
Refers to the evening meal. The measure words 顿 (dùn) and 餐 (cān) emphasize the occasion of eating, while 份 (fèn) indicates a portion or serving, and 次 (cì) indicates the instance or occurrence of the meal.


~
狂
Implies an extreme degree of something, often with a negative connotation of wildness, recklessness, or madness.


~
钱包
Specifically a wallet or purse used for carrying money and cards.


~
小于
A mathematical term meaning "less than."


~
宽度
Specifically refers to the width of something.  For length, use 长度 (chángdù).

~
对抗
For "combat," a more common word is simply 打仗 (dǎzhàng). 对抗 has more of a sense of *mutual* antagonism; it's not just one side attacking the other. It emphasizes the oppositional nature of the conflict.  For example, it's often used in the context of political or ideological struggles. It can also be used for things like sports matches.

~
发放
This word is more formal than 给 (gěi). It implies a structured, organized process of distribution, often by an institution or authority. Think of contexts like issuing permits, distributing relief aid, or paying out salaries.

~
孤儿
While 孤儿 technically refers to a child without any parents, it is often used more broadly to refer to children without one or both parents, especially those who are alone and lack care.


~
肿
Besides the literal swelling of a body part, 肿 can also figuratively describe something as "inflated" or "exaggerated", like a price or a story. For example, 你说的太肿了 (nǐ shuō de tài zhǒng le) means "you're exaggerating."


~
看来
This is often used at the beginning of a sentence, similar to “it seems that” or “apparently” in English.  Note that it can be used mid-sentence to transition to a conclusion, like “so it seems.”


~
上市
In the context of companies, 上市 can refer to both an initial public offering (IPO) and being listed on a stock exchange after the IPO. So, a company can 上市 on the New York Stock Exchange.


~
有关
  While 有关 can generally mean "related," it carries a slightly more formal tone than other synonyms like  关于 (guānyú) or  和…有关 (hé…yǒuguān).  有关 often appears in official contexts, announcements, or news reports.


~
回报
回报 can mean "return" in a financial sense, but it also has the broader meaning of reciprocation or payback, even in non-financial situations.  It can refer to returning a favor, repaying kindness, or even retaliating against a wrong.  The specific meaning depends heavily on the context.


~
东方
Besides referring to the East geographically or culturally, 东方 can also be used as a surname.  Also, be aware of the idiom 东方不亮西方亮 (dōngfāng bù liàng xīfāng liàng), which means “when one door closes another opens”.


~
较
较 is usually used in comparisons. It implies a slight degree of difference.  It precedes adjectives or adverbs to create comparative expressions, like  较好 (jiào hǎo - relatively good) or  较早 (jiào zǎo - relatively early).


~
身上
身上 literally means "on the body," but it can also figuratively refer to qualities or characteristics a person possesses, or even items they are carrying. For instance,  他身上有很多优点 (tā shēnshang yǒu hěn duō yōudiǎn) translates to "He has many good qualities."


~
不止
不止 can mean "more than" in quantity or "incessantly" in terms of action.  The context clarifies the intended meaning. Note that it has a different meaning from 不只 (bùzhǐ), which means "not only."


~
围栏
围栏 refers to a structure specifically designed to enclose an area, such as a fence, railing, or barrier.  It implies a clear boundary.


~
新年
新年 can refer to any new year, not just the Lunar New Year. To specify the Lunar New Year, you would usually say 春节 (chūnjié) or 农历新年 (nónglì xīnnián).


~
延期
延期 implies a formal postponement to a later date.  It is often used in official contexts like project deadlines, meetings, or legal proceedings.


~
部队
部队 usually refers to military units of a considerable size, rather than individual soldiers.  It's commonly used in news and military contexts.


~
试点
试点 implies a small-scale, experimental implementation of a project or policy before widespread adoption.  It carries a sense of testing and evaluation.


~
不料
不料 highlights the unexpected nature of an event and often introduces a surprising or contrasting outcome. It's often used at the beginning of a sentence or clause.


~
即将
即将 indicates that something is about to happen very soon. It carries a sense of imminence.


~
初
初 often indicates the beginning stage of something or the first time something happens.  For instance, 初学者 (chūxuézhě) means "beginner," and  月初 (yuèchū) means "beginning of the month."


~
基金
基金 refers to a pooled investment fund, not just any kind of fund.  It usually refers to mutual funds, hedge funds, or other professionally managed investment vehicles.


~
果酱
果酱 is a general term for fruit preserves. It can refer to jam, jelly, marmalade, or other similar spreads.


~
交代
交代 has a range of meanings beyond simply "handing over."  It can also imply explaining oneself, giving an account of one's actions, confessing, or even facing the consequences of one's deeds.


~
姐妹
姐妹 can refer to both blood-related sisters and close female friends. The context usually makes the meaning clear.  It can also refer to a sister city or sister school.


~
听见
听见 emphasizes the auditory perception of a sound, whereas 听到 (tīngdào) implies successful comprehension of the sound's meaning. For instance, you might 听见 a noise but not 听到 what someone said.


~
便于
便于 implies that something is convenient for a specific purpose or action. It suggests ease of use or facilitation.


~
保养
保养 includes regular maintenance and care to preserve something's condition or prolong its lifespan. It can refer to maintaining equipment, vehicles, or even one's health.


~
伤亡
伤亡 refers to both injuries and deaths, typically used in contexts of accidents, disasters, or conflicts.


~
危机
危机 refers to a serious situation that poses a significant threat or danger. It implies a sense of urgency and potential negative consequences.


~
味儿
味儿, with the "er" sound, often carries a more nuanced or subjective sense of taste or flavor. It can also refer to the general atmosphere or feeling of a place or situation.


~
之中
之中 indicates being within a specific range, time period, or group. It emphasizes inclusion or being surrounded by something.


~
绝望
绝望 describes a complete loss of hope and a sense of utter hopelessness. It implies a deep emotional state of despair.


~
发起
发起 suggests initiating or spearheading a project, activity, or movement. It implies taking the lead and setting something in motion.


~
武器
武器 refers to any instrument or tool used for fighting or attacking, ranging from simple tools to advanced weaponry.


~
中学生
中学生 typically refers to students in junior and senior high school, covering grades 7-12.  The context might make it clear whether it refers specifically to junior high or senior high school students.


~
中医
中医 specifically refers to traditional Chinese medicine, encompassing various practices like acupuncture, herbal medicine, and massage.


~
南极
南极 refers to the geographical South Pole, while  南极洲 (nánjízhōu) refers to the continent of Antarctica.


~
签约
签约 emphasizes the formal act of signing a contract or agreement, indicating a legally binding commitment.


~
书法
书法 refers to the art of Chinese calligraphy, which emphasizes aesthetics and expressive brushstrokes, not just handwriting in general.


~
钢笔
钢笔 specifically refers to a fountain pen, distinguishing it from other types of pens like ballpoint pens or gel pens.

~
新型
新型冠状病毒 (xīnxíng guānzhuàng bìngdú), or "novel coronavirus," is a very common collocation.

~
令
令 is a formal way to say "make" or "cause." A more common way to say this is 让 (ràng).

~
胖子
This word can be offensive if used to refer to someone directly.

~
混
混 is often used with the word 进去 (jìnqù), as in:

混进去 (hùn jìnqù)

This means to "sneak in."

~
分工
The difference between 分工 (fēngōng) and 分开工作 (fēnkāi gōngzuò) is that 分工 implies a systematic or organized division of labor, whereas 分开工作 simply means to work separately. 分工 emphasizes the coordinated distribution of tasks to achieve a common goal, while 分开工作 may just indicate people working independently on different things.

~
分裂
分裂 can be used figuratively, such as in referring to a political party or other organization that is disintegrating due to internal strife.

~
声门音
The 声门音, also known as the glottal stop, is a sound produced by the momentary closure of the vocal cords. It is not a distinct phoneme in Mandarin Chinese.

~
混乱
混乱 can be used both to describe the state of a place and to describe the state of one's mind.

~
考察
考察 emphasizes fieldwork, practical application, and direct experience. It often implies a systematic and investigative approach. In contrast, 调查 (diàochá) generally focuses on collecting information and conducting research, often through methods like surveys, interviews, or document analysis. 调查 may not necessarily involve direct on-site observation.

~
忍
The character 忍 (rěn) is made up of two radicals: 心 (xīn, heart) and 刃 (rèn, blade). This hints at its meaning – to endure pain or hardship as if a blade were piercing the heart.

~
见过
The "过" (guo) particle implies having had the experience at some point in the past, and retaining the knowledge or memory of that experience. It implies familiarity or knowledge gained through previous contact.

~
进展
进展 is often used in formal settings or written reports, such as project updates or business presentations. It indicates quantifiable or demonstrable steps forward. A similar word, especially in spoken Chinese, is "进步" (jìnbù), meaning "progress" or "advancement."

~
进一步
This word is similar to 更进一步 (gèng jìnyībù). But "更" is just slightly stronger.

~
早就
This word often conveys a sense of "I already knew that" or "it has been this way for a while."

~
热线
This is just like hotline in English.

~
恰当
There are many ways to say "appropriate." 恰当 (qiàdàng) is used specifically to describe something that is fitting, proper, or suitable for a particular situation. It is a formal word often used in writing. 合适 (héshì) is more general and commonly used in everyday speech.

~
以下
以下 includes the boundary it mentions, while 如下 (rúxià, "as follows") does not.

~
嘛
In some contexts, the particle 嘛 (ma) can imply impatience or a slight sense of annoyance, especially if the speaker believes the information is obvious or self-evident.

~
远远
远远 can be used to describe abstract differences, such as prices or expectations. For example, 远远不够 (yuǎnyuǎn bùgòu) means "far from enough."

~
明亮
明亮 (míngliàng) implies a clear, bright light that is also gentle and pleasing to the eye, as opposed to simply being intensely bright. It suggests a comfortable and welcoming illumination.

~
宽广
The word 宽广 describes two dimensions: 宽 (kuān), width, and 广 (guǎng), breadth or vastness. It describes something that is spacious in both directions.

~
夫人
夫人 is generally used for the wife of an important person, such as a high-ranking official or someone of high social standing.  太太 (tàitai) is the more general and common term for a married woman.

~
附件
This word can mean appendix, enclosure, or attachment, depending on context.

~
天上
天上 can also mean heaven (as in "a heaven on earth") or the celestial realm.

~
不行
不行 (bùxíng) means "not okay," which could mean "I can't do that," "that won't work," or "that is impossible." 不要 (bùyào) simply means "do not" or "don't want."

~
改
改 can refer to any change in plans, decisions, or appointments.

~
应当
应当 (yīngdāng) suggests responsibility, propriety, or the way things should be done. 应该 (yīnggāi) is similar but can also carry the additional meaning of "probably" or "likely."

~
独自
This implies doing something without companionship or assistance, emphasizing solitude. It often conveys a sense of independence or self-reliance. 单独 (dāndú), which is close in meaning to 独自, describes being separate from others.

~
肉
This can be confusing for learners because 肉 can refer to "meat" (as in the food) or "flesh."

~
环节
环节 emphasizes its importance as a component of a larger system.

~
摄像
摄像 refers specifically to the act of capturing images with a video camera, including both the technical process and the artistic considerations involved.

~
星星
星星 (xīngxing) refers to stars that are far away in the sky. 星星 can also mean stars (figurative), as in movie stars or sports stars.

~
岸上
岸上 is the opposite of 水里 (shuǐ lǐ).

~
刷
Besides its common meanings related to cleaning or applying something with a brush, 刷 also has online slang meanings, such as "to swipe a card," "to gain presence online," or "to flood with comments."

~
防治
The term 防治 (fángzhì) is a commonly used pairing that emphasizes both proactive prevention and active treatment of an issue, particularly in healthcare.

~
爆
爆 is a versatile character used in many contexts, each carrying a nuance of suddenness or intensity.

~
度
度 is a multifaceted character that carries the core meaning of measurement, limit, or extent.

~
引导
引导 implies not only showing the way but also providing instruction or explanation, often with the goal of influencing someone's understanding or behavior.

~
大批
大批 (dàpī) suggests a substantial quantity of a specific group or category of things, often implying an influx, a sudden increase, or a significant presence.

~
住院
住院 (zhùyuàn) implies staying in a hospital for an extended period to receive ongoing medical treatment, including regular checkups, medications, therapies, and possible surgical procedures. It suggests a degree of medical oversight and care requiring admission to the facility.  On the other hand, simply going to the hospital for a checkup or a quick treatment is more accurately expressed as 去医院 (qù yīyuàn).

~
二手
Although this can mean "second-hand", it also has the meaning of "indirectly acquired". For example, information from an unverified source can be described as 二手消息.

~
准
This character has many meanings, but it's usually straightforward to distinguish them based on context. However, one usage of 准 that might not be obvious is when it's used before a noun, as in 准新娘 or 准女婿. It means something like "soon-to-be" or "almost". It's also possible to use 准 as a verb, in which case it has meanings like "permit" or "allow".

~
病人
Be mindful of the subtle difference between 病人 (bìngrén) and 患者 (huànzhě). While both refer to someone with an illness, 病人 emphasizes the state of being sick, while 患者 focuses on the person receiving medical treatment. So, if you're talking to a doctor about a medical condition, 患者 might be more appropriate. If you're simply talking about someone who is unwell, 病人 is perfectly fine.

~
此处
This is a more formal or literary way to say “here”.  A more common way to say “here” is 这里 (zhèlǐ).  This is more appropriate in informal situations.  The equivalent of “there” is 那里 (nàlǐ).


~
嫌
This word has a wide range of negative connotations, from mild dislike to active suspicion or resentment.  When used before a verb, it indicates reluctance or avoidance due to dislike. The related words 嫌弃 (xiánqì) and 讨厌 (tǎoyàn) both mean "to dislike" but 讨厌 has a stronger, more active sense of dislike.


~
大声
In Chinese, saying something in a loud voice isn't necessarily negative. It can simply mean projecting one's voice so others can hear. If you want to indicate that someone is being loud in a disruptive or angry way, you'd use a word like  吵 (chǎo - noisy) or  大声嚷嚷 (dàshēng rāngrang - to yell).


~
常用
This is slightly more formal than 经常用 (jīngcháng yòng) - both mean "frequently used."


~
歌
Remember the measure words for 歌 (gē): 支 (zhī) for songs in general, and 首 (shǒu) for more poetic or formal contexts, such as when discussing lyrics or the artistic value of a song.


~
回避
This word suggests actively avoiding something or someone, often out of a sense of discomfort, conflict, or potential trouble. It's a more deliberate action than simply "avoiding" something.


~
山坡
This can refer to any sloping side of a mountain or hill, gentle or steep. If you specifically want to talk about a steeper slope, you might use words like 陡坡 (dǒupō) or 斜坡 (xiépō).


~
盛行
This describes something that is widespread and common, often in a temporary or trendy way, such as a fashion trend or a popular opinion.


~
抽奖
This refers specifically to the act of drawing lots or selecting winners in a lottery or raffle.


~
院
This character has several meanings, often related to enclosed spaces. It can mean a courtyard, a hospital, or even a specialized institution. Pay attention to context to determine the specific meaning.


~
湖
The measure word 片 (piàn) is typically used for a broad expanse of a lake, emphasizing its surface area, whereas 个 (gè) is a more general measure word.


~
男女
While this simply means "men and women," its usage can sometimes be more nuanced.  In some contexts, it can refer to the relationship or interaction between men and women, sometimes even implying romantic involvement.


~
中药
This refers to the specific system of traditional Chinese medicine using herbal remedies and other traditional practices.


~
胡同儿
This word specifically refers to the narrow alleyways or lanes typically found in older, traditional Chinese cities, especially Beijing.


~
挑选
This emphasizes a careful and selective process of choosing. If you just want to express general choosing, you'd use 选 (xuǎn).


~
创建
This describes the process of creating something new and significant, like an organization or a system, often involving some effort and planning.


~
取款机
This term specifically refers to an ATM machine.


~
界
This refers to a boundary, but can also mean a field or realm of expertise or activity.


~
蓝天
A more descriptive or poetic way to express "blue sky" might be 蔚蓝的天空 (wèilán de tiānkōng).


~
守
When used before a noun like "law" or "rules," it emphasizes adherence to and compliance with regulations.


~
倒车
This can also mean to change vehicles, like buses or trains, in addition to reversing a car.


~
约定
This suggests a more formal or binding agreement than a casual promise.


~
正念
This has a specific meaning in Buddhism, referring to a state of mindful awareness.


~
跨
This word emphasizes the action of stepping or striding over something.


~
故障
This is a more technical term for a malfunction or breakdown, often used for machines or systems.


~
通知书
This is specifically a written notice, more formal than just a verbal notification.


~
内衣
Be mindful of cultural sensitivities when discussing underwear.  It's generally not a topic for casual conversation.


~
看好
This expresses optimism or positive expectations about something's future prospects.


~
琴
This is a general term for stringed instruments, and can refer to several different kinds.


~
场地
This refers to a dedicated space for a particular activity, such as a sports field or a building site.


~
讲课
This is specifically the act of teaching or lecturing in a formal setting.


~
哪些
This asks for a selection from a specific group of things or people.


~
协商
This implies a process of discussion and negotiation to reach a mutually acceptable agreement.


~
惊喜
This implies a pleasant and unexpected surprise.


~
纸
Remember the measure words: 张 (zhāng) for sheets of paper, and 沓 (dá) for stacks or reams of paper.


~
标题
This can also refer to headlines in news articles or captions for images.


~
驻
This often refers to the official stationing of personnel, like troops or diplomats, in a specific location.

~
尝试
The most common structure is 尝试 + verb, or 尝试 + noun. You can also use 尝试着 + verb, but this has a slightly different meaning.  尝试 + verb means "to attempt to do something". 尝试着 + verb means "to tentatively try doing something".

~
合
This character has many meanings, but learners of Chinese probably only need to know two:

1. To close, shut, combine, join
This meaning is usually used with the character 上 (合上) or 并 (合并)

2. Suitable, fitting, appropriate (合适 héshì)

~
果树
The measure word for 果树 is 棵 (kē).  This measure word is usually used for plants which have a trunk, such as trees.

~
献
This word is quite formal and not used very often.  A similar word is 提供 tígōng, which is much more common.

~
助理
Can be used as a noun (assistant) or a verb (to assist).

~
实力
This word is very similar to 力量 lìliàng, but there is a subtle difference.  实力 refers to the inherent power or capability that one possesses.  It focuses on the potential to do things.  On the other hand, 力量 can refer to strength that might be external.

~
规范
规范 is both a noun and a verb.  As a noun, 规范 is usually seen in formal settings and means "regulation" or "standard".  As a verb, 规范 means "to regulate" or "to standardize."


~
服
This word has many meanings.  The most common ones are:

1.  Clothing
2.  To take medicine
3.  To admire (佩服 pèifu)
4.  To serve (time in prison, in the military)


~
外头 (outside)
This word is very similar to 外面 (wàimiàn), but slightly more colloquial.


~
超
超 is usually seen in the structure 超过 (chāoguò) which means "to surpass" or "to exceed".


~
手法
手法 is usually used in a negative context. For example, if you're describing a magician's 手法, you would probably use 技巧 (jìqiǎo) instead.

~
不必
不必 is very formal.  A more common and colloquial synonym is 不用 (bùyòng).

~
体育场
体育场 is a more formal and official way to say stadium, compared to 运动场 (yùndòngchǎng).

~
厂
厂 is no longer commonly used by itself, but is seen in the word 工厂 (gōngchǎng - factory)


~
扁
This character is not used very frequently.  It does appear in the word 扁桃体 (biǎntáotǐ - tonsils), though.

~
球鞋
More commonly used in Taiwan. In mainland China, people generally say 运动鞋 (yùndòngxié).


~
看得起
The opposite of 看不起 (kànbuqǐ).  The literal meaning is "to be able to see/look up to someone", meaning to respect or think highly of someone.  The literal meaning of 看不起  is "to be unable to see/look up to someone", meaning to look down upon or disrespect someone.

~
不对
不对劲儿 (bùduìjìnr) means "something's not right".

~
沿
沿 is more often used to mean "along" in the sense of direction, while 顺着 (shùnzhe) might be more focused on the action of following something.  This is a subtle distinction.

~
没收
没收 is generally used by government or organizations with authority, rather than individuals.


~
防
防 is usually used together with other characters, such as 预防 (yùfáng) or 防止 (fángzhǐ).

~
降
The meaning of "to surrender" comes from the idea of someone lowering their position and submitting to another.

~
光线
光线 refers to natural light. If you wish to talk about electric light, you can use 灯光 (dēngguāng).


~
子弹
A common measure word for 子弹 is 发 (fā), which is the same measure word for gunshots.

~
透露
透露 means to "reveal" or "disclose," but it suggests partial and subtle revelation, often of secrets or confidential information.  泄露 (xièlòu) means to leak, divulge or reveal something that was not supposed to be made public.  It often has a negative connotation.

~
好玩儿
好玩儿 can be used to describe something as interesting or fun.  For people, it usually refers to children, and the meaning is closer to "playful".


~
获
获 is usually used in formal writing, and usually seen together with another character, e.g. 获得 (huòdé - to obtain, gain)

~
路线
路线 usually refers to an ideological path, as in a political line or strategic course of action. 路 (lù) is the general word for path or road.

~
肺
The measure word for 肺 is 个 (gè). The measure words for internal organs are usually 个, even though they don't look like a typical 个.

~
赞赏
赞赏 is more formal than other words like 称赞 (chēngzàn - praise)

~
多久
The character 多 (duō) usually means "many" or "much".  But when it is placed before another character describing quantity, such as 久 (jiǔ - long time), 少 (shǎo - small amount), or 大 (dà - large/big), it means "how + adj".  E.g. 多大 (duōdà - how big).

~
联合国
联合国 (Liánhéguó) is the abbreviation for the full name 联合国组织 (Liánhéguó zǔzhī).


~
铃声
铃声 now most commonly refers to the ringtone of a phone.

~
舞蹈
舞蹈 can refer to the dance itself, or the act of dancing.

~
收音机
This word is somewhat dated.  A more modern way to say "radio" is 广播 (guǎngbō).

~
出行
出行 refers to going out for a specific purpose, such as a business trip or a sightseeing excursion. It carries a sense of formality and planning.  On the other hand, 出门 (chūmén) is a much more general word and simply means to go out.

~
年初
年初 refers to the first few months of the year. 年头 (niántóu) on the other hand, can refer to either the beginning of the year or a time long ago.  年尾 (niánwěi) means "end of the year".

~
考核
考核 is more formal than 评估 (pínggū), and emphasizes the measurement of performance against established standards.

~
评论
评论 can refer to the act of reviewing or commenting, or the comment itself.

~
顽皮
顽皮 is more often used to describe children, while 调皮 (tiáopí) can be used for both adults and children.

~
分类
The meanings "to classify" and "classification" are both represented by this word.  When it means "to classify", it can be followed by the 把 (bǎ) construction.

~
势力
This word usually has a negative connotation, unlike 影响力 (yǐngxiǎnglì, "influence"), which is neutral.

~
转换
Can be followed by the 把 (bǎ) construction.

~
场景
This word is more often used to refer to a particular setting in a play, movie, or novel, rather than a real-life situation. For real-life situations, the word 情景 (qíngjǐng) might be more appropriate.

~
养
This word can have a slightly different meaning depending on the object.  养宠物 (yǎng chǒngwù) means "to keep a pet,"  养孩子 (yǎng háizi) means "to raise a child," 养花 (yǎng huā) means to grow flowers.

~
短处
Can be considered a synonym of 缺点 (quēdiǎn), although 缺点 describes a more serious or inherent flaw.

~
传来
This word often implies that the sound or news is coming from a distance or another room.

~
罢了
This word often carries a sense of resignation or helplessness.  It downplays the importance of what precedes it.  For example, "我只不过是个普通人罢了" (wǒ zhǐ buguò shì ge pǔtōng rén bàle) means "I'm just an ordinary person, that's all."

~
常常
This word suggests a habit or frequent occurrence, more so than 经常 (jīngcháng).

~
议题
This word implies a more formal topic of discussion, such as in a meeting or conference.  For casual conversations, 话题 (huàtí) is more common.

~
区分
Can be followed by the 把 (bǎ) construction.

~
归
The meaning "to return" can also take the form 归来 (guīlái).

~
向前
向前 (xiàng qián) emphasizes the direction of movement, while 向前走 (xiàng qián zǒu) emphasizes the action of moving forward.

~
机器人
This word encompasses both "robot" and "android."

~
参议员
This refers specifically to a member of the Senate. A more general term for a politician is 政治家 (zhèngzhìjiā).

~
泉
While 泉 can refer to a "spring" as the source of a stream, it can also mean "fountain," especially an ornamental one.

~
选拔
This emphasizes the careful selection from a group, often through competition or testing.  A more general term for selection is 选择 (xuǎnzé).

~
笑话儿
This word emphasizes the humorous aspect, while 笑话 (xiàohuà, without the 儿) is more neutral and can also mean "joke" or "jest."

~
人工
人工 can refer to either manual labor or something man-made, as opposed to natural.

~
光荣
This word is often used in a patriotic or formal context.  For a more general sense of "glory," 荣耀 (róngyào) can be used.

~
反问
This specifically refers to asking a question to make a point, not simply asking a question in reply.

~
难听
This can refer to both unpleasant sounds and offensive language.

~
商城
商城 is more accurately translated as "online mall" or "e-commerce platform."  For a physical shopping mall,  购物中心 (gòuwù zhōngxīn) is more appropriate.

~
领
Be careful of the tones.  领 (lǐng) means "to lead" or "to receive," while 岭 (lǐng) means "mountain ridge."

~
赠
This word has a more formal and respectful connotation than 送 (sòng, "to give").

~
古老
This implies a greater age and historical significance than simply 老 (lǎo, "old").

~
需求
This refers to a more formal or essential requirement, while 需要 (xūyào) is more general.

~
大力
大力 often collocates with verbs like 支持 (zhīchí, "to support") or 推广 (tuīguǎng, "to promote").

~
和谐
In recent years, this word has also taken on the meaning of "censored" or "harmonized" due to its use in official contexts.

~
前后
This can also mean "approximately" when used with a quantity.

~
两侧
This specifically refers to the two sides of something, while both sides in a debate or conflict is 双方 (shuāngfāng).

~
创作
This implies artistic or intellectual creation, while 制造 (zhìzào) refers to the production of physical objects.

~
军舰
This word specifically refers to military vessels, while 船 (chuán) is a more general term for boats and ships.

~
住宅
This refers specifically to a house or apartment for living in, while 房子 (fángzi) is a broader term that can include any building.

~
脑子
This word can also refer to one's mind or way of thinking, not just the physical organ.

~
上面
Can also be shortened to 上 (shàng).

~
无疑
This is stronger than 可能 (kěnéng, "maybe") and indicates a near certainty.

~
降价
This is an intransitive verb, meaning the price itself drops.  To lower a price actively, use 降低价格 (jiàngdī jiàgé).

~
炒股
This term often has a negative connotation, suggesting risky speculation rather than long-term investment.

~
北
Besides "north", this word can also mean to be defeated (from ancient battles facing north) - now archaic.

~
笔
When talking about how many pens you have, the measure word is 支 (zhī).  枝 (zhī) is only used for flowers or plants.

~
前年
前年 can also refer to any year before last year, not just *the* year before last year. So if it is 2024 now, 前年 could refer to 2022, but it could also refer to 2019 or 1945.  If you want to specifically refer to the year *right* before last year, you should use 大前年 (dàqiánnián).

~
访问
访问 (fǎngwèn) can also mean "to interview," as in interviewing somebody for a job or for news.

~
亲眼
亲眼 is often used together with 看到 (kàndào), so you get the phrase 亲眼看到 meaning to "see with one's own eyes".  It is not usually used alone.

~
达成
达成 (dáchéng) usually refers to reaching some kind of agreement or consensus, such as a business deal or a political agreement. It can also be used for the sense of fulfilling or achieving something, such as a goal or target.

~
传递
传递 (chuándì) carries a connotation of relaying or handing off of information or items.

~
赶不上
赶不上 (gǎnbushàng) emphasizes the inability to catch up in terms of speed, progress, or schedule. It suggests falling behind or failing to keep pace.

~
家属
家属 (jiāshǔ) generally refers to immediate family members, such as spouses, parents, children, and siblings.  It's more formal than saying just 家庭.

~
送给
送给 (sònggěi) is similar to 给 (gěi), but it specifically implies giving as a gift or present.  This is unlike 给, which is just a generic word for giving.

~
串
串 (chuàn) can be used as a verb meaning "to string together," as in stringing beads onto a necklace, or "to skewer," as in putting meat or vegetables onto a skewer for grilling. It can also be used as a noun meaning "string," "bunch," or "skewer," or as a classifier for things that are strung together, in a bunch, or in a row.  A more colloquial and commonly used alternative is the measure word  "把" (bǎ).

~
海军
海军 (hǎijūn) is the term for "navy" in general. If you want to refer to the specific navy of a country, you would use the country's name as a modifier before 海军. For example, "美国海军" (měiguó hǎijūn) would be "the United States Navy".

~
午夜
午夜 (wǔyè) is a more formal and literary way of saying midnight.  A more colloquial way is 半夜 (bànyè).

~
牵
牵 (qiān) can also mean "to involve" or "to be related to". This usage often appears in more formal contexts.

~
机械
机械 (jīxiè) can also have a negative connotation of being inflexible, rigid, or lacking creativity.

~
主导
主导 (zhǔdǎo) implies a stronger sense of control and influence compared to other leadership words. It suggests taking the initiative and directing others.

~
研发
研发 (yánfā) is commonly used in the context of scientific and technological development. It can refer to both basic research and the development of practical applications.

~
记载
记载 (jìzǎi) is a formal way of saying "to record."  A more colloquial way would be just to say "写" (xiě), which means "to write."

~
长远
长远 (chángyuǎn) usually refers to long-term plans or goals, rather than just a long distance or time.

~
夹
夾 (jiā) is used as a verb, meaning to "put between."  It can also be a noun, referring to the things that do the putting between (e.g. chopsticks).  夹子 (jiāzi) refers to a tool which is designed specifically for the purpose of holding something between two parts (e.g. a clip or tweezers).

~
中断
中断 (zhōngduàn) suggests a complete cessation or disruption, often due to unforeseen circumstances.

~
有的
Note the difference between "有的" and "一些". While both can mean "some", 有的 is used to categorize. Some are like this, and some are like that.  一些 (yīxiē) means some, and is a quantity word similar to "几个" or "一些".

~
检测
检测 (jiǎncè) is a more technical term than 测试 (cèshì), and often involves specific procedures or instruments. It suggests a thorough examination to assess quality or identify problems.

~
景
In more literary contexts, 景 (jǐng) can also refer to sunlight or an object of admiration or reverence.

~
群众
群众 (qúnzhòng) refers to the general public or the common people.  It's a term that's associated with the PRC and it sometimes has a meaning that is more specific than just the general public, but often in spoken Chinese, its more or less interchangeable with 大家 or 老百姓.

~
外资
外资 (wàizī) refers specifically to foreign capital or investment.  It's different from 外国人 (wàiguórén), which refers to foreign people.

~
爆发
爆发 (bàofā) is often used for sudden and violent events like wars or epidemics.

~
先前
先前 (xiānqián) can also mean "previously" or "beforehand," but it emphasizes the order of events rather than a specific time frame.

~
试题
试题 (shìtí) refers to questions on a test or exam, while 题目 (tímù) can be any topic of discussion or question in any situation.

~
环保
