环保 (huánbǎo) is often used as an adjective to describe things that are environmentally friendly, such as "环保产品" (huánbǎo chǎnpǐn) for "environmentally friendly products."

~
向导
向导 (xiàngdǎo) refers to a person who guides others, often in an unfamiliar area. It can also be used metaphorically for something that provides guidance or direction.

~
鲜明
鲜明 (xiānmíng) is often used to describe colors, images, or ideas that are vivid, clear, and easily understood.

~
现场
现场 (xiànchǎng) always refers to a location where something happens, is happening, or just happened.  It can mean something like "on the spot."

~
电源
电源 (diànyuán) is more technical or general than 插座 (chāzuò, wall outlet/socket).  If you want to say wall outlet/socket, use 插座 instead.

~
编制
编制 (biānzhì) also refers to the authorized strength or staffing level of an organization or department. It can also mean "to weave" or "to plait," as in making a basket or braid.

~
千克
千克 (qiānkè) is the more formal term for kilogram. In everyday conversation, 公斤 (gōngjīn) is more common.

~
出售
出售 (chūshòu) is more formal than 卖 (mài) and often implies selling something of higher value or in a more official context.

~
初步
初步 (chūbù) describes the very initial or rudimentary stage, whereas 初期 (chūqí) refers to the initial period of something.

~
严
严 (yán) can also refer to one's father in a formal or respectful way.

~
点燃
点燃 (diǎnrán) emphasizes the action of starting a fire, while 烧 (shāo) focuses on the state of something already burning.

~
周期
周期 (zhōuqī) refers to a recurring period of time or a complete cycle, often used in scientific or technical contexts.

~
泼
The word 泼 (pō) can mean "to splash" or "to spill," but it often carries a negative connotation, suggesting a careless or reckless action. For example, 泼水 (pō shuǐ) can mean "to splash water," but it can also imply "to spill water carelessly."  泼 can also be used to describe someone as "rough and coarse" or "brutish," often referring to their behavior or mannerisms.

~
贴
贴 (tiē) has a wide range of meanings. In addition to its literal meanings of "stick," "paste," and "glue," it can also mean "to nestle up to" or "to keep close to."  It can also mean "to subsidize" or refer to an "allowance." Note the special usage 贴心 (tiēxīn) - "attentive, considerate".

~
磨
磨 (mó) can mean "to rub," "to grind," "to polish," or "to sharpen." It can also mean "to wear down," "to die out," or even "to dawdle" or "to waste time." Additionally, it can be used figuratively to mean "to pester" or "to insist," as in 磨人 (mó rén) - "to pester someone."

~
墓
While 墓 (mù) generally translates to "tomb," "grave," or "mausoleum," it's more commonly used to refer to larger, more elaborate tombs or mausoleums rather than simple graves.

~
说明书
While 说明书 (shuōmíngshū) generally refers to a manual or instruction booklet, it can also be used more broadly to refer to any explanatory document, such as a synopsis of a play or film or even a patent specification.

~
确保
确保 (quèbǎo) emphasizes taking necessary measures to guarantee something will happen, while 保证 (bǎozhèng) is more of a promise or assurance.

~
尺寸
尺寸 (chǐcùn) can refer to both physical dimensions and figurative "propriety" or appropriate behavior. This figurative meaning is less common and somewhat colloquial.

~
障碍
障碍 (zhàng'ài) refers to a more significant obstacle that impedes progress or achievement, while 阻碍 (zǔ'ài) refers to a more general hindrance or obstruction.

~
姓名
姓名 (xìngmíng) specifically refers to a person's full name, including both surname and given name.

~
中部
中部 (zhōngbù) is a more formal term than 中间 (zhōngjiān) and is typically used for geographical regions or larger entities.

~
老是
老是 (lǎoshì) emphasizes a habitual or persistent action, often with a negative connotation.

~
纯净水
纯净水 (chúnjìngshuǐ) specifically refers to purified water, often bottled, not just any clean water.

~
坚定
坚定 (jiāndìng) suggests unwavering resolve and firmness, often in the face of challenges.

~
之类
之类 (zhīlèi) is often used after a noun or noun phrase, whereas 等等 (děngděng) is typically used at the end of a list.

~
转移
转移 (zhuǎnyí) can have both physical and abstract meanings, such as transferring objects or shifting attention or topics.

~
回到
回到 (huídào) emphasizes the process of returning to a place or state, while 回 (huí) simply means "to return."

~
协调
协调 (xiétiáo) emphasizes the smooth and harmonious interaction of different elements, while 合作 (hézuò) refers to collaboration or cooperation.

~
大师
大师 (dàshī) is a term of high respect, reserved for individuals with exceptional skill and mastery in a particular field.

~
乱象 (luànxiàng)
乱象 is more specifically "chaotic circumstances", and describes the overall situation, while 乱 (luàn) can mean generally chaotic or disorderly.

~
鼠
鼠 (shǔ) can refer to both mice and rats, but it is more commonly used for rats.

~
挤
挤 (jǐ) can mean both "to squeeze" physically and "to find time" in a busy schedule.

~
学费
学费 (xuéfèi) is specifically tuition or school fees, not other educational expenses.

~
忘
忘 (wàng) is a more common and general term for "to forget," while 忘记 (wàngjì) is more emphatic or formal.

~
有着
有着 (yǒuzhe) emphasizes the continuous possession or existence of something.

~
兔
兔 (tù) refers to both rabbits and hares.

~
发出
发出 (fāchū) implies emitting or sending something out, often sound, light, or a signal.

~
齿龈音
齿龈音 (chǐyínshēng) is a technical term in linguistics, specifically referring to alveolar sounds.

~
解放
解放 (jiěfàng) can refer to both literal and figurative liberation, including political and social liberation.

~
功课
功课 (gōngkè) refers to schoolwork in general, encompassing homework, classwork, and assignments.

~
不敢当
不敢当 (bùgǎndāng) is a humble expression used to downplay praise or compliments.

~
快递
快递 (kuàidì) refers specifically to express delivery services.

~
难题
难题 (nántí) emphasizes the difficulty or complexity of a problem, while 问题 (wèntí) is a more general term.

~
坚固
坚固 (jiāngù) emphasizes physical strength and stability, while 牢固 (láogù) emphasizes firmness and security.

~
珍珠
珍珠 (zhēnzhū) specifically refers to pearls, not other gemstones.

~
原先
原先 (yuánxiān) emphasizes the original or initial state or condition.

~
正当
正当 (zhèngdàng) can mean both "proper" or "timely" and "honest" or "reasonable."

~
选修
选修 (xuǎnxiū) refers specifically to elective courses, not mandatory ones.

~
忠心
忠心 (zhōngxīn) emphasizes loyalty and devotion, often to a cause or person.

~
升高
升高 (shēnggāo) can refer to both physical elevation and figurative increase, such as in temperature or price.

~
被告
被告 (bèigào) specifically refers to the defendant in a legal case.

~
喜爱
Although 喜爱 (xǐ'ài) can be translated as both "like" and "love," it carries a stronger sense of fondness or affection than simply liking something. It's closer to "be fond of" or "cherish."  It's not typically used for romantic love.  For romantic love, 爱 (ài) is more appropriate.

~
时装
时装 (shízhuāng) specifically refers to fashionable clothing, often high-end or designer wear. It's not used for everyday clothes.  For everyday clothes, you would say 衣服 (yīfu).

~
叫作
叫作 (jiàozuò) is more formal than other ways of saying "be called," such as 叫 (jiào) or 叫做 (jiàozuo). It's often used in official contexts or when introducing technical terms.

~
园林
园林 (yuánlín) refers to a classical Chinese garden, which emphasizes harmony with nature and artistic design. It's not just any park or garden.  For a generic garden, you could use 花园 (huāyuán) or 菜园 (càiyuán) depending on the context.  For park, you would use 公园 (gōngyuán).

~
更是
更是 (gèng shì) emphasizes a heightened degree or a more significant aspect of something already mentioned.  It's not simply "more," but "even more so." It's like saying "all the more" or "in particular."

~
家里
家里 (jiālǐ) specifically refers to one's own home. If you want to refer to someone else's home, you should use their surname or title plus 家 (e.g., 王家 - Wáng jiā, "the Wang family's home").

~
长寿
While 长寿 (chángshòu) primarily means "long life," it's also the name of a district in Chongqing. Be mindful of context to avoid confusion.

~
鬼
鬼 (guǐ) has a broader range of meanings than just "ghost." It can also refer to a mischievous spirit, a clever or sly person, or a person with a particular addiction (e.g., 酒鬼 - jiǔguǐ, "alcoholic").

~
家长
家长 (jiāzhǎng) can refer to both parents or specifically the head of the household, who traditionally holds authority. It's often used in the context of education, where it refers to the parents or guardians of a student.

~
透
透 (tòu) has many meanings beyond the basic "through." Pay attention to how it combines with other characters to form words like  透彻 (tòuchè) - thorough, or  透露 (tòulù) - to reveal.

~
出台
出台 (chūtái) has a specific usage related to policies or regulations being officially launched or announced. It's not just any kind of "publishing" or "appearing."

~
民歌
民歌 (míngē) specifically refers to traditional folk songs. It doesn't include other genres like pop songs.

~
深化
深化 (shēnhuà) emphasizes the intensification or further development of something existing, like a reform, relationship, or understanding.

~
河
河 (hé) refers to a river, often smaller than a 江 (jiāng).  江 usually refers to a large river, such as the Yangtze River (长江 - Cháng Jiāng).

~
熟人
熟人 (shúrén) is someone you know well, an acquaintance.  朋友 (péngyou) denotes a closer relationship, more like a "friend".

~
划船
划船 (huáchuán) is about propelling a boat using oars or paddles.  Other ways to travel by boat would use different words.

~
预期
预期 (yùqī) often implies a formal or calculated expectation, like a financial forecast.  期望 (qīwàng) is more about a personal hope or anticipation.

~
桥梁
桥梁 (qiáoliáng) can refer to a bridge in both a literal and figurative sense, meaning a connection or link between things.

~
野生
野生 (yěshēng) refers to plants or animals living in a natural, uncultivated state. It doesn't necessarily mean dangerous or aggressive.

~
老人
老人 (lǎorén) is a respectful term for elderly people.  It can also refer to one's own aged parents or grandparents.

~
来信
来信 (láixìn) specifically refers to an incoming letter, in contrast to 去信 (qùxìn) which is an outgoing letter.

~
番
番 (fān) has many meanings, including a classifier for events or actions, a way to describe multiples (like "double"), and an older term referring to foreigners (often derogatory).

~
全场
全场 (quánchǎng) can refer to all people present or the entire duration of an event, like a sports game.

~
提升
提升 (tíshēng) implies a raising to a higher level or position, both literally and figuratively (e.g., skills improvement).

~
推行
推行 (tuīxíng) implies putting something into practice or implementing a policy or system.

~
加上
加上 (jiāshàng) is more versatile than just "add" in mathematics.  It can mean "in addition," "moreover," or "furthermore," implying adding information or actions.

~
静
静 (jìng) describes stillness, quietness, or calmness, emphasizing the absence of movement or noise.

~
要素
要素 (yàosù) refers to essential factors or key elements that are crucial for something.

~
大哥
大哥 (dàgē) can be a respectful term for an older man or a term of address for a male friend. It's also been used to refer to gang leaders.

~
模样
模样 (múyàng) refers to appearance, style, or likeness. It can also mean "approximately" when combined with other words.

~
熊
熊 (xióng) is "bear," but colloquially, it can also mean to scold or criticize someone. It can also mean weak or incompetent in some dialects.

~
净
净 (jìng) implies complete cleanliness, emptiness, or purity. It can also refer to net income or exports.

~
按
按 (àn) has diverse meanings, including pressing, checking, restraining, and "according to."  Be aware of the specific context.

~
默契
默契 (mòqì) refers to a deep, unspoken understanding and coordination between people, often without explicit communication.

~
借鉴
借鉴 (jièjiàn) implies learning from others' experiences, often to avoid repeating mistakes or to improve upon existing methods.

~
理智
理智 (lǐzhì) emphasizes rationality and reason, often in contrast to emotions or impulses.

~
心愿
心愿 (xīnyuàn) represents a heartfelt wish or cherished desire, often long-held and deeply personal.

~
罚
罚 (fá) encompasses various forms of punishment, including fines, penalties, and other sanctions.

~
外出
外出 (wàichū) specifically refers to going out from a place where one normally stays, like one's home or workplace.

~
药品
药品 (yàopǐn) is a general term for medicinal drugs.  If you want to refer to traditional Chinese medicine, you can use 中药 (zhōngyào).

~
指定
指定 (zhǐdìng) carries a stronger sense of authority and formality than simply "choosing" or "selecting." It implies an official or explicit act of assigning or designating something specific.  Think of it like "officially appointing" or "specifically designating."

~
叉
When used to mean "diverge" or "to open (as legs)," the pronunciation changes to chǎ.  This is also the pronunciation for the onomatopoeia of something forking or splitting apart.

~
名誉
名誉 (míngyù) translates to both "fame" and "reputation," but it leans more towards the positive connotations of having a good name or prestige.  It's less about being widely known (famous) and more about being respected and esteemed.

~
真理
真理 (zhēnlǐ) isn't just any truth; it refers to a fundamental, universal, and objective truth, often with philosophical or ideological weight. Think "universal truth" or "fundamental principle."

~
司长
司长 (sīzhǎng) is a director of a department or bureau within a ministry of the Chinese government.  It's a fairly high-ranking position.

~
绘画
绘画 (huìhuà) encompasses both painting and drawing.  There isn't a clear distinction between the two as in English.

~
中级
中级 (zhōngjí) denotes a level higher than beginner but lower than advanced. It's "intermediate" in the sense of being in the middle stage of a progression, not necessarily "mid-level" in a hierarchy.

~
同样
While 同样 (tóngyàng) can mean "same," it is often used where English would use "also" or "too".

~
讨好
讨好 (tǎohǎo) has negative connotations of insincerity.  It suggests trying to win favor through flattery or excessive compliance, rather than genuine kindness.

~
出面
出面 (chūmiàn) emphasizes personally appearing or intervening in a situation, often to resolve a problem or represent someone.  Think "to step in" or "to show one's face."

~
缺
缺 (quē) as a verb carries the implication that the shortage is problematic or undesirable.

~
必需
必需 (bìxū) highlights something fundamental and crucial, implying that it's absolutely necessary or required.  Think of it as "essential" or "indispensable."

~
人力
人力 (rénlì) can also refer to human effort or exertion, not just the workforce or manpower.

~
听写
听写 (tīngxiě) specifically refers to the educational exercise of writing down words or sentences spoken aloud.  It is a common practice in language learning.

~
维生素
维生素 (wéishēngsù) is a direct transliteration of "vitamin."

~
女性
女性 (nǚxìng) can refer to women as a social group or the feminine gender in general, not just individual women.

~
比分
比分 (bǐfēn) is specifically used for scores in competitive events, especially sports.

~
必
必 (bì) conveys a strong sense of certainty or inevitability.  It is more emphatic than simply "must" or "will."

~
眼前
眼前 (yǎnqián) can also refer to the immediate future, like "in the near future" or "right around the corner."

~
大众
大众 (dàzhòng) refers to the general public or the ordinary people, often contrasted with elites or specialists.

~
不见
不见 (bújiàn) can also imply that something is missing or lost.

~
白色
In political contexts, 白色 (báisè) can refer to anything that is counter-revolutionary or reactionary.  It was originally used to describe White Terror.

~
合约
合约 (héyuē) emphasizes a mutually agreed-upon arrangement or deal, often implying a degree of formality.  It can also be a shorter form of 合同 (contract).

~
检验
检验 (jiǎnyàn) suggests a thorough and rigorous process of testing or examination, often scientific or technical.  It's more formal and comprehensive than a simple check.

~
羊
羊 (yáng) can encompass both sheep and goats.  Context usually clarifies which animal is being referred to.

~
百货
百货 (bǎihuò) specifically refers to a department store that sells a wide variety of goods.

~
外部
外部 (wàibù) can also refer to an external factor or influence.

~
钟
Note the two different pronunciations and meanings.  zhōng: clock, time. zhòng: bell, cup, goblet.

~
季
季 (jì) as a season refers to a three-month period on the traditional Chinese calendar, not necessarily corresponding exactly to the Western four seasons.

~
使得
使得 (shǐde) introduces a result or consequence. It sets up a cause-and-effect relationship.

~
酱
酱 (jiàng) refers to a thick, savory sauce, often made from fermented soybeans. It encompasses a broader range than just "soy sauce."

~
仰
仰 (yǎng) can also mean to admire or respect someone, literally "to look up to."

~
修车
修车 (xiūchē) can refer to repairing any vehicle, including bicycles and motorcycles, not just cars.

~
接连
接连 (jiēlián) emphasizes events happening consecutively without interruption, creating a sense of continuity or a chain reaction.

~
西南
西南 (xīnán) specifically refers to the southwest direction or region.

~
他们/这里
These are useful to know.

~
型号
型号 (xínghào) signifies a specific model or type within a product line, usually distinguished by features or specifications.

~
杂
杂 (zá) can also function as a verb meaning "to mix" or "to combine different elements."

~
关爱
关爱 (guān'ài) emphasizes care and concern that is active and demonstrated, not just felt internally. It implies looking out for someone's well-being.

~
补偿
Can be used as a noun or a verb.

~
字典
Note the measure word is 本 (běn).

~
拜访
This word is more formal than 看望 (kànwàng). It is usually used for visiting someone respectable, or someone you are not very familiar with.

~
民工
This word can have slightly negative connotations, as it can imply low-skill, low-wage labor, often involving difficult or dangerous working conditions.  More neutral terms include 外来务工人员 (wàilái wùgōng rényuán) - outside workers, and 农民工 (nóngmín gōng) - rural workers.

~
调
This character has many meanings and readings. The musical meanings are all pronounced diào. The other meanings are pronounced tiáo.

~
开创
This word is a bit formal (书面). More colloquial synonyms include 开始 (kāishǐ) and 创建 (chuàngjiàn).

~
母女
There is a similar word 父女 (fùnǚ), which means father and daughter.

~
精品
There is no difference in meaning or usage between 精品 and "boutique" or "quality goods" in English.

~
默默
A related word is 默默地 (mòmò de). 默默 is an adjective, while 默默地 is an adverb.

~
动画
Can also be used as an adjective, like in 动画电影 (animated movie) or 动画片 (cartoon).

~
干扰
The related word 干涉 (gānshè) also means “to interfere”.  However 干涉 implies intervening in other's affairs, or meddling, while 干扰 means to interrupt or obstruct.

~
望见
More formal than 看见 (kànjiàn).

~
齐
Another meaning of 齐 is "Qi", a state during the Spring and Autumn and Warring States periods (771-221 BC). It was located in modern-day Shandong province.

~
高原
The measure word is 片 (piàn).

~
迎来
Often used in official contexts, such as news reports or political speeches.

~
远处
In some situations, 远处 can be considered a noun. For example,  "Look into the distance" is "望向远处" (wàng xiàng yuǎnchù).

~
酒水
This is a more formal word. More colloquial words are 酒 (jiǔ) and 水 (shuǐ)

~
过时
This is often used for objects, things, or ideas/concepts. It's less commonly used to describe people, unlike outdated in English.

~
西部
Usually refers to Western China. If you want to say Western Europe, you say 西欧 (xī'ōu).

~
接收
Has a broader meaning than its English equivalent “receive.” It suggests formally taking possession or control of something.

~
跳水
As a verb, this is usually used to talk about diving into water for sport or recreation. But if the context makes it clear, it can also be used to describe jumping into water to commit suicide. As a noun, it usually refers to the sport of diving.

~
抢救
Implies a critical and urgent situation, requiring immediate action to save someone or something.

~
受
As a passive marker, 受 is generally used in formal or written Chinese. In spoken Chinese, 被 (bèi) is more commonly used.

~
相片
More common in Taiwan, whereas 照片 (zhàopiàn) is more common in mainland China.

~
报刊
Refers to printed news publications. If you want to say online news publications, use 网络报刊 (wǎngluò bàokān).

~
游
This character has multiple pronunciations, but the meanings given here are all pronounced yóu.

~
有的是
This phrase often carries a slightly dismissive tone. It implies an abundance so great that there’s no need to worry or be concerned about the availability of something.

~
工商
工商 can also refer to the specific government body responsible for regulating industry and commerce.  In China this is the State Administration for Market Regulation (国家市场监督管理总局).

~
防范
Implies taking precautions to prevent or mitigate potential threats or risks.

~
恰恰
Has a stronger emphasis than “just” or “exactly.” It often highlights a coincidence or an unexpected turn of events.

~
小学生
Measure word can be either 个 (gè) or 名 (míng).

~
跪
Usually used to describe kneeling down as a gesture of respect or apology.  Less commonly, it can also refer to kneeling as a form of punishment.

~
学会
When used in names of organizations, it means "Learned Society".  For example, 中国物理学会 (Chinese Physical Society).

~
强化
More formal than 加强 (jiāqiáng), but the meaning is essentially the same.

~
面子
A crucial concept in Chinese culture, so pay attention to its different meanings.

~
衡量
This verb often appears in formal writing and usually collocates with abstract nouns such as  价值 (jiàzhí - value),  利弊 (lìbì - advantages and disadvantages),  得失 (déshī - gains and losses).

~
也好
In the sense of "may as well", it implies a lack of better alternatives or a sense of resignation.  In the sense of "that's fine", it indicates agreement or acceptance, often with a slight sense of indifference.

~
平凡
More commonly used to describe people than in English.

~
打开
Besides the literal meaning of "opening" something physically, 打開 can also metaphorically refer to opening up one’s mind, thoughts or a new situation.

~
传
The meanings related to "spread" or "transmit" (传染 (chuánrǎn), 传播 (chuánbō)) are typically used for intangible things like news or diseases.  For physical objects, use other verbs like递 (dì), 交给 (jiāogěi), or 给 (gěi).

~
分散
When used with troops or personnel, 分散 emphasizes their scattering to multiple locations, implying a loss of concentrated force.  For general scattering of objects, use 散开 (sànkāi) instead.

~
资助
资助 specifically refers to financial assistance, often for education or charitable causes.  For general help or assistance, use 帮助 (bāngzhù).

~
公
公 has a wide range of meanings.  Pay attention to the context to determine the intended meaning.  It's especially important to differentiate between "public" (公共 gōnggòng), "fair" (公平 gōngpíng), and "male" (男性 nánxìng).

~
不曾
不曾 is more formal and literary than 从来没有 (cónglái méiyǒu) or 没 + Verb + 过 (méi + Verb + guò), which are more common in spoken Chinese.

~
电动
电动 refers specifically to things powered by electricity.  For things powered by an engine in general, use 机动 (jīdòng).

~
牙
牙 can also be a classifier for some objects resembling teeth, like cloves of garlic.

~
近期
近期 refers to the near future or recent past.  For the distant future or past, use 远期 (yuǎnqī) or long time ago respectively.

~
相等
相等 is used for numerical or measurable equality. For equality in status or rights, use 平等 (píngděng).

~
虫子
虫子 is a general term for small, crawling creatures. It doesn't include flying insects like flies or mosquitoes. For those, use 昆虫 (kūnchóng).

~
学
学 can also mean "to imitate," often used with a negative connotation. For example, 学坏 (xué huài) means "to learn bad habits."

~
治理
治理 emphasizes bringing order and control to a situation, often involving complex problems like pollution or social issues.  For simple management, use 管理 (guǎnlǐ).

~
表面上
表面上 highlights the deceptive nature of appearances, often implying a hidden reality.  For merely describing the surface appearance, use 外表 (wàibiǎo).

~
已
已 indicates completion of an action.  Don't confuse it with 以 (yǐ), which is a preposition.

~
通道
通道 can also refer to abstract channels like communication channels.

~
更加
更加 emphasizes a higher degree of something that already exists.  Don't use it if there's no basis for comparison.

~
女子
女子 is a more formal and respectful term for "woman" than 女人 (nǚrén), which can sometimes be considered slightly derogatory.

~
启动
启动 specifically refers to starting a machine or process.  For setting off on a journey, use 出发 (chūfā).

~
球星
球星 only refers to stars in ball sports like basketball, soccer, or baseball.  For stars in other sports, use 运动明星 (yùndòng míngxīng).

~
听说
听说 indicates information received from others, implying uncertainty.  If you know something for sure, don't use 听说.

~
外边
外边 refers to the outside of a place.  For abroad or overseas, use 国外 (guówài).

~
本期
本期 usually refers to a specific time period within a recurring cycle, such as a magazine issue or a financial quarter.

~
用品
用品 refers to items used for a specific purpose, like office supplies or toiletries. For general goods or products, use 商品 (shāngpǐn).

~
感到
感到 emphasizes subjective feelings or perceptions. For objective observations, use 觉得 (juéde).

~
填
填 implies filling a void or completing a blank, like filling a hole or filling out a form.  For adding more of something, use 加 (jiā).

~
优良
优良 describes something of high quality or excellence. It is more formal and literary than 好 (hǎo).

~
早晚
早晚 (sooner or later) implies inevitability.  For simply referring to morning and evening, clearly distinguish the context.

~
下雪
下雪 can be used as a noun ("snow") or a verb ("to snow").

~
吃力
吃力 emphasizes the difficulty and effort involved in a task.  For simply being tired, use 累 (lèi).

~
机关
机关 can also refer to government organizations or intricate plots and schemes.  Be aware of the context.

~
铁
铁 has a range of figurative meanings related to strength, firmness, and determination.

~
原理
原理 refers to the underlying principles or logic behind something.  For a general theory, use 理论 (lǐlùn).

~
儿科
儿科 specifically refers to the medical specialty of pediatrics.  For children's education or other matters, use 儿童 (értóng).

~
疼痛
疼痛 refers to physical pain. For emotional pain or suffering, use 痛苦 (tòngkǔ).

~
战友
战友 specifically refers to comrades who have fought together in a war.  For general colleagues or friends, use 同事 (tóngshì) or 朋友 (péngyou).

~
空中
空中 refers to the space above the ground.  For "sky," use 天空 (tiānkōng).

~
站台
In Taiwan, 站台 also means "to publicly support someone," often a political candidate.

~
电视机
电视机 specifically refers to the television set itself.  For television programs or broadcasting, use 电视 (diànshì).

~
拆迁
拆迁 is a sensitive topic in China, often associated with forced relocation and social issues.

~
怎么办
怎么办 expresses perplexity and seeks a solution.  It's not simply asking "how to do something" but rather "what should be done in this difficult situation?"

~
意志
Often used in the four character idiom 意志坚定 (yìzhì jiāndìng), which means showing great resolution or perseverance in the face of difficulty.


~
负
As a verb, this is literary/formal and not as commonly used as other words with similar meaning, such as 输 (shū), 败 (bài), or 失败 (shībài).


~
设计师
Can refer to any kind of designer, not just architects or building designers. For example, a fashion designer is a 服装设计师 (fúzhuāng shèjìshī).


~
问路
More often used to describe asking for directions in person, rather than using a map app.


~
音节
The concept of a "syllable" is slightly different in Chinese compared to English. While English syllables can have complex consonant clusters, Chinese syllables are generally simpler, consisting of an initial consonant (optional), a vowel, and a final consonant (optional). Be aware that tones play a significant role in distinguishing syllables in Chinese.


~
厂长
This term typically refers to the director of a factory in a more traditional, state-owned enterprise setting. In modern, private companies, terms like 总经理 (zǒng jīnglǐ) or CEO are more common.


~
本土
Be aware of the political context of 本土 in relation to discussions of Taiwan, where it can carry sensitive connotations. In less politically charged situations, it simply refers to local or domestic.


~
出事
Implies a serious accident or mishap, often involving injury or other significant negative consequences. For minor incidents, other words would be more appropriate.


~
电灯
This term is somewhat dated and less commonly used than the more general term 灯 (dēng).


~
尽
This character has many meanings and can be tricky to use correctly. Pay close attention to its different usages and grammatical roles.


~
好好
As an adverb meaning "properly" or "carefully", 好好 often appears reduplicated and placed before the verb it modifies.  For example, 好好学习 (hǎohǎo xuéxí) – study hard, 好好工作 (hǎohǎo gōngzuò) – work hard, 好好休息 (hǎohǎo xiūxi) – rest well.


~
机制
Be aware of the different meanings of 机制. It can refer to a literal mechanical mechanism or a more abstract system or process.


~
清
This character, while simple-looking, has a wide range of meanings and pronunciations. Be sure to study them carefully.


~
行驶
Specifically used for vehicles, especially motorized vehicles. Don't use it for people walking or cycling.


~
场所
More formal than 地方 (dìfang) and implies a specific designated area for a particular activity.


~
奔跑
Implies running quickly and energetically, more so than the more general word 跑 (pǎo).


~
送到
Often followed by a location word, indicating the destination of the delivery.


~
诗歌
Can refer to poetry in general or to a specific poem. Note the different measure words used.


~
持有
Often used in formal contexts, such as holding a license, passport, or official document.


~
除
The meaning and usage of 除 can be tricky. Pay attention to the context to determine whether it means "except" or "remove."


~
卫生
Encompasses broader concepts of health and sanitation, beyond just personal hygiene.


~
名
Has a literary connotation when used to mean "famous." More commonly, it's used as a noun meaning "name" or as a classifier for people.


~
撤离
Implies a planned and organized withdrawal, often in response to an emergency or dangerous situation.


~
摄像头
A general term for cameras used in surveillance or recording, including webcams, security cameras, and traffic cameras.


~
羽绒服
Specifically refers to down jackets or other clothing filled with down feathers.


~
路边
Can refer to the side of any road, from a small street to a highway.


~
众多
More formal than 多 (duō) and emphasizes a large and varied collection.


~
路过
Indicates passing by a place without stopping or entering.


~
夫妻
Refers to a married couple. For unmarried couples, other terms are used.


~
房价
Specifically refers to the price of housing or real estate.


~
双打
Used in the context of sports or games where two players compete as a team against another team of two.


~
变更
Implies a more formal or official change than 改变 (gǎibiàn).


~
变
A versatile word with broad meanings related to change or transformation. Pay attention to context to understand the specific meaning.


~
法
Has various meanings, including law, method, and way. It's also an abbreviation for France. Be sure to distinguish between these meanings based on context.


~
重组
Implies a significant restructuring or reorganization, often in a business or organizational context.


~
肠
Refers to the intestines or bowels. Can be used literally or figuratively.


~
化石
Refers to fossils, the preserved remains of ancient organisms.


~
癌症
A general term for cancer, a serious medical condition.


~
牺牲
Can refer to sacrificing something tangible or intangible, such as one's life, time, or resources.


~
命大
An idiomatic expression implying that someone is fortunate or lucky to have survived a dangerous situation.

~
飞船
While both 飞船 and 宇宙飞船 can be translated as "spaceship," 宇宙飞船 is more specific and refers to spacecraft that travel beyond Earth's atmosphere. 飞船 can also refer to airships or dirigibles.

~
测定
测定 emphasizes the process of measurement and obtaining a precise result, often involving scientific instruments or methods.  It's suitable for contexts where accuracy and precision are important.  A similar word, 测量 (cèliáng), focuses on the act of measuring itself, which may or may not lead to a precise determination.

~
影视
影视 is a combined term referring to both film and television as a single industry or category.  It's often used in contexts like 影视作品 (yǐngshì zuòpǐn) – film and television productions, or 影视明星 (yǐngshì míngxīng) – film and television stars.

~
体操
体操 refers specifically to gymnastics as a sport or physical activity. It doesn't encompass other forms of physical exercise.

~
此事
此事 is a formal and somewhat literary way of saying "this matter."  In casual conversation, 这件事 (zhè jiàn shì) or simply 这事 (zhè shì) are more common.

~
命案
命案 specifically refers to a criminal case involving death or murder.  案件 (ànjiàn) is a more general term for "case."

~
衬衣
衬衣 refers to shirts worn as an undergarment, such as dress shirts or blouses.  For casual shirts or T-shirts, you would use other terms like T恤 (T xù) or 短袖衫 (duǎn xiù shān).

~
疯
疯 can be used both literally and figuratively.  It can mean "insane" in the clinical sense but also "crazy" in a more casual sense, to describe someone's wild or eccentric behavior.  Be mindful of the context to avoid causing offense.

~
真的
真的 can function both as an adjective meaning "real" or "true" and as an adverb meaning "really" or "truly."  Its meaning depends on the context.

~
目光
目光 refers specifically to the gaze or expression in one's eyes.  It carries a more nuanced meaning than simply "eyes" and often reflects emotions or intentions.

~
方便面
方便面 is the standard term for "instant noodles" throughout China.  泡面 (pào miàn) is a more colloquial term commonly used in some regions.

~
慢慢
慢慢 is an adverb that can mean both "slowly" and "gradually."  The specific meaning is usually clear from the context.

~
知足
知足 emphasizes contentment and satisfaction with one's current situation.  It's often used in the phrase 知足常乐 (zhīzú chánglè) - contentment brings constant happiness.

~
陷入
陷入 suggests falling into a difficult or negative situation, like a trap or a state of despair.  It carries a stronger negative connotation than simply "entering" or "getting into."

~
那样
那样 implies a similarity or comparison with something previously mentioned.  It can also emphasize the degree or extent of something.

~
考题
考题 refers specifically to the questions on an examination.  试卷 (shìjuàn) refers to the entire exam paper.

~
后边
后边 refers to the space or area behind something.  后面 (hòumiàn) is more general and can also refer to the later part of a period of time.

~
艰难
艰难 emphasizes the difficulty and hardship of a task or situation.  困难 (kùnnan) is a more general term for difficulty.

~
长短
长短 can refer to both physical length and more abstract concepts like the merits and demerits of something. Be aware of the context to determine the intended meaning.

~
晴朗
晴朗 describes weather that is sunny and clear.  晴天 (qíngtiān) simply means "sunny day."

~
火腿
火腿 refers to cured ham.  If you want to specify cooked ham, you would use 熟火腿 (shú huǒtuǐ).

~
水槽
水槽 generally refers to any kind of sink or basin used for washing.  洗碗池 (xǐwǎnchí) specifically refers to a kitchen sink.

~
以便
以便 indicates purpose or intention, similar to "in order to" or "so that."  为了 (wèile) is another way to express purpose, but 以便 is often considered more formal.

~
轮船
轮船 specifically refers to ships propelled by paddle wheels or propellers.  船 (chuán) is a more general term for boats and ships.

~
救援
救援 emphasizes the act of saving or rescuing someone from danger or distress.  帮助 (bāngzhù) is a more general term for helping.

~
清晨
清晨 specifically refers to the early hours of the morning, typically before sunrise.  早上 (zǎoshang) is a more general term for morning.

~
拆除
拆除 implies taking something apart completely, often involving destruction.  移除 (yí chú) means to remove or take away, which may not involve dismantling.

~
回去
回去 emphasizes returning to a place where one was previously.  返回 (fǎnhuí) has a similar meaning but can also refer to returning something to its original state.

~
开业
开业 specifically refers to the grand opening or commencement of a business.  开始营业 (kāishǐ yíngyè) means "to start doing business" and is more general.

~
只见
只见 is used to highlight a specific observation, often to emphasize contrast or surprise. It suggests that only the mentioned thing was seen, even though other things might have been present.

~
旅行社
旅行社 is the standard term for "travel agency" in China.

~
不怎么
不怎么 indicates something is not done to a great extent or not very often. It's more emphatic than simply saying "not very."

~
推出
推出 can have multiple meanings depending on the context. It can mean "to push out" literally, but it's also commonly used figuratively to mean "to release," "to launch," "to introduce," or "to recommend."

~
窗台
窗台 refers specifically to the horizontal surface at the bottom of a window.

~
烟
烟 can refer to smoke, tobacco, or cigarettes.  The specific meaning depends on the context.  香烟 (xiāngyān) is the specific term for cigarettes.

~
毒品
毒品 refers to illegal drugs or narcotics.  药品 (yàopǐn) refers to medicines or pharmaceuticals.

~
理财
理财 encompasses various activities related to managing personal finances, including investing, saving, and budgeting.  It's a broader term than simply "saving money."

~
种种
种种 emphasizes a variety of factors, reasons, or elements.  It's often used to summarize multiple items or to express the complexity of a situation.

~
造型
造型 can refer to the overall shape, form, or design of something, often in the context of art, fashion, or product design. It can also refer to a specific pose or posture.

~
年度
年度 refers to a specific year, often used in formal contexts like financial reports or annual reviews.  年 (nián) is the more common and general term for "year."

~
A变了
The structure "A + 变 + 了" indicates a change in A's state.  The “了” (le) particle signifies the completion of the change.  The context determines whether this change is positive, negative, or neutral.

~
宁静
While 宁静 translates to "peaceful" or "tranquil," it carries a more profound sense of stillness and quietude compared to other similar words like 安静 (ān jìng - quiet). 宁静 often describes a state of inner peace or the serenity of nature, whereas 安静 simply refers to the absence of noise.

~
茶叶
The measure words for 茶叶 are worth noting.  盒 (hé) is for a box of tea, 罐 (guàn) is for a tin or canister, 包 (bāo) refers to a bag or packet, and 片 (piàn) is used for individual tea leaves.

~
屋
屋 (wū) is a more literary and less common way to say "room" or "house" than  房间 (fángjiān) or 房子 (fángzi). You'll likely encounter it more in formal writing or older texts.

~
赠送
赠送 (zèngsòng) implies giving a gift with a sense of formality or respect.  It's more formal than simply giving something (给 - gěi).  It's often used for presenting gifts to superiors, organizations, or in official ceremonies.

~
支配
支配 (zhīpèi) suggests a higher level of control than simply managing or directing. It implies having authority or power over something or someone, even manipulating or dominating.

~
法规
法规 (fǎguī) encompasses both laws and regulations, often referring to specific rules within a larger legal framework. It is broader than just 法律 (fǎlǜ - law), which refers to more fundamental legal principles.

~
班级
班级 (bānjí) refers specifically to a class as a group of students, while 年级 (niánjí) refers to a grade level within a school system.

~
微波炉
The measure word for 微波炉 is 台 (tái), commonly used for appliances and machines.

~
途中
途中 (túzhōng) specifically refers to being *in the middle of* a journey. It doesn't just mean "on the way" in a general sense but emphasizes the ongoing nature of the travel.

~
摔进
摔进 (shuāi jìn) emphasizes falling *into* something.  The "进" (jìn) part implies entering or penetrating a space as a result of the fall.

~
游人
游人 (yóurén) specifically refers to people traveling for leisure or sightseeing, whereas 游客 (yóukè) can also include people traveling for other purposes.

~
最佳
最佳 (zuì jiā) unequivocally denotes "the best." It implies a superlative quality and is often used in formal or evaluative contexts.

~
队员
队员 (duìyuán) specifically refers to a member of a team, emphasizing belonging and participation within a group.

~
福
福 (fú) has deep cultural significance, representing good fortune, happiness, and blessings.  It's a common motif in Chinese culture, especially during festivals and celebrations.

~
促销
促销 (cùxiāo) specifically refers to sales promotions aimed at boosting sales volume, often involving discounts, special offers, or other marketing tactics.

~
或
或 (huò) is used as an inclusive "or," suggesting one or more of the options are possible. It differs from 或者 (huòzhě), which can also be exclusive ("either... or...").

~
比重
比重 (bǐzhòng) can refer to both specific gravity in scientific contexts and the relative importance or proportion of something in general usage.

~
理
理 (lǐ) is a complex word with multiple meanings. It can refer to reason, logic, truth, as well as the natural order of things.  It can also mean "to manage" or "to pay attention to."

~
代理
代理 (dàilǐ) emphasizes acting *on behalf of* someone, often with a formal or legal authorization. It can also refer to acting as a substitute or proxy.

~
确立
确立 (quèlì) emphasizes the *firm establishment* of something, often a concept, principle, or system. It implies a sense of finality and stability.

~
音量
音量 (yīnliàng) specifically refers to the loudness or volume of sound.

~
首次
首次 (shǒucì) explicitly means "for the first time," emphasizing the inaugural nature of an event.

~
上门
上门 (shàngmén) can mean "to drop in" for a visit but can also refer to services that come to your home, like repairs or deliveries. It can also have the traditional meaning of a man moving in with his wife's family.

~
楼下
楼下 (lóuxià) can also be used figuratively to refer to people who live downstairs, even if they are not directly beneath you.

~
没有
没有 (méiyǒu) serves as both a negation of possession ("don't have") and existence ("there isn't").

~
官司
The measure word for 官司 (guānsi - lawsuit) is 场 (chǎng), indicating an event or occasion.

~
价钱
价钱 (jiàqian) is a more colloquial term for "price" than 价格 (jiàgé).

~
另
另 (lìng) is used to indicate something different, separate, or additional.  It's often used in constructions like 另外 (lìngwài - in addition, moreover).

~
热水
热水 (rèshuǐ) specifically refers to *hot* water, as opposed to warm or boiling water.

~
哇
哇 (wa) is an onomatopoeia, mimicking the sound of crying, vomiting, or expressing surprise.

~
职务
职务 (zhíwù) encompasses both the position or post held and the duties and responsibilities associated with it.

~
才能
才能 (cáinéng) refers to an innate ability or talent, often suggesting a natural aptitude or gift.

~
大海
大海 (dàhǎi) evokes a more poetic and vast image of the sea or ocean than simply 海 (hǎi).

~
用处
用处 (yòngchu) refers to the usefulness or practicality of something.

~
划分
划分 (huàfēn) means to divide or categorize things according to specific criteria, implying a more systematic or organized division than simply splitting something apart.

~
一同
一同 (yītóng) implies doing something together in the same place and at the same time, emphasizing shared participation in an activity.

~
汽车
汽车 (qìchē) can refer to both cars and buses. Context usually clarifies the specific meaning.

~
不光
不光 (bùguāng) means "not only," introducing additional information or actions beyond the initial statement.  It requires a follow-up clause, usually connected by "而且" (érqiě - but also) or "还" (hái - also).


~
称号
称号 (chēnghào) specifically refers to a title or appellation, often honorary or descriptive, that is bestowed upon someone or something. It carries more weight and formality than simply a name.

~
继承

There are two main verbs for "inherit" in Chinese: 继承 (jìchéng) and 遗传 (yíchuán).  While both relate to passing things down, 继承 refers to inheriting non-physical things like traditions, titles, beliefs, or property.  遗传 is for inheriting physical traits or genetic conditions.  Think of 继承 as "to inherit" and 遗传 as "to be inherited."

~
坏人

While 坏人 literally translates to "bad person," it carries a stronger connotation than simply "bad."  It implies someone who is actively malicious, villainous, or even criminal.  For a more general "bad person," consider using 不好的人 (bù hǎo de rén).

~
救助

救助 carries a more formal and serious tone than other words for "help" like 帮助 (bāngzhù).  It often implies a situation of danger, emergency, or significant hardship.  Think of 救助 as closer to "rescue" or "relief."

~
晓得

晓得 is primarily used in spoken language and has a regional feel, most commonly associated with southern dialects.  知道 (zhīdào) is the more common and versatile word for "to know."

~
调解

调解 emphasizes mediating between two or more parties in a dispute, often with the goal of reaching a compromise.  It is a more formal term than 说和 (shuōhé), which also means "to mediate" but is used in less serious situations.

~
马车

马车 is a general term for horse-drawn carriages.  However, if you want to be more specific, you can use 馬車 (mǎchē) for a general carriage, 馬車 (mǎchē) for a wagon or cart, and 戰車 (zhànchē) for a chariot.

~
码头

While 码头 can refer to any docking area, it more often refers to piers or wharves used for passenger transport.  For cargo docks, 港口 (gǎngkǒu) is a more appropriate term.

~
费用

费用 refers to the cost of a service or activity, such as tuition fees or travel expenses.  It carries a more formal connotation than other words for cost, such as 价格 (jiàgé) for the price of goods or 成本 (chéngběn) for production costs.

~
随后

随后 emphasizes the immediacy of following, suggesting little to no time gap.  It is closer to "immediately after" or "right after."  稍后 (shāo hòu) means "a little later."

~
树叶

树叶 can be both singular and plural, so you wouldn't have to say "树叶们" to pluralize.


~
补助

补助 specifically refers to financial aid or subsidies provided to individuals or organizations, often by the government.  It's different from 津贴 (jīntiē), which are specific allowances given for a particular purpose (like housing allowance).

~
增

增 is often used as a component in compound words, such as 增加 (zēngjiā) "to increase," 增多 (zēngduō) "to increase in number," or 增強 (zēngqiáng) "to strengthen."  It’s less common as a standalone verb.

~
机动车

机动车 is a broad term encompassing all motorized vehicles, including cars, trucks, buses, and motorcycles.  汽车 (qìchē) specifically refers to cars or automobiles.

~
医疗

医疗 refers to the entire system and practice of medical care, including treatment, prevention, and research.  治疗 (zhìliáo) is more specific to the act of treating a disease or injury.

~
或是

或是 implies a choice between two exclusive options, similar to "either... or..."  或者 (huòzhě) can also mean "or," but can also connect more than two options or non-exclusive options.

~
学科

学科 is a more formal and academic term for a field of study than 科目 (kēmù), which usually refers to a school subject.

~
国会

Remember that 国会 corresponds to the legislative body of a specific country.  It's not always a direct equivalent to "parliament" or "congress."  For example, Japan's parliament is called 国会 (guóhuì) in Chinese, while the US Congress is 美国国会 (měiguó guóhuì).

~
镜头

镜头 can refer to both the physical camera lens and a shot or scene in a film.  The context usually clarifies the meaning.

~
间接

间接 means "indirect," emphasizing that something occurs through an intermediary or intermediate step.  It's often used in contrast with 直接 (zhíjiē) "direct."

~
快速

快速 emphasizes speed and efficiency, often implying modern technology or advanced methods.  快 (kuài) is a more general term for "fast."

~
无效

无效 means something is legally or officially not valid or effective.  It carries a more formal tone than 没用 (méiyòng), which simply means "useless" or "ineffective."

~
展现

展现 suggests a gradual or unfolding revelation of something.  It's often used for abstract concepts like talent or potential.  显示 (xiǎnshì) is more general for "to show" or "to display."

~
困惑

困惑 suggests a state of being deeply puzzled or bewildered, often about something complex or difficult to understand.  It is stronger than simply confused and closer to "perplexed."

~
内蒙古

内蒙古 is the shortened form of 内蒙古自治区 (Nèi Měnggǔ Zìzhìqū), the Inner Mongolia Autonomous Region.  Be mindful of the full name in formal contexts.

~
组长

组长 is a general term for a group leader, and the specific responsibilities can vary widely depending on the context.

~
午餐

午餐 is a more formal term for "lunch" than 午饭 (wǔfàn), which is more commonly used in everyday conversation.

~
暴雨

暴雨 indicates heavy rainfall, significantly stronger than just heavy rain.  It suggests potential for flooding or other weather-related damage.

~
塞

塞 has multiple meanings, including "to fill," "to stuff," "a strategic pass," and "Serbia." Pay attention to context to determine the correct meaning.

~
停止

停止 implies a complete cessation of an action or process.  暂停 (zàntíng) means to temporarily pause or suspend something, with the possibility of resuming later.

~
口号

口号 usually refers to slogans used for political, social, or commercial purposes.  标语 (biāoyǔ) can also mean "slogan," but often refers to written slogans or banners.

~
戏曲

戏曲 encompasses a variety of traditional Chinese theatrical forms, including opera and other musical performances.  It is broader than just Chinese opera.


~
急救

急救 refers to providing immediate and temporary medical care in emergency situations.  It is more specific than 救治 (jiùzhì), which refers to medical treatment in general.

~
得了

得了 has two main meanings. One is an imperative meaning "stop it," "cut it out," or "enough!" The other indicates understanding or agreement like “got it,” "okay," or "fine." Tone and context are essential to understanding which meaning is intended.

~
时时

时时, while meaning "often" or "constantly," is somewhat literary or archaic.  常常 (chángcháng), 经常 (jīngcháng), or 总是 (zǒngshì) are more common in modern usage.

~
起码

起码 emphasizes the absolute minimum requirement or lowest acceptable standard.  至少 (zhìshǎo) also means "at least," but doesn't necessarily carry the same sense of a bare minimum.

~
型

型 refers to a general type, model, or style.  类型 (lèixíng) is more specific and refers to a category or classification.

~
海底

海底 specifically refers to the ocean floor or seabed.  水底 (shuǐdǐ) is a more general term for the bottom of any body of water.


~
不大

不大 is generally used before adjectives or verbs and can have different nuances depending on context. It can indicate small size (not big), low frequency (not often), or mild degree (not very).  It can also be a polite way to downplay something.

~
斗争

斗争 carries a more intense and often political connotation than other words for fighting or struggling, such as 奋斗 (fèndòu) "to strive" or  努力 (nǔlì) "to work hard."  It often implies conflict, resistance, or opposition.

~
长大

长大 specifically means "to grow up," referring to the process of maturing from childhood to adulthood.  长大 also carries the connotation of becoming bigger physically.  成长 (chéngzhǎng) is a broader term encompassing various aspects of development, both physical and mental.

~
摄像机
No additional notes.

~
树林
Remember that this can also refer to Shulin city in New Taipei City.

~
动
This word has a more literary meaning of "to alter," which is quite different from its usual meaning of "to move."

~
母子
This can refer to either mother and child or mother and son. It can also refer to a parent and subsidiary company, or even principle and interest!

~
背着
This word has the additional meaning of "keeping (one's hands) behind one's back."

~
大爷
This word can also be used in a derogatory way, to refer to an arrogant, self-centered show-off.

~
本事
This word has the additional, somewhat literary meaning of "source material" (of a story).

~
闹
This word has a large number of meanings besides "noisy," including:
*   to suffer (from a disease)
*   to vent (feelings)
*   to go in for (some activity)
*   to joke

~
被迫
No additional notes.

~
车辆
No additional notes.

~
饼
No additional notes.

~
一下子
This word can also mean "for a short while." Note the possible contradiction between this and its primary meaning.

~
今日
This is more formal/literary than 今天.

~
出来
出来 can often be placed after a verb, where it indicates completion of the action, or the ability to discern or detect something.  For example, 看出来 (kàn chūlái) - to be able to see / to realize.

~
烧
烧 can also mean "to run a fever."  Colloquially, it can also mean "to let things go to one's head".

~
发行
No additional notes.

~
盲人
No additional notes.

~
网
No additional notes.

~
顾
This word has additional meanings of "to look after" and "to attend to." Note the similarity to its usage in the word 照顾 (zhàogù).

~
开花
Figuratively, this can mean "to burst," "to split open," or "to burst with joy." It can also mean "to spring up everywhere" or "to flourish."

~
黑暗
No additional notes.

~
反抗
No additional notes.

~
受灾
This word can also refer to *the people* who are afflicted by a disaster, rather than the disaster itself.

~
依次
No additional notes.

~
文娱
No additional notes.

~
考生
No additional notes.

~
公民
No additional notes.

~
咱
Although this word is often taught as simply meaning "we," it can also mean "I" or "me." Note the possible ambiguity.

~
视为
No additional notes.

~
有毒
No additional notes.

~
外界
No additional notes.

~
少数
No additional notes.

~
现状
No additional notes.

~
抓住
No additional notes.

~
清洗
This word can have the darker connotation of a political purge.

~
炸药
No additional notes.

~
拾
Besides meaning to pick something up, this has the additional meaning of "to ascend in light steps."  Also, the character is used as the banker's anti-fraud numeral for "ten".

~
企图
No additional notes.

~
体育馆
No additional notes.

~
市长
No additional notes.

~
辈
Can be used to refer to people of the same generation as oneself (e.g., 我们这一辈人), or a generation older than oneself (e.g., 父辈, 上辈), or a generation younger than oneself (e.g., 下一辈).  It emphasizes the generational relationship more than the specific age.

~
手续费
While 手续费 generally refers to a handling or processing fee, it often carries a negative connotation in colloquial Chinese, suggesting an unnecessary or excessive charge.  Think of it as "hidden fees" or "extra charges".

~
金钱
金钱 is more formal and literary than just 钱.  It can sometimes carry a slightly negative connotation, implying greed or materialism, especially when used in idioms like 金钱至上 (money is paramount) or 见钱眼开 (eyes light up at the sight of money).

~
权
权 is often paired with 利 (lì, benefit/profit) to form 权益 (quányì, rights and interests) or 权利 (quánlì, rights/power).  It's essential to distinguish between 权利 and 权力 (quánlì, power/authority).

~
黄瓜
In some dialects, 黄瓜 specifically refers to the cucumber melon.

~
尺
尺 (chǐ) as a unit of measurement is approximately one-third of a meter. However, its actual length has varied throughout history. The modern definition is exactly one-third of a meter.

~
清明节
Tomb-Sweeping Day is a significant holiday in Chinese culture, involving visiting ancestral graves, cleaning and offering food and incense.  It's a time for remembering and honoring ancestors.

~
茄子
The slang usage of 茄子 (qiézi) as "say cheese" comes from its pronunciation, which sounds vaguely similar to "cheese."  It's commonly used by photographers to get people to smile.

~
意味着
意味着 (yìwèizhe) implies a deeper, more significant meaning or consequence, often with long-term implications.  It's stronger than simply "to mean."

~
地名
Be aware of the tones: 地名 (dìmíng).  Many learners mistakenly pronounce it as dì míng.

~
肥
肥 (féi) can also mean "loose-fitting" for clothing.  Be aware of the context to avoid misunderstanding.

~
取得
取得 emphasizes the process of obtaining something through effort or achievement, often something valuable or significant.

~
有力
有力 can describe physical strength, a strong argument, or powerful evidence.  It implies effectiveness and impact.

~
小声
小声 is often used as an imperative:  小声点儿 (xiǎoshēng diǎnr) - "Be quiet!" or "Speak softly!"

~
动态
动态 usually refers to trends, developments, or news, often implying change or progress.  It's frequently used in news reports or analysis.

~
就要
就要 implies imminence - something is about to happen very soon.

~
迷
迷 can be used with various hobbies or interests, like  球迷 (qí mí, soccer fan), 影迷 (yǐng mí, movie fan), etc.

~
心灵
心灵 refers to the inner world of thoughts, feelings, and spirit.  It's more profound than just "mind" or "heart."

~
南部
南部 is a general term.  For specific southern regions of China, more precise terms are often used, like 华南 (South China) or西南 (Southwest China).

~
美女
美女 is a common and generally polite way to address or refer to a woman, especially in service industries.  However, overuse can sound insincere or even inappropriate in certain contexts.

~
书房
书房 is a dedicated room for studying and reading, often containing bookshelves, a desk, and other related items.

~
期限
期限 always refers to a specific deadline or time limit, often with consequences if it's not met.

~
括号
Remember the different types of brackets:  圆括号 (yuán kuòhào) - parentheses ( ), 方括号 (fāng kuòhào) - square brackets [ ], and 尖括号 (jiān kuòhào) - angle brackets < >.

~
王后
王后 specifically refers to the queen consort, the wife of a king.

~
公告
公告 is a formal, official announcement, often issued by government or other authorities.

~
证实
证实 implies providing concrete evidence or proof to verify something.  It's more formal and authoritative than just "to confirm."

~
彩色
彩色 refers to multiple colors, while 颜色 (yánsè) is a more general term for color.

~
塑料
塑料 is a non-biodegradable material, so its environmental impact is a growing concern in China.

~
设置
设置 implies configuring or establishing something, often involving specific parameters or options.

~
看上去
看上去 is based on visual observation, while 觉得 (juéde) is based on overall feeling or impression.

~
侧
侧 can also mean "to incline towards" in a figurative sense, as in 侧重 (cèzhòng), "to emphasize" or "to focus on."

~
强壮
强壮 emphasizes physical strength and robustness, often implying good health and vitality.

~
王
王 is also used in the names of playing cards, chess pieces, and certain animals, like the 王牌 (wángpái, ace) or  狮王 (shīwáng, lion king).

~
著作
著作 refers to significant written works, often academic or literary in nature.

~
过年
过年 involves various customs and traditions, such as family reunions, giving red envelopes (红包, hóngbāo), and setting off firecrackers.

~
病情
病情 is used to describe the current state of a patient's illness, whether improving or worsening.

~
当选
当选 specifically means to be successfully elected to a position or office.

~
看到
看到 emphasizes the act of seeing something, while 看见 (kànjiàn) emphasizes the result of seeing something.

~
花瓶
The figurative use of 花瓶 as a "pretty face" is generally derogatory, suggesting a lack of substance or ability.

~
过道
过道 is a narrow passageway or aisle, often for walking through.

~
掌声
Like many words for sounds, 掌声 is measure word is 阵 (zhèn). You can say 一阵掌声 (yī zhèn zhǎngshēng) - a round of applause.

~
楼上
This has two meanings. It means "upstairs", but on the internet it can also mean "the previous poster". This is analogous to how some English internet forums will refer to previous posters with a caret (^).

~
族
族 (zú) has a similar range of meanings to English words like "clan", "tribe", and "race/ethnicity", but in modern Chinese it can also be used to refer to any social group, particularly one defined by occupation or hobby.  For example, 上班族 (shàngbānzú) refers to office workers,  月光族 (yuèguāngzú) refers to people who spend their entire monthly salary, and  低头族 (dītóuzú) refers to people who constantly look down at their phones.

~
内心
Aside from its literal meaning of "inner heart; innermost being," 内心 (nèixīn) can also be used in mathematics to refer to the "incenter" of a triangle or other geometric figure.

~
冰
In slang, 冰 (bīng) can refer to crystal methamphetamine.

~
哪里
Aside from its usage as a question word, 哪里 (nǎlǐ) is also used as a humble expression to deny a compliment, similar to "Where do you get that idea?" in English.  For instance, if someone praises your cooking, you might respond with  哪里哪里 (nǎlǐ nǎlǐ).

~
枝
枝 (zhī) is a measure word specifically for long, thin objects like branches, sticks, pencils, flowers and so on.  Don't confuse it with 支 (zhī), which has broader applications but isn't used for things that grow naturally, like plants.

~
代表团
The measure word for 代表团 (dàibiǎotuán) is 个 (gè).  This might seem unusual for a group, but it's the standard measure word.

~
大学生
大学生 (dàxuéshēng) refers specifically to university students. College students are called 大专生 (dàzhuānshēng).

~
消防
消防 (xiāofáng) combines "fire prevention" (消) and "firefighting" (防).  Therefore, it covers both aspects of fire safety.

~
教学楼
教学楼 (jiàoxué lóu) refers specifically to the building where teaching takes place. Administrative or other buildings on a school campus would not be called 教学楼.

~
餐饮
餐饮 (cānyǐn) is a more formal word that combines both food (餐) and drink (饮), often used in commercial contexts or when referring to the food service industry as a whole.

~
定
定 (dìng) has a wide range of meanings, so its meaning must be determined from context.

~
战胜
战胜 (zhànshèng) specifically refers to winning in a battle, competition, or against something abstract.  It doesn't refer to winning a prize or a lottery; the verb for those would be 中 (zhòng).

~
上去
上去 (shàngqù) implies movement upwards and away from the speaker.

~
调动
调动 (diàodòng) can refer to the transfer of personnel, but more broadly, it means to mobilize or redeploy resources.

~
将
The word 将 (jiāng) has a similar usage to the word 把 (bǎ). Both are used to introduce the object of the verb and to emphasize the action being done on the object. The difference is subtle, but 将 emphasizes that the object is undergoing some transformation as a result of the verb.

~
舌头
舌头 (shétou) literally means "tongue", but it also has a figurative meaning, which is not obvious from the dictionary definition. It can refer to an enemy soldier captured specifically to obtain information.

~
曾
曾 (céng) can act as a past tense marker, even if the word "already" doesn't seem to make sense in the English translation.

~
低头
低头 (dītóu) literally means "lower one's head," but it also carries the figurative meaning of "to submit" or "to give in."

~
卫星
The measure word for 卫星 (wèixīng) is 颗 (kē), which is used for small, round objects.

~
球队
球队 (qiúduì) refers to any sports team that plays with a ball.  It's more general than specific team names like basketball team or soccer team.

~
深度
深度 (shēndù) has both a literal meaning of physical depth and a figurative meaning referring to the profundity or complexity of something, such as a discussion or analysis.

~
类
Aside from meaning "category" or "type," 类 (lèi) can also function similarly to the English suffix "-like" or the word "similar." For example,  猫科动物 (māokē dòngwù) translates to "cat-like animals" or "felines."

~
不顾
不顾 (bùgù) often appears paired with a contrasting clause, often introduced by 但是 (dànshì) or 可是 (kěshì).

~
下来
下来 (xiàlái) implies downward movement toward the speaker.  It's also commonly used as a complement indicating completion of an action.

~
显著
显著 (xiǎnzhuó) often refers to a statistically significant result or a noticeable, evident difference.

~
歌手
歌手 (gēshǒu) specifically refers to a professional singer.  Someone who sings casually wouldn't be called a 歌手.

~
投诉
投诉 (tóusù) specifically refers to making a formal complaint, usually to a business or authority.  It's more formal than simply complaining to a friend.

~
预计
预计 (yùjì) often implies a degree of uncertainty, similar to "forecast" or "project" in English.

~
性能
性能 (xìngnéng) doesn't just refer to general performance; it refers specifically to measurable capabilities or functionalities, like the performance of a machine or device.

~
模范
模范 (mófàn) implies not just being a good example, but also being worthy of emulation or imitation.

~
教学
教学 (jiàoxué) can refer to both the act of teaching (verb) and the methods or content of instruction (noun).

~
舍得
舍得 (shěde) implies a willingness to part with something valuable, either literally or figuratively.

~
中
中 (zhōng) can also mean "to win" (a prize, lottery, etc.).  Don't confuse this with 战胜 (zhànshèng), which is to defeat an opponent.

~
药片
药片 (yàopiàn) refers specifically to a solid pill or tablet. Liquid medicine or other forms are not called 药片.

~
建造
建造 (jiànzào) emphasizes the construction of large structures like buildings or ships.  For smaller objects, other verbs might be more appropriate.

~
录音机
录音机 (lùyīnjī) is an older term for a tape recorder.  Modern recording devices would be called 录音笔 (lùyīnbǐ) for digital recorders or simply 录音设备 (lùyīn shèbèi) for recording equipment.

~
不少
不少 (bùshǎo) is a double negative meaning "not few," therefore, "a lot" or "many."

~
处在
处在 (chǔzài) emphasizes being in a particular state or situation, rather than simply a physical location.

~
挨着
This word emphasizes physical closeness, often involving direct contact or proximity.  Think "snuggled up against" or "right next to".  It's more intimate than 靠近 (kàojìn), which simply means "near" or "close to".

~
转动
When referring to circular motion, 转动 is a general term, while 旋转 (xuánzhuǎn) specifically implies rotation around an axis.  For example, a wheel 转动, but the Earth 旋转.

~
扇
As a measure word, 扇 is specifically for things with a flat, swinging or opening/closing motion, primarily doors and windows.

~
平方米
Remember the measure word is 平方米, not just 米.

~
商标
This includes both trademarks and logos, but 商标 emphasizes the legal protection aspect more.

~
带来
This word implies a direct cause-and-effect relationship.  The thing brought has a tangible impact.  It's not just bringing an object, but bringing a consequence.

~
读音
This refers specifically to the pronunciation of a single character, not a whole word or sentence.  For pronunciation of words or phrases, use 发音 (fāyīn).

~
塔
While 塔 can refer to various tower-like structures, it primarily signifies a Buddhist pagoda.

~
制成
This word highlights the process of transformation or creation.  It emphasizes the raw materials and the final product.

~
胜
Besides "win" or "defeat," 胜 also means "surpass" or "be better than." In this sense, it often follows 比 (bǐ). For example, A 比 B 胜 (A is better than B).

~
专用
This implies exclusivity and restriction to a specific purpose. It's stronger than 特用 (tèyòng), which just means "special purpose" but doesn't necessarily imply restricted access.

~
晚点
Specifically used for transportation delays. For other types of lateness, use  迟到 (chídào).

~
严厉
This implies not just strictness but also a harsh or severe manner of enforcement.  It carries a stronger negative connotation than 严格 (yángé), which is simply "strict" without necessarily being unpleasant.

~
紧
紧 has many meanings. In terms of urgency, 紧急 (jǐnjí) is a more formal synonym.  When describing physical tightness, it implies a state of tension or pressure.

~
常规
This refers to established norms or procedures, often implying a sense of habit or routine.

~
关怀
This implies deep and genuine care, often from someone in a position of authority or responsibility, like a leader or elder.  It's more profound than 关心 (guānxīn), which is general concern.

~
自身
This emphasizes the independent nature of the subject, often contrasting it with external factors. It's more emphatic than 自己 (zìjǐ).

~
等候
This suggests a respectful or patient wait, often for someone of higher status. It's more formal than 等 (děng).

~
虎
The measure word is 只 (zhī), used for most animals.

~
顾问
This refers to a professional advisor, often in a formal capacity.  It's more formal than simply 劝告 (quàngào), which is just "advice."

~
简介
This is a concise summary, focusing on key points. It's shorter and more focused than 介绍 (jièshào), which can be a more detailed introduction.

~
街头
Refers specifically to the end of a street, or a place where streets intersect.  It's more specific than just 街道 (jiēdào), which refers to streets in general.

~
饭
Besides rice or a meal, 饭 can also be used as a suffix for fans of certain things, like 影迷 (yǐngmí) for movie fans.

~
同期
This emphasizes the exact correspondence in time, often used for comparisons or statistics.

~
公认
Implies widespread acceptance or acknowledgement, often as a standard or authority.

~
捐款
Specifically refers to monetary donations. For donations of goods, use 捐赠 (juānzèng).

~
长假
Usually refers to extended holidays, longer than a typical weekend.

~
票价
Specifically refers to the price of a ticket. For other prices, use 价格 (jiàgé).

~
扣
扣 has a wide range of meanings. It's essential to pay attention to the context to discern the correct meaning.

~
起到
Always used in the structure "起到...作用" (qǐ dào...zuòyòng), meaning "to play a role" or "to have an effect."

~
聊天儿
This is casual conversation.  It's more informal than 谈话 (tánhuà), which can be a serious discussion.

~
创意
Emphasizes originality and innovation.  It's more than just a good idea; it has a novel or unconventional aspect.

~
有害
Implies potential or actual harm. It's a stronger word than just 不好 (bù hǎo), which simply means "not good."

~
下车
Specifically means getting off a vehicle.  For getting off other things, like a plane or boat, different verbs are used.

~
协议书
A formal, written agreement. It's more legally binding than just 协议 (xiéyì), which can also refer to verbal agreements.

~
用来
Specifically expresses the purpose or function of something. It emphasizes the intended use.

~
男士
A polite and formal term for "man" or "gentleman."

~
播出
Specifically for radio or television broadcasts.  For other forms of dissemination, different verbs are used.

~
球拍
Refers to racquets used in sports like tennis, badminton, or table tennis.

~
开机
开机 (kāijī) is specifically used for electronic devices. For cars and other engines, you would use 启动 (qǐdòng).

~
力
力 (lì) can also mean "physical strength".  A more common word for "power" (as in political power) is 权力 (quánlì).

~
井
井 (jǐng) is usually used to refer to water wells.  Oil wells are 油井 (yóujǐng).

~
年底
年底 (niándǐ) is a more specific term used to indicate the very end of the year, typically the last month or two.  年末 (niánmò) has a broader meaning and can refer to the later part of the year.

~
城里
城里 (chénglǐ) is usually used in contrast to the countryside, i.e. 乡下 (xiāngxia).

~
大道
大道 (dàdào) is also used metaphorically to refer to a righteous or correct path or principle.

~
测量
测量 (cèliáng) often implies a more precise and scientific measurement compared to other words like 量 (liáng).

~
老家
老家 (lǎojiā) refers specifically to one's ancestral home or the place where their family originated from, possibly generations ago.  It may not be the place where they currently live or grew up.

~
半夜
半夜 (bànyè) is more accurately translated as "the middle of the night," implying a time significantly later than simply "midnight."

~
古
古 (gǔ) can also be used as a prefix meaning "ancient" or "old".

~
播
播 (bō) can also mean "to sow seeds".

~
出租
出租 (chūzū) is used for renting out things.  For renting something *in*, you use 租 (zū).

~
两手
两手 (liǎngshǒu) can also figuratively mean "two-pronged approach" or "dual tactics".

~
当初
当初 (dāngchū) specifically refers to a point in the past that contrasts with the present situation. It emphasizes the difference between then and now.

~
别的
别的 (biéde) can also function as a pronoun meaning "other things" or "other people."

~
靠谱
靠谱 (kàopǔ) is a very colloquial term and should be avoided in formal situations.

~
英文
英文 (yīngwén) is both the English language and things written in English.

~
花费
花费 (huāfèi) is the money spent.  The action of spending money is 花 (huā).

~
脚步
脚步 (jiǎobù) can also figuratively refer to "pace" or "development," such as the footsteps of progress.

~
值
值 (zhí) can also mean "to be on duty" or "to be one's turn."

~
课本
课本 (kèběn) specifically refers to textbooks used in school. Other types of books would use different classifiers, such as 书 (shū) for general books.

~
等到
等到 (děngdào) suggests waiting until a specific event or time occurs before doing something else.  It emphasizes the anticipation and the subsequent action.

~
全家
全家 (quánjiā) can be used both as a noun (the whole family) and an adverb (with the whole family).

~
工程
工程 (gōngchéng) can refer to both the process of engineering and the resulting product or project.

~
礼拜
礼拜 (lǐbài) originally means religious service, but now colloquially refers to a week. It can also refer to Sunday.  Do not confuse this with  星期 (xīngqī) which unambiguously means "week."

~
睡眠
睡眠 (shuìmián) is a more formal way to say "sleep," and it usually refers to the process or state of sleeping.  睡觉 (shuìjiào) is the more common word.

~
走进
走进 (zǒujìn) implies entering a place by walking.  If you enter by other means (e.g., driving), you should use 进入 (jìnrù).

~
经费
经费 (jīngfèi) specifically refers to funds allocated for a particular purpose, often research or operations.

~
跳高
跳高 (tiàogāo) refers specifically to the sport of high jump. Jumping high in other contexts would use different words like 跳得很高 (tiào de hěn gāo).

~
正规
正规 (zhèngguī) means that something is compliant with official regulations or standards. 正式 (zhèngshì) refers to something official or formal, but not necessarily standards-compliant.

~
只得
只得 (zhǐdé) implies a lack of choice or a sense of resignation, similar to "have no choice but to."  It's stronger than 必须 (bìxū) or 得 (děi).

~
之一
之一 (zhīyī) is always used after a number or a demonstrative pronoun like 这 (zhè) or 那 (nà), e.g.  三个人之一 (sān ge rén zhī yī) – one of the three people.

~
佛
佛 (fó) specifically refers to the Buddha or Buddhism.  Other deities or religions would use different terms.

~
强盗
强盗 (qiángdào) refers to robbers or bandits who use force or violence.  小偷 (xiǎotōu) is used for thieves who steal stealthily.

~
日报
日报 (rìbào) is a newspaper published daily. It does not mean "daily report".

~
红酒
While technically 红酒 can refer to any red wine, in China it is typically used to refer to dry red wines.  If you want to be specific about other types of red wine, such as sweet red wines, you would need to use more specific terms.

~
治安
治安 is more about public order and safety, whereas the broader term for "law" is 法律 (fǎlǜ).  治安 is often used in contexts relating to policing, crime prevention, and maintaining social stability.

~
强势
When referring to a person's personality or attitude, 强势 describes someone assertive, forceful, or even domineering.  It can carry a slightly negative connotation, suggesting someone who is overbearing or inflexible.

~
样
样 (yàng) is a very versatile word. Be aware of the usage of 一样 (yīyàng) meaning "same".  Another common phrase is 什么样 (shénmeyàng) meaning "what kind of".  It can also be used as a suffix to mean "-like" or "-shaped," such as  "猫样 (māoyàng)" meaning "cat-like."

~
民间
民间 emphasizes a grassroots or non-official nature. It often refers to traditions, customs, or activities that originate from ordinary people rather than the government or established institutions.

~
连接
连接 suggests a physical connection or joining of two or more things, whereas 联系 (liánxì) refers to a more abstract connection, such as a relationship or communication.

~
必将
必将 implies a high degree of certainty and often carries a formal or literary tone. It's frequently used in official announcements, speeches, or written documents.

~
改装
改装 usually refers to modifications made to vehicles or equipment, often to improve performance, appearance, or functionality. It can also refer to altering clothing.

~
发炎
发炎 specifically refers to inflammation caused by infection, whereas if the inflammation is not due to infection, other terms like  炎症 (yánzhèng) might be more appropriate.

~
赌
赌 is a general term for gambling.  More specific terms exist for different types of gambling, such as  赌博 (dǔbó) for gambling in general, and specific words like 打麻将 (dǎ májiàng - playing mahjong).

~
局面
局面 usually describes a situation in terms of its overall state or the arrangement of various factors involved, often in a complex or dynamic situation.

~
书包
书包 is the standard term for a schoolbag in mainland China. In Taiwan, however, the more common term is 書包 (shūbāo), written with the traditional character for "book."

~
大门
大门 can refer to either a large entrance gate or simply the main door of a building, depending on the context.  It can also refer to a powerful or influential family.

~
得到
得到 implies obtaining something desirable or beneficial. It's often used in contexts involving achievements, acquisitions, or gaining something abstract like knowledge or recognition.

~
竞赛
竞赛 suggests a more formal and organized competition, often with established rules and procedures, whereas 比赛 (bǐsài) is a more general term for competition and can be used in both formal and informal contexts.

~
网友
网友 can refer to any internet user or an acquaintance with whom one only interacts online, akin to "online friend." However, be aware that 网友 can be used casually for any online contact and doesn't necessarily imply a strong friendship like in some Western cultures.

~
决策
决策 often refers to high-level decision-making, particularly in strategic or organizational contexts, whereas 决定 (juédìng) is a more general term for making a decision.

~
母
母 (mǔ) can refer to either the mother of humans or animals, but it can also be used in compound words for female animals or to indicate the origin or source of something (e.g., 母语 mǔyǔ "mother tongue").

~
幅度
幅度 refers to the range or extent of a change or variation, typically used with quantities, measurements, or degrees.  It emphasizes the magnitude of the difference.

~
时光
时光 refers to a period of time, often with a nostalgic or sentimental connotation, whereas 时间 (shíjiān) is a more neutral and general term for time.

~
来往
来往 describes reciprocal movement or interaction, whereas  来回 (láihuí) simply means back and forth.  来往 also commonly refers to social interactions or dealings between people.

~
落
落 has many meanings. Be aware of its specific usage when meaning "to leave out" or "be missing".  Also recognize its use in place names like "杭州" and "福州".

~
率先
率先 highlights being the first or leading the way, implying initiative and being ahead of others.  It often appears in official contexts.

~
干预
干预 implies intervening in a situation, often uninvited, to influence or change the course of events.  It can carry a negative connotation, suggesting interference or meddling.

~
外地
外地 is always relative to the speaker's location and means "anywhere outside of the place I am currently in".

~
黄
While 黄 primarily means "yellow," be aware of its slang usage to refer to pornography or sexually suggestive content.  Context is key to understanding this meaning.

~
查询
