查询 suggests a formal or official inquiry, often involving searching for information in databases or records.  It's commonly used in customer service, banking, and administrative contexts.

~
对立
对立 emphasizes a state of antagonism or opposition, often with two opposing sides or viewpoints, whereas 反对 (fǎnduì) refers to actively opposing or disagreeing with something.

~
下面
下面 can have a literal meaning of "below" or "underneath," but it can also be used figuratively to introduce a subsequent topic, statement, or performance, similar to "the following" or "next."

~
阔
阔 while usually meaning "wide" can also be used in more formal Chinese to refer to wealth.

~
顽强
顽强 emphasizes resilience and persistence in the face of adversity, often against strong opposition or difficult circumstances, suggesting a strong will to resist or overcome challenges.

~
遭到
遭到 suggests encountering something negative or unpleasant, often unexpectedly, implying that the subject is passively affected by an external force or event.

~
掏
掏 suggests removing something from a confined space, such as a pocket, bag, or hole, often using one's hand.  It implies a searching or retrieving motion.

~
早期
早期 is a relative term and its meaning depends on the specific context. It generally refers to a period near the beginning of a development, process, or historical period.

~
有事
有事 can mean both "to be busy" and "to have something the matter." The intended meaning is usually clear from the context.

~
开车
开车 literally means "to drive a car," but can also be used colloquially as a euphemism for firing someone from a job.

~
家园
家园 refers to one's home or homeland, often with a strong emotional or nostalgic connotation, emphasizing the sense of belonging and connection to a place.

~
直升机
直升机 is the standard term for "helicopter."  Remember the measure word is 架 (jià).

~
收养
收养 specifically refers to legally adopting a child, whereas  领养 (lǐngyǎng) refers to taking in a child or animal without formal legal adoption procedures.

~
看作
看作 implies considering or regarding something as something else, often involving a subjective interpretation or perspective, whereas 认为 (rènwéi) suggests believing or holding an opinion that something is true or factual.

~
出访
This word is usually used to describe visits abroad by high-ranking officials or important figures, such as heads of state, diplomats, or business leaders. It emphasizes the official or formal nature of the visit.  A more general word for visiting a foreign country, regardless of the purpose or status of the visitor, is simply 去国外 (qù guówài).

~
协助
协助 (xiézhù) and 帮助 (bāngzhù) both mean "to help" or "to assist," but there's a subtle difference. 协助 implies working together with someone else, providing support or aid in a joint effort. It often suggests a more formal or official context.  帮助 is more general and can be used in any situation where someone is providing help. It doesn't necessarily imply a joint effort.

~
学院
学院 (xuéyuàn) refers to a specialized institution within a university, such as the "college of arts and sciences" or the "college of engineering." It can also refer to a tertiary institution that offers a limited range of programs, such as a "teachers' college" or an "art college."  大学 (dàxué), on the other hand, refers to a university as a whole.

~
遭受
遭受 (zāoshòu) emphasizes the negative impact of the suffering or loss. It suggests that the person or thing has been subjected to something unpleasant or harmful.  It is usually used with negative events like disasters or misfortunes, such as 遭受损失 (zāoshòu sǔnshī) "to suffer losses," or 遭受打击 (zāoshòu dǎjī) "to suffer a blow."  A more general word for "to suffer" is 受到 (shòudào).

~
彩票
While 彩票 (cǎipiào) can refer to any type of lottery ticket, it is most commonly associated with government-run lotteries or officially sanctioned games of chance.  For informal or private lotteries, you might use 抽奖券 (chōujiǎng quàn) instead.

~
电力
电力 (diànlì) specifically refers to electric power as a resource or a utility, like electricity supply.  电 (diàn) is a more general term referring to electricity itself.  For example, we say 电力公司 (diànlì gōngsī), meaning "electric power company" or "power utility" not "electric company".

~
决不
决不 (juébù) is a strong and emphatic negation, conveying absolute certainty. It is more forceful than simply saying 不 (bù).

~
蒙 (cover, deceive, etc)
蒙 (méng) has many meanings, but they all share a common theme of covering or obscuring something. This might be physically covering something with a blanket, mentally being in a state of ignorance, or metaphorically covering up the truth through deception.

~
车站
车站 (chēzhàn) is a general term for any type of station where vehicles stop for passengers to board or disembark. It can refer to a train station, bus station, or even a subway station.  火车站 (huǒchēzhàn) specifically refers to a train station.  汽车站 (qìchēzhàn) is for bus station.

~
场面
场面 (chǎngmiàn) refers to the atmosphere, circumstances, or general situation of a particular event or scene. It can be used to describe both physical and social situations. It often emphasizes the scale, grandeur, or complexity of the situation.

~
舞台
舞台 (wǔtái) can also be used metaphorically to refer to any platform or opportunity for someone to perform or showcase their talents, not just a literal stage.  For example, one might talk about the international stage 国际舞台 (guójì wǔtái).

~
预备
预备 (yùbèi) implies making preparations in advance for something that is expected to happen in the future.  准备 (zhǔnbèi) is more general and can refer to any kind of preparation, whether for a future event or for immediate use.

~
金 (gold, etc)
金 (jīn) can be used metaphorically to represent something precious, valuable, or of high quality. For example, 金玉良言 (jīnyùliángyán) means "golden words of wisdom."

~
国歌
Remember to capitalize 国歌 (guógē) "national anthem" just like you capitalize "National Anthem" in English.

~
办 (do, etc)
办 (bàn) has a wide range of meanings related to managing, handling, or dealing with things. It's often used in combination with other verbs to create more specific meanings, such as 办理 (bànlǐ) "to handle or process," or 举办 (jǔbàn) "to hold or organize (an event)."

~
增值
增值 (zēngzhí) is most often used in a financial or economic context to describe the increase in value of an asset or investment. It is not typically used to describe increases in other kinds of value.  增加 (zēngjiā) is a more general word and has broader usage for non-financial contexts.

~
暖
暖 (nuǎn) can also be used figuratively to describe a kind or heartwarming feeling.  For example, 暖心 (nuǎnxīn) means "heartwarming."

~
冬季
冬季 (dōngjì) is the formal term for winter.  冬天 (dōngtiān) is more colloquial.

~
早已
早已 (zǎoyǐ) emphasizes that something happened much earlier than expected or anticipated.  It often carries a sense of completion or finality.

~
坐下
坐下 (zuòxià) is the action of sitting down.  坐着 (zuòzhe) describes the state of being seated.

~
分数
分数 (fēnshù) can also refer to a fraction in mathematics.

~
分成
分成 (fēnchéng) is used when dividing or separating things, including groups of people, locations, or even tasks.


~
车号
车号 (chēhào) refers to various identification numbers associated with vehicles, including license plate numbers, taxi numbers, bus numbers, and train car numbers.

~
技能
技能 (jìnéng) emphasizes practical abilities and expertise, often acquired through training or experience.  It's more specific than 能力 (nénglì) which is the more general term for ability.

~
跑
跑 (pǎo) can also be used figuratively to mean "to escape," "to flee," or "to run away from something."

~
线路
线路 (xiànlù) can also refer to communication lines or circuits, not just physical routes.

~
口袋
口袋 (kǒudài) can be used metaphorically to refer to someone's financial resources or wealth.

~
一些
一些 (yīxiē) can also be used as a softener or a hedge, making a statement less direct or absolute.

~
许可
许可 (xǔkě) suggests formal permission or authorization, often granted by an authority.  允许 (yǔnxǔ) is a more general term for permission.

~
发言人
发言人 (fāyánrén) is a formal title or designation, typically used for official representatives of organizations or government bodies.

~
见 (see, etc)
见 (jiàn) also has meanings relating to opinions or viewpoints, such as 意见 (yìjiàn) "opinion."  This is because seeing something tends to give you an opinion on it.

~
里头
里头 (lǐtóu) is more colloquial than 里面 (lǐmiàn).

~
紧密
紧密 (jǐnmì) emphasizes a close, interconnected, and often interdependent relationship.

~
人家
人家 (rénjiā) can be used as a polite way to refer to someone else or their family, especially when showing respect or deference.  It can also be used in a slightly critical or sarcastic way to imply that someone else has something that the speaker doesn't.

~
深入
深入 (shēnrù) can also be used figuratively to describe thorough research, investigation, or understanding of a subject.

~
里边
里边 (lǐbiān) is more colloquial than 里面 (lǐmiàn).

~
乌云
乌云 (wūyún) can be used metaphorically to represent impending trouble, gloom, or misfortune.

~
印
印 (yìn) also refers to the impression or mark left by a seal or stamp. It can also be used metaphorically to describe a lasting impression or influence.

~
外面
外面 (wàimiàn) can also refer to a person's outward appearance or demeanor. It can also be used metaphorically to represent the external world or society.

~
事
事 (shì) is a very general term that can encompass a wide range of meanings related to events, matters, affairs, or situations. It's often used in combination with other words to create more specific meanings.

~
时常
时常 (shí cháng) and 经常 (jīng cháng) both mean "often," but 时常 emphasizes that something happens at intervals, while 经常 emphasizes that something happens repeatedly.  Think of 时常 as "from time to time" and 经常 as "frequently."

~
奶粉
For baby formula, use 配方奶粉 (pèi fāng nǎi fěn).

~
辞典
This is a more formal and less common way of saying 词典 (cí diǎn).

~
递给
The object being handed over usually comes *before* 递给.  For example, 把书递给我 (bǎ shū dì gěi wǒ) - "Hand the book over to me."

~
毁
Be careful of the tones!  毁 (huǐ) means "destroy," while 毁 (huì) is an interjection of agreement.

~
罪恶
This is a more literary or formal word for "evil" or "sin."  In everyday conversation,  坏 (huài) or 罪行 (zuì xíng) are more common.

~
会谈
This word often refers to formal discussions or negotiations between organizations or governments.

~
一下儿
The 儿 (er) is often dropped in casual speech.  The specific meaning depends heavily on context.

~
染
When referring to catching a disease, 染上 (rǎn shàng) is commonly used.  For example, 染上感冒 (rǎn shàng gǎn mào) – to catch a cold.

~
这些
This refers to plural, tangible objects.  For intangible concepts, use 这 (zhè) + measure word + noun.

~
打雷
This usually refers to the sound of thunder, not lightning.  For the flash of lightning, use 闪电 (shǎn diàn).

~
提起
This can also mean to "carry" or "lift," often in a more metaphorical sense, such as 提起精神 (tí qǐ jīng shén) - "to raise one's spirits."

~
加以
This is quite formal and often used in written Chinese.

~
圆满
This implies a sense of completeness and perfection, often in the context of completing a task or achieving a goal.

~
厅
This can refer to a variety of rooms, depending on context.  In a government setting, it often refers to an office.  In a home, it can be a living room or dining room.

~
挺好
This is a common colloquial expression for "pretty good" or "quite good."

~
单打
Specifically refers to one-on-one matches. In doubles matches, use 双打 (shuāng dǎ).

~
田
Often used in combination with other characters to form words related to agriculture, such as 田地 (tián dì) - farmland, or 水田 (shuǐ tián) - paddy field.

~
追究
This implies a thorough investigation, often to assign responsibility or blame.

~
打牌
This can refer to playing cards or mahjong.  If you want to be specific, use 打扑克 (dǎ pū kè) for playing cards.

~
半决赛
The character 赛 (sài) itself can mean competition or match.

~
隔
This can also mean "to be separated by," either physically or metaphorically, e.g., 隔了一条河 (gé le yī tiáo hé) - separated by a river.

~
处长
This is a relatively high-ranking position in a government department or large organization.

~
相机
As an adverb, it means to act according to circumstances.  相机行事 (xiāng jī xíng shì) - to act as the circumstances allow.

~
约
This character has many meanings.  As a verb, it usually means "to make an appointment."  It can also function as an adjective meaning "approximately," e.g., 约10分钟 (yuē shí fēn zhōng) - about 10 minutes.

~
险
This can also describe terrain as steep or treacherous.

~
盒饭
This term specifically refers to a pre-packaged meal sold in a box, typically a simple and inexpensive option.

~
由此
This is a more formal way of saying "from this" or "therefore."

~
来历
This implies a detailed background or history, often with a sense of mystery or uncertainty.

~
救灾
This focuses on the act of providing relief and assistance during a disaster.

~
清理
This implies a thorough cleaning or clearing, often involving removing unwanted items.

~
面前
This can also be used figuratively, meaning "in the face of" or "in the presence of."

~
吸烟
This specifically refers to smoking tobacco.

~
平稳
This suggests a lack of significant change or fluctuation, often used to describe economic conditions or a vehicle's movement.

~
球场
The type of court or field is often specified by the sport, e.g., 篮球场 (lán qiú chǎng) - basketball court.

~
加盟
Specifically refers to joining a franchise or chain operation.

~
查出
Implies an investigation or search to discover something hidden or unknown.

~
架
As a classifier, it is used for large machinery, airplanes, etc.  It can also mean "to support something."

~
装置
This implies a complex piece of equipment or machinery.  It can also be used as a verb, meaning "to install."

~
不许
Stronger and more direct than 不要 (bú yào), implying a prohibition or rule.

~
照样
This word has a subtle difference in usage compared to its English equivalents. While it can mean "as before," "as usual," or "in the same manner," it often carries a connotation of *persistence* or *unyieldingness* in the face of obstacles or changes.  Think of it as "still" or "nevertheless" with emphasis.

~
银行卡
While this technically translates to "bank card," it almost exclusively refers to a *debit card* in everyday usage.  For credit cards, the term 信用卡 (xìnyòngkǎ) is used.

~
普及
Be mindful of the collocations. You can say 普及知识 (pǔjí zhīshi) "spread knowledge", 普及教育 (pǔjí jiàoyù) "spread education", or 普及科学 (pǔjí kēxué) "popularize science".  A less common meaning is "universal" or "ubiquitous." For example,  义务教育普及 (yìwù jiàoyù pǔjí) means "compulsory education is universal."

~
露 (lù)
This word has a very broad range of meaning. Here's a quick way to look at it:
- Showing something unintentionally: 露馅儿 (lù xiànr) - "reveal a secret," "let the cat out of the bag"
- Showing some part of your body: 露脸 (lù liǎn) - "to show one's face"
- Outdoors: 露营 (lù yíng) - "camping"
- Dew:  露水 (lùshuǐ) - "dew"

~
再说 (zàishuō)
In spoken Chinese, 再说 is frequently used as a way to politely decline something or end a conversation, similar to "Let's talk about it later" or "We'll see." It implies a reluctance to directly refuse or commit.

~
依法
This term is quite formal and appears mainly in official contexts or legal documents.  In casual conversation, it's more natural to use  根据法律 (gēnjù fǎlǜ).

~
仓库
Think of this as a large-scale storage facility, like a warehouse or depot. For smaller storage spaces, like a closet or storeroom, other terms are more appropriate (e.g., 储藏室 (chǔcángshì)).

~
氧气
No special usage notes, straightforward equivalent to "oxygen."

~
慌 (huāng)
This word expresses a panicked, flustered state of mind. It can often be intensified with 得 (de), as in 慌得不行 (huāng de bùxíng) - "extremely panicked."

~
上帝
While 上帝 can refer to any supreme being, it is most commonly associated with the Christian God. Other deities have their own specific terms.

~
正如
This word sets up a comparison or analogy. It can usually be translated as "just as," "exactly as," or "precisely as."

~
想不到
It can also mean "I never would have thought..." or "Who knew..."

~
新娘
No unusual notes.

~
采购 (cǎigòu)
This word suggests purchasing in bulk or for a company or organization, rather than personal shopping.  For everyday shopping, the more common words are 买 (mǎi) or 购物 (gòuwù).

~
柜子
No unusual notes.

~
股 (gǔ)
This is a multi-purpose word! Pay attention to the context: It can mean thigh, share (as in stocks), a strand, or even a small administrative unit.

~
难以
This word simply means "difficult to."  It's often followed by a verb, like 难以想象 (nányǐ xiǎngxiàng) - "hard to imagine."

~
手里 (shǒulǐ)
手里 emphasizes possession and control, more so than just physical location.  It's like saying "in someone's hands" figuratively.

~
绿化 (lǜhuà)
The slang meaning of "Islamization" is incredibly offensive and inappropriate in almost every context.

~
下去 (xiàqù)
下去 can express continuation of an action.  For example,  说下去 (shuō xiàqù) - "continue speaking."

~
变动 (biàndòng)
变动 implies a fluctuation or dynamic change, not just a single, static alteration.

~
超越 (chāoyuè)
No unusual notes.

~
缩小 (suōxiǎo)
No unusual notes.

~
量 (liàng)
量 has many meanings, including "measure", "estimate", and "amount". Note the difference in tone between 量衣服 and 量体温. The first means "to measure clothes" and uses the fourth tone. The second means "to take one's temperature" and uses the second tone.

~
晚安 (wǎn'ān)
Straightforward equivalent to "good night."

~
不利 (búlì)
This word describes something unfavorable or disadvantageous. It often precedes a noun or phrase, like 不利于健康 (búlì yú jiànkāng) - "harmful to health."

~
卷 (juǎn)
The character 卷 has a number of different meanings, each of which uses a different tone.  It’s especially important to understand this in spoken Chinese.

~
睡 (shuì)
睡 can mean either "to sleep" or "to lie down", so the context is very important.

~
不再 (búzài)
Make sure you don't confuse this with 再不 (zài bù) (see above).

~
全国 (quánguó)
No unusual notes.

~
池子 (chízi)
This refers to a relatively small, man-made pool or pond. For natural bodies of water, other terms like 湖 (hú) or 河 (hé) are used.

~
支撑 (zhīchēng)
This word describes both physical and metaphorical support, similar to "prop up," "sustain," or "bolster."

~
侄女 (zhínǚ)
No unusual notes.

~
作 (zuò/zuō)
The pronunciation of this character changes based on the word it appears in. For example, 作家 is pronounced zuòjiā, while 工作 is pronounced gōngzuò. It's important to memorize which words use which pronunciation.

~
混合 (hùn hé)
This can be used as an adjective or a verb, similar to "mixed" or "to mix."

~
损害 (sǔnhài)
损害 can refer to both physical damage and reputational harm.

~
多年 (duō nián)
No unusual notes.

~
中奖 (zhòngjiǎng)
This specifically means to win a prize in a lottery, raffle, or similar contest. It's not used for other kinds of victories.

~
聘请 (pìnqǐng)
聘请 implies formally hiring someone, often for a professional or specialized role. It carries more weight than simply "hiring."

~
查看 (chákàn)
This means to thoroughly inspect or investigate something. It suggests a more careful examination than just "looking over."

~
刮
When talking about wind, a useful collocation is "刮风" (guāfēng), which simply means "windy".

~
通信
Can also mean pen pal.

~
尖
The character 尖 (jiān) can be used to describe high-pitched sounds, sharp objects, or even outstanding individuals. When used with sounds, it implies a shrill or piercing quality.  For objects, it signifies a pointed or tapered shape. When referring to people, it suggests they are the best or the cream of the crop. It can also carry a negative nuance of shrillness or harshness when referring to someone’s voice.


~
一半
The measure word for 一半 (yībàn, half) is 一半儿, not 半个. Be careful not to say 半个一半, even though logically it seems correct.


~
作战
作战 (zuòzhàn) is generally used to describe battles or military operations, while 打仗 (dǎzhàng) is a more colloquial term for fighting or war in general.  作战 is more formal and strategic, often referring to planned military engagements. 打仗 is broader and can encompass any kind of fighting, from small skirmishes to large-scale wars.

~
海报
海报 (hǎibào) is similar to English "poster". It doesn't normally refer to an advertisement you might see on a billboard. For that, you would use 广告 (guǎnggào).

~
赶到
The phrase 赶到 (gǎndào) emphasizes the act of hurrying or rushing to a destination. It implies that there was a time constraint or a need to be somewhere quickly.  It suggests making an effort to arrive on time or before a deadline.

~
传输
传输 (chuánshū) refers specifically to the transmission of data, signals, or information, often in a technical context. 运输 (yùnshū), on the other hand, refers to the transportation of physical goods or people from one place to another.  It carries no suggestion that information is being conveyed.

~
全年
全年 (quánnián) means "the whole year."  It's sometimes used interchangeably with 整年 (zhěngnián), but there's a subtle difference. 全年 emphasizes the completeness or totality of the year, while 整年 highlights the year as a continuous, uninterrupted period.

~
气象
气象 (qìxiàng) can refer to meteorological phenomena, the broader study of meteorology, or the general atmosphere or ambience of a place or situation. When used in the latter sense, it's similar to the word "atmosphere" in English, encompassing the feeling or mood of a particular environment.

~
修复
修复 (xiūfù) implies restoring something to its original or near-original condition. It often involves repairing damage or decay, particularly in older or valuable items. 修理 (xiūlǐ) is a more general term for repairing or fixing something that is broken or malfunctioning. It doesn't necessarily imply restoring something to its former glory, but rather making it functional again.

~
供给
供给 (gōngjǐ) implies a sustained provision of resources or materials, often essential ones.  It carries more weight than 供应 (gōngyìng), which is more straightforward and involves making goods available without the extra nuance of continued support or necessary provision.  提供 (tígōng) is about making things accessible or presenting something to someone. It is also a more everyday way of providing something.

~
名单
名单 (míngdān) refers specifically to a list of names, often in a formal or official context. 列表 (lièbiǎo) is a more general term for any kind of list, whether it contains names, items, or other information.

~
天然气
天然气 (tiānránqì) refers specifically to natural gas as a fuel source. 煤气 (méiqì) is a different type of gas, often produced from coal, and can be used for cooking or heating. 

~
评
评 (píng) is a multi-purpose verb that can mean "to comment, review, criticize, judge, or choose." Its specific meaning depends on the context. When used with movies, books, or performances, it often means to review or critique. When used in a competition setting, it can mean to judge or evaluate.

~
值班
值班 (zhíbān) implies being on duty or working a shift, typically in a professional or official capacity. It often involves taking responsibility for a specific task or area during a designated time period.  值日 (zhírì) is similar but often used in a school setting, where students take turns performing duties like cleaning or maintaining order.

~
男孩儿
男孩儿 (nánháir) is the standard term for "boy," while 男孩子 (nánháizi) is another common variant.  There is no difference in meaning.

~
牙刷
The measure word for 牙刷 (yáshuā, toothbrush) is 把 (bǎ), which is used for objects with handles.

~
西北
西北 (xīběi) can refer to the northwest direction, the northwestern region of a specific area, or Northwest China, which encompasses several provinces like Shaanxi, Gansu, Xinjiang, etc.

~
开关
开关 (kāiguān) is a versatile word that can refer to various types of switches, including power switches, gas valves, and even the opening and closing of city gates.  It emphasizes toggling between on/off states for anything from lights to machinery.

~
总监
总监 (zǒngjiān) typically refers to a director or head of a department or organizational unit. Its specific meaning can vary depending on the context.

~
学员
学员 (xuéyuán) generally refers to someone who is undergoing training or learning, often in a structured program.  It can be used for students, trainees, or officer cadets. 学生 (xuéshēng) is a broader term for any student, regardless of the level or type of education.

~
列入
列入 (lièrù) means to include something on a list, often a formal or official one. It emphasizes the act of adding something to a pre-existing list.  加入 (jiārù) means to join or become a member of something. It is focused more on becoming part of a group or activity.

~
毒
毒 (dú) has a wide range of meanings, from literal poison or toxins to figurative uses describing something harmful, malicious, or even intense.  It can also refer to narcotics.

~
个儿
个儿 (gèr) is a colloquial term for height or size, often used in casual conversation. It emphasizes physical stature rather than the abstract concept of size.  个子 (gèzi) is another common term with essentially the same meaning, but might be considered slightly more formal.

~
行程
行程 (xíngchéng) encompasses the entire duration and route of a journey, often implying a planned itinerary. 路线 (lùxiàn) focuses more on the path taken from a starting point to a destination.

~
起点
起点 (qǐdiǎn) is most commonly used to refer to the starting point of a journey or endeavor, such as the beginning of a race or the first step in a project.  It can also refer to the beginning of something more abstract, like a relationship.  开端 (kāiduān) is another term that can mean beginning, but it tends to be used more for abstract things or events, emphasizing the initial part of a process or activity.

~
课堂
课堂 (kètáng) refers specifically to a classroom as a physical space dedicated to teaching and learning. 课 (kè) can also refer to a class, but it focuses more on the lesson itself rather than the location where it is taught.

~
游行
游行 (yóuxíng) refers to organized marches, parades, or demonstrations, often involving a group of people moving together for a specific purpose.  It carries a stronger implication of public display and collective action.  行走 (xíngzǒu) simply means to walk or move from one place to another and has no connotation of protest or celebration.

~
试图
试图 (shìtú) implies making an attempt to do something, often something challenging or ambitious.  It suggests effort and intention but doesn't guarantee success. 尝试 (chángshì) is similar, but implies trying something out, possibly multiple times.

~
结
结 (jié) has a diverse range of meanings, from bearing fruit or forming bonds to tying knots or checking out of a hotel. Its specific meaning depends heavily on the context.

~
气温
气温 (qìwēn) is the standard term for "air temperature." The measure word is 个 (gè).

~
胆小
胆小 (dǎnxiǎo) describes someone who is timid or cowardly.  It suggests a lack of courage or a tendency to be easily frightened. 害羞 (hàixiū) describes shyness or bashfulness, often related to social interactions.

~
便是
便是 (biànshi) has several meanings including "that's it",  "precisely," "exactly," "even," "if," and "just like."

~
凉
凉 (liáng) can describe a cool temperature, a refreshing feeling, or the act of letting something cool down.  It is not as extreme as 冷 (lěng), which means cold.  凉快 (liángkuai) is closer to refreshing, describing a pleasantly cool feeling.

~
沉重
沉重 (chénzhòng) can describe physical weight or a heavy emotional burden, implying seriousness or gravity.  It can describe something that is hard to bear, whether physically or emotionally.  沉 (chén) by itself also means heavy.

~
悲伤
悲伤 (bēishāng) describes a deep sense of sadness or sorrow, often associated with loss or grief.  难过 (nánguò) is a more common and less intense word for sadness or feeling bad.

~
宝
宝 (bǎo) is a versatile word that can refer to treasures, precious objects, jewels, or terms of endearment.  Its specific meaning depends on the context.

~
绝
绝 (jué) has a wide range of meanings, from "cut off" or "exhausted" to "unique," "extremely," or "absolutely."  It often intensifies the meaning of the word it modifies.  It’s important to consider the specific context to determine the intended meaning.

~
银牌
银牌 (yínpái) refers specifically to a silver medal, usually awarded as second place in a competition.  The measure word is 枚 (méi), which is often used for small, flat objects.

~
得以
得以 is used to express that something has become possible or achievable, often after overcoming difficulties or fulfilling certain conditions.  It emphasizes the enabling factor or condition that makes the action possible. Think of it as "finally able to" or "managed to."  It's often used in formal writing or official contexts.

~
认得
While 认得 means "to recognize," it is generally only used for people. For recognizing objects, use 认识.

~
解
解 has many meanings. Note that when it means "understand", it refers to a deeper understanding, like 解释 (jiěshì) or 说明 (shuōmíng). It is not typically used in the same way as 理解 (lǐjiě) or 明白 (míngbai).

~
真相
真相 is more than just a "fact."  It refers to the hidden or underlying truth, often one that has been obscured or concealed.  Think of it as "the real story" or "the truth behind something."

~
信念
信念 implies a deeply held belief or principle that guides one's actions and values.  It's stronger than just a simple belief (相信 xiāngxìn). Think of it as a "conviction."

~
调研
调研 is more formal and in-depth than just research (研究 yánjiū). It implies on-the-ground investigation and often involves fieldwork or surveys.  Think of it as "field research" or "fact-finding."

~
大奖赛
大奖赛 (dàjiǎngsài) is specifically used for Grand Prix events, particularly in motorsports, but can also be used for other competitions with a similar format.

~
总体
总体 describes the entirety of something considered as a whole, like "overall" or "in general." It is usually used with 上 (shàng), as in 总体上.

~
其
其 is a classical Chinese pronoun with multiple uses, making it somewhat tricky.  Pay attention to context! It can replace possessive pronouns (his, her, its, their), demonstrative pronouns (that, those), or even act as a personal pronoun (he, she, it, they).  Its formal tone makes it more common in written than spoken Chinese.

~
住房
住房 specifically refers to housing as a place of residence. It differs from 房屋 (fángwū), which is a more general term for buildings or houses.

~
特性
特性 describes inherent and distinguishing qualities, similar to "property" in the scientific sense. It's different from 特点 (tèdiǎn), which refers to more general characteristics or features.

~
这里
这里 and 这儿 are interchangeable. The difference is just tone.

~
前来
前来 is more formal than 来 (lái) and suggests a purposeful arrival or visit.  Think of it as "to come to" or "to arrive at."

~
出院
出院 specifically refers to being discharged from a hospital.

~
模式
模式 implies a fixed or established way of doing something, like a "model" or "pattern."  It's different from 方法 (fāngfǎ), which refers to a more general method or approach.

~
大巴
大巴 is a colloquial shortening of 大型巴士 (dàxíng bāshì), meaning "large bus."

~
外币
外币 is specifically used for currencies other than the local currency.

~
配备
配备 refers to the provision and allocation of equipment or resources, often in a systematic or organized way. It is different from 装备 (zhuāngbèi), which emphasizes being equipped or outfitted *with* something.

~
之下
之下 is commonly used after a comparison or contrast, indicating a lower position or status relative to something else. It’s similar to "under" or "below" but often figuratively.

~
忍受
忍受 implies enduring something unpleasant or difficult, suggesting a degree of suffering or tolerance. It's stronger than just "to bear" and carries a more negative connotation.

~
用不着
用不着 is more direct and colloquial than 不需要 (bù xūyào).

~
因
因 as "because" is often used in formal writing or official documents. It is almost always paired with 为 (wèi) to create 因为 (yīnwèi).

~
好似
好似 is more literary or poetic than 像 (xiàng) or 好像 (hǎoxiàng).

~
当场
当场 emphasizes the immediacy of an action or event, meaning "on the spot" or "right then and there."

~
中毒
中毒 refers specifically to being poisoned by a toxic substance.

~
美好
美好 suggests something positive, desirable, and often associated with happiness or beauty. It's a more evocative term than just "good" or "fine."

~
只不过
只不过 minimizes or downplays something, similar to "only" or "just," often to contrast with a stronger point.

~
戏 & 舞
戏 (xì) generally refers to plays or dramas performed on a stage.  舞 (wǔ) specifically refers to dancing or movements performed to music.

~
玉
玉 (yù) specifically refers to jade, a precious stone highly valued in Chinese culture.

~
常
常 can mean "often" or "frequently," but it also implies something habitual or regular.

~
进攻
进攻 is used specifically for offensive actions in sports or military contexts.

~
都市
都市 refers to a large, bustling city, often with a modern and cosmopolitan feel. It is different from just 城市 (chéngshì), which is just a generic city.

~
肯
肯 emphasizes willingness or readiness to do something. It can imply overcoming reluctance or hesitation.

~
调节
调节 refers to making adjustments to achieve balance or harmony, often in a system or process.

~
品
品 has multiple meanings. As a verb, it implies savoring or appreciating something with careful attention, often related to taste, art, or character.

~
前往
前往 is more formal than 去 (qù) and suggests a purposeful journey or visit.

~
餐馆
餐馆 specifically refers to a restaurant or eatery.

~
出场
出场 describes the act of entering a stage or arena for a performance or competition. It can also figuratively refer to someone entering a scene or situation.

~
好友
好友 implies a close or intimate friend, stronger than just 朋友 (péngyou), which is a generic term for "friend."

~
难看
This can also mean "embarrassing" or "awkward," referring to a situation rather than a physical appearance. For example, if someone makes a social blunder, you might say "场面很难看" (chǎngmiàn hěn nánkàn) - "The scene was very awkward."

~
立
When used to mean "immediately," 立 is usually combined with 即 (jí) to form 立即 (lìjí).  This is slightly more formal than 马上 (mǎshàng).

~
原有
This can imply that something *no longer* exists. For example, 原有的建筑 (yuányǒu de jiànzhù) suggests that the original buildings are no longer there.

~
海水
海水 can be used metaphorically to represent a vast and overwhelming amount of something, often troubles or difficulties.  For example, "像海水一样的问题" (xiàng hǎishuǐ yīyàng de wèntí) - "problems like a sea."

~
市民
A more formal/official term is 公民 (gōngmín), meaning "citizen." 市民 specifically refers to residents of a city or municipality.

~
运
When referring to "luck" or "fortune," 运 is often combined with other characters to form words like 运气 (yùnqi - luck) or 命运 (mìngyùn - fate/destiny).  On its own, it carries more of a sense of "flow" or "movement," often in a more abstract or philosophical context.

~
存款
存款 can also refer to the *act* of depositing money.

~
看得见
This implies not only that something is physically visible, but also that it is noticeable or perceptible.  For example, you might use it to describe subtle changes in someone's mood or behavior.

~
男朋友
While this technically means "boyfriend," in some contexts, particularly online or in informal settings, it can be used to refer to a close male friend. The context will usually make it clear whether a romantic relationship is implied.

~
食欲
Lack of appetite can be expressed as 没有食欲 (méiyǒu shíyù) or 食欲不振 (shíyù bùzhèn - loss of appetite).

~
面貌
面貌 can also refer to the appearance or character of something non-human, such as a city, a country, or a situation. For example, "城市面貌" (chéngshì miànmào) - "the appearance of the city."

~
进入
This can also have a more abstract meaning of entering a new stage or phase. For example, 进入新时代 (jìnrù xīn shídài) - "entering a new era."

~
斤
Be aware that the exact weight of a 斤 varies slightly across different regions.

~
通报
This word emphasizes the official and widespread dissemination of information, often about important events or incidents.

~
监测
This implies continuous or regular monitoring, often using technical equipment.

~
一生
This can also be used to describe something that lasts a very long time, even if not literally a lifetime. For example, "一生的朋友" (yīshēng de péngyou) - "a lifelong friend."

~
上级
Can also refer to higher-level organizations or institutions.

~
被动
This can also describe a disadvantageous position or situation. For example, 处于被动 (chǔyú bèidòng) - "to be in a passive position."

~
高峰
Can be used metaphorically to describe the highest point of an activity or trend.

~
地板
Be mindful of the measure word. 块 (kuài) is generally used for floors, e.g., 一块地板 (yī kuài dìbǎn).

~
回应
回应 can refer to a response that is a reaction to a specific event, question, or criticism. It often carries a sense of addressing or dealing with something.

~
到来
到来 often emphasizes the anticipated arrival of something significant or important, often with positive connotations.

~
景点
Remember the measure word for 景点 is 个 (gè), e.g., 三个景点 (sān gè jǐngdiǎn).

~
总部
Not just for companies, also can be used for military, political and other organizations.

~
薄弱
Can be used figuratively, referring to weaknesses in skills, knowledge, or arguments.

~
想到
想到 implies that a thought comes to mind suddenly or unexpectedly, or is the result of a mental process.

~
风光
When meaning “scenery," it usually suggests an impressive or expansive view. The meanings “to be well-regarded" or "to be well-off" are often used ironically now.

~
长久
Has more of a sense of permanence than other words for "a long time."

~
动机
Often implies a hidden or underlying reason for an action.

~
灰色
When used figuratively, it often refers to something ambiguous, morally questionable, or depressing.

~
挑
挑 can also be used metaphorically, as in 挑毛病 (tiāo máobìng) - "to find fault with; nitpick."

~
没错
Can also mean "certainly" or "definitely" when affirming something.

~
难得
This can also mean "precious" or "valuable" because of its rarity.

~
啦
This character is often used in spoken Chinese and adds a more casual and lively tone to the sentence.  It can also soften a command or suggestion.

~
怎样
Can also ask about the quality or nature of something.  For example, "这本书怎么样?" (Zhè běn shū zěnmeyàng?) - "How is this book?" (meaning "Is it good?")

~
底下
When referring to "afterwards," it's usually in a more classical or literary context.

~
截止
Pay attention to the preposition used with 截止.  It is often used with 到 (dào) to indicate "up to" or "by" a certain time or date, e.g., 截止到日期 (jiézhǐ dào rìqī).

~
织
Can also refer to organizing or constructing something complex, such as a network or a plan.

~
公交车
Short for 公共汽车 (gōnggòng qìchē), meaning "public bus."

公众
No special notes.

~
点头
Remember that 点头 can also mean "agree".

~
安
As a word on its own, 安 (ān) is rarely used, except perhaps in classical Chinese.  More common words formed with 安 include 安全 (safe), 安心 (peace of mind), 安静 (quiet).

~
街区
There is no difference between 街区 in Chinese and "neighborhood" in English.

~
代价
代价 (dài jià) is a more formal and literary way to say 价格 (jià gé, “price”). 代价 often implies a high price or significant sacrifice.  It's not usually used for the price of everyday items.

~
采用
No special notes.

~
为此
This is somewhat formal (书面).  A more colloquial way to say this would be 为了这个 (wèile zhège).

~
柱子
No special notes.

~
牢
牢 (láo) primarily refers to a cage or pen for animals. While it can metaphorically refer to a prison,  监狱 (jiānyù) is the more common and direct word for "prison".  牢 is also used to mean "firm" or "sturdy," e.g., 牢固 (láogù).

~
停车场
No special notes.

~
网球馆
No special notes.

~
蓝色
No special notes.

~
晕车
Remember that the general word for motion sickness is 晕船 (yùnchuán), with the boat radical. 晕车 is specifically motion sickness related to cars.

~
战士
No special notes.

~
练
When it means "to practice", 练 (liàn) is often followed by a skill or activity, e.g., 练钢琴 (liàn gāngqín),  练书法 (liàn shūfǎ).

~
发送
No special notes.

~
意愿
No special notes.

~
碰到
No special notes.

~
团结
No special notes.

~
天才
No special notes.

~
亲
As a noun, 亲 (qīn) can refer to relatives or parents, often with a modifier like 母亲 (mǔqīn - mother), 父亲 (fùqīn - father), or 亲戚 (qīnqi - relatives).  As an adjective, it implies closeness or intimacy. The verb form, meaning "to kiss," is less common than  吻 (wěn).

~
女孩儿
No special notes.

~
里面
No special notes.

~
特快
No special notes.

~
嘴巴
Remember that 嘴巴 (zuǐba) is more colloquial than 口 (kǒu) when referring to the mouth.

~
通用
No special notes.

~
收到
No special notes.

~
摆动
No special notes.

~
丧失
丧失 (sàngshī) is a more formal and severe word for "loss" compared to 失去 (shīqù). It often implies the loss of something important or irretrievable, such as 丧失信心 (sàngshī xìnxīn - to lose confidence) or 丧失机会 (sàngshī jīhuì - to lose an opportunity).

~
加工
No special notes.

~
为何
This is a more formal or literary way of saying 为什么 (wèishénme).

~
指示
No special notes.

~
祝愿
No special notes.

~
只顾
No special notes.

~
吃饭
No special notes.

~
饭馆
No special notes.

~
束
No special notes.

~
仅仅
No special notes.

~
乐
乐 (lè) is the more common character for "happy," especially in compound words like 快乐 (kuàilè).  It also relates to music.  Its other pronunciation, yuè, is less common and generally used in specific names or classical contexts.

~
惨
Besides meaning "miserable" or "wretched," 惨 (cǎn) can also describe something as "cruel" or "inhuman," particularly when discussing violence or suffering. It can also be used as an adverb meaning "badly," as in 惨败 (cǎnbài - a crushing defeat).

~
好事
This can be sarcastic, like saying "That's a fine thing indeed!".

~
摩擦
The meanings related to "disharmony" or "conflict" are somewhat formal (书面).  More colloquial words for these meanings are 争执 (zhēngzhí) or 冲突 (chōngtú).

~
法语
A related word is 法文 (fǎwén), which refers to the written French language.

~
吉利
Note the tone change on the second character from second tone to neutral tone.

~
刺 (cì)
The onomatopoeia "whoosh" applies specifically to the sound of an arrow flying through the air.

~
价 (jià)
The meanings "great, good, middleman, servant" are all archaic and not used in modern Chinese.

~
应 (yīng)
应 can also mean "to fulfill a promise or an obligation."  For example, one might say "他答应了我的请求，而且履行了他的承诺 (tā dāying le wǒ de qǐngqiú, érqiě lǚxíng le tā de chéngnuò)" - "He agreed to my request and fulfilled his promise."  Here, 履行 (lǚxíng) is a synonym for 应.

~
侄子
Remember that Chinese kinship terms are very specific. 侄子 only refers to the son of your brother. The son of your sister is your 外甥 (wàisheng).

~
线 (xiàn)
As a classifier, 线 is also used for things that resemble threads, such as rays of light.

~
温和
温和 can describe the weather, a person's temperament, or even political policies.

~
交费
More colloquial synonyms are 付款 (fùkuǎn) and 付钱 (fùqián).

~
美金
More formally, this is called 美元 (měiyuán).

~
下楼
The opposite of this is 上楼 (shànglóu), which means "to go upstairs".

~
考 (kǎo)
考, meaning "deceased father," is a very formal and literary term.

~
让座
This word emphasizes the politeness and respect shown by giving up one's seat.

~
演奏
演奏 is usually used for formal performances, unlike the more general term  "play," which is usually translated as 弹 (tán), 拉 (lā), or 吹 (chuī) depending on the instrument.

~
本子
Note that 本子 can also have a negative connotation, referring to a file or dossier kept on someone, especially by the police.

~
病房
A single room in a hospital is called a 单人间 (dānrénjiān).

~
路人甲
This term has become more common online and can be used humorously to refer to oneself or others as unimportant or insignificant in a given situation.

~
新兴
This word usually refers to things that are newly developing and have the potential for future growth and importance.

~
外文
Specifically refers to a *written* foreign language. 外语 (wàiyǔ) is the more general term for foreign languages.

~
报答
This implies a deeper sense of gratitude and a stronger obligation to repay than simply "returning a favor."

~
高考
In Taiwan, this refers to the high-level civil service exam.

~
如此
This is more formal than 这样 (zhèyàng) or 那样 (nàyàng).

~
于 (yú)
The myriad uses of 于 can be challenging for learners. Pay close attention to the context to determine the appropriate meaning.

~
服从
This implies complete obedience and compliance, often in a hierarchical structure like the military or workplace.

~
签字
This specifically refers to signing one's name, not just any kind of marking.

~
敲 (qiāo)
敲 can also be used figuratively, like "敲诈 (qiāozhà)" to extort or blackmail.

~
捐赠
This is more formal than just "giving" something (给 gěi). It implies a charitable donation or contribution to a worthy cause.

~
冷气 (lěngqì)
In Taiwan, this can refer to just cool air, not necessarily air conditioning.

~
轮子 (lúnzi)
The slang meaning referring to Falun Gong practitioners is derogatory and should be used with extreme caution.  It arose due to the organization's early practice of sitting in circles.

~
打击 (dǎjí)
This can refer to a physical strike, a military attack, a crackdown on illegal activity, or an emotional blow. The specific meaning depends on the context.

~
消灭
This word suggests complete eradication, often used in contexts of war, disease, or pests.

~
关上
This can also mean to "turn off" electronic devices, not just to close physical objects.

~
乘客
This refers specifically to someone riding in a vehicle or on public transport.

~
归主
This is a euphemism for dying, used primarily within Christian communities.

~
推动
This word often implies a sustained effort to promote or advance something.

~
宽阔
This can describe physical spaces or abstract concepts like a broad mind (心胸宽阔 xīnxiōng kuānkuò).

~
自我
This can be used as a prefix, similar to "self-" in English.  It also refers to one's self-awareness or self-image.

~
上台
上台 (shàngtái) can refer to both literally going onto a stage and figuratively coming into power.  Be aware of the context.  For "coming to power," a similar word is 就职 (jiùzhí), but this emphasizes the inauguration or formal assumption of office.

~
关机
关机 (guānjī) can mean to turn off a device, or, in a filmmaking context, to finish shooting.

~
南边
南边 (nánbiān) is more colloquial than 南方 (nánfāng).  南方 also implies a larger, more geographically significant area.

~
保守
保守 (bǎoshǒu) has a much wider range of meanings than just "conservative" politically. It can also mean to guard or keep something (like a secret).

~
修建
修建 (xiūjiàn) specifically refers to constructing buildings or other large structures. It wouldn't be used for making small items.  建造 (jiànzào) is a synonym, but can be used more broadly, including abstract creations.

~
不太
不太 (bù tài) softens the following adjective.  It's more like "not very" than "not too."

~
老太太
老太太 (lǎotàitai) is generally a respectful term for an elderly woman. In some dialects, however, it can be used more casually or even derogatorily.  Be mindful of your audience and region.  It can also mean "esteemed mother," particularly used when addressing someone else's mother with respect.

~
瓶
瓶 (píng) can be used as a measure word for bottles and other containers of liquids. Be aware of which liquids are typically measured with 瓶 (e.g. wine, bottled drinks) versus other measure words.

~
获取
获取 (huòqǔ) often implies acquiring something through effort or skill, rather than simply receiving it.

~
下降
下降 (xiàjiàng) is more formal than 减少 (jiǎnshǎo) or 降低 (jiàngdī) when referring to a decrease.

~
拼
拼 (pīn) can have various meanings from spelling to going all out, piecing things together and even risking one's life (拼了 pīn le). Pay close attention to context.

~
好久
好久 (hǎojiǔ) is flexible and can refer to both a long time in the past and a long time into the future.

~
脸盆
脸盆 (liǎnpén) is specifically a basin for washing one's face and hands.

~
乱象
乱象 (luànxiàng) refers to a chaotic *situation* or a state of disorder, not simply a messy appearance.

~
签名
签名 (qiānmíng) is the act of signing one’s name.  The resulting signature is called 签名 (qiānmíng) as well.

~
测
测 (cè) can range from precise measurement to mere conjecture.  The specific meaning depends on the context.

~
现有
现有 (xiànyǒu) emphasizes what is currently available or in stock, often in contrast to what might be available later.

~
题材
题材 (tícái) refers specifically to the subject matter of a creative work like a book or film.

~
灾区
灾区 (zāiqū) is specifically an area affected by a disaster.

~
回顾
回顾 (huígù) usually refers to looking back on past events, often to summarize or reflect.

~
大量
大量 (dàliàng) suggests a large quantity, often implying a surplus or abundance.

~
教师
教师 (jiàoshī) is a general term for teacher.  More specific terms exist, such as 老师 (lǎoshī), which is more common in everyday conversation.

~
高价
高价 (gāojià) refers to a high price, often implying that it's higher than it should be.

~
所长
所长 (suǒzhǎng) has two distinct meanings: one's strengths or what one is good at and head of an institute or station. Context is crucial.

~
听讲
听讲 (tīngjiǎng) emphasizes focused listening, typically in a lecture or formal setting.

~
情感
情感 (qínggǎn) is a more literary or formal word for feelings or emotions.

~
安检
安检 (ānjiǎn) is short for 安全检查 (ānquán jiǎnchá).  It's used specifically for security checks, especially in transportation contexts.

~
文艺
文艺 (wényì) encompasses both literature and art.

~
关联
关联 (guānlián) suggests a connection or relationship, often implying causality or interdependence.

~
跳远
跳远 (tiàoyuǎn) is specifically the long jump in athletics.

~
酒鬼
酒鬼 (jiǔguǐ) is a rather strong and negative term for a drunkard.  Use with caution.

~
实惠
实惠 (shíhuì) can mean both tangible benefits and economical or cheap.

~
打官司
打官司 (dǎ guānsi) refers to the process of engaging in a lawsuit, from filing to the verdict.

~
岗位
岗位 (gǎngwèi) refers to a specific job position or post within an organization.

~
评估
评估 (pínggū) emphasizes a systematic and often formal evaluation.

~
派出
派出 (pàichū) often implies sending someone with a specific mission or task.

~
增大
增大 (zēngdà) generally refers to increasing size or volume.

~
道教
道教 (dàojiào) is Taoism, the Chinese philosophical and religious tradition.

~
往后
往后 (wǎnghòu) means from now on, referring to the future.  It can also mean backward, but this is less common.

~
认出
The word 认出 (rènchū) carries a nuance of successful identification or recognition after some effort or uncertainty. It's not simply seeing something, but realizing what it is or who someone is.  Think of it as "recognizing" rather than just "seeing." A similar word is 辨认 (biànrèn), which implies more careful scrutiny or analysis to distinguish something or someone.

~
防守
防守 (fángshǒu) emphasizes protecting one's own territory or interests, often in a reactive manner. It contrasts with 进攻 (jìngōng - offense), which implies actively trying to gain an advantage.  In sports, 防守 is often used for defensive plays, while 保护 (bǎohù) is more general, meaning "to protect" or "safeguard."

~
神奇
神奇 (shénqí) describes something extraordinary, bordering on the supernatural, yet not necessarily impossible.  It implies a sense of wonder and mystery.  It differs from 神话 (shénhuà - myth), which refers to traditional stories about gods or supernatural beings.  It also differs from 不可思议 (bùkěsīyì - inconceivable), which highlights the inability to comprehend something.

~
短语
短语 (duǎnyǔ) refers specifically to a group of words that function as a single unit within a sentence, but do not form a complete sentence themselves.  It's different from 句子 (jùzi - sentence), which is a complete thought.  Think "phrase" vs. "sentence."

~
团长
团长 (tuánzhǎng) primarily refers to the leader of a military regiment. In other contexts, it can refer to the head of a delegation or, more recently, an organizer of a group buy. Be mindful of the context to avoid misunderstanding.

~
电子版
电子版 (diànzǐbǎn) specifically refers to a digital version of a document or publication. It is different from 电子邮件 (diànzǐ yóujiàn - email), which refers to an electronic mail message.

~
期望
期望 (qīwàng) implies a strong desire or hope for something to happen, often with a sense of anticipation. It's more formal and carries greater weight than 希望 (xīwàng - hope), which is more general.

~
会见
会见 (huìjiàn) suggests a formal meeting, often between people of relatively equal status, like dignitaries or officials. It carries more formality than 见面 (jiànmiàn - meet), which is more general.

~
识
识 (shí) is often used in compound words to indicate knowledge or recognition of specific things, like 辨识 (biànshí - discern, differentiate) or 常识 (chángshí - common sense). On its own, it's less commonly used than 知道 (zhīdào - to know) or 认识 (rènshi - to recognize).

~
小孩儿
小孩儿 (xiǎoháir) is a colloquial term for "child."  While 孩子 (háizi) is also common, 小孩儿 is generally more affectionate and informal.

~
挨打
挨打 (áidǎ) emphasizes the passive experience of receiving a beating, highlighting the suffering involved.  It differs from 打架 (dǎjià - to fight), which describes a mutual physical altercation.

~
愿
愿 (yuàn) often expresses a wish, hope, or desire for oneself or others.  It can also be used in the sense of "willingness," as in 心甘情愿 (xīngānqíngyuàn - wholeheartedly willing).

~
前
前 (qián) as "ago" is used with a time period *before* a specific point in the past, not from the present. For example,  "three years ago" in a story set in 2020 would be 2017, which would be expressed using 前.

~
大街
大街 (dàjiē) refers to a major street, often a wide, important thoroughfare in a city. It carries more significance than just any 街 (jiē - street).

~
月份
月份 (yuèfèn) is the word for "month," but when specifying a particular month, use the number followed by 月 (yuè), e.g., 一月 (yīyuè - January).

~
狠
狠 (hěn) primarily means "ruthless" or "cruel." While it can intensify adjectives, its primary meaning is different from 很 (hěn - very), which is solely an intensifier.

~
打发
打发 (dǎfa) has a range of meanings.  "Send someone away" is the best translation in most cases.  It has a more colloquial, less formal connotation than 派遣 (pàiqiǎn - dispatch). It can also mean "to kill time" or "to while away the time".

~
后年
后年 (hòunián) specifically means "the year after next."  Be careful not to confuse it with 明年 (míngnián - next year).

~
配套
配套 (pèitào) suggests components or elements designed to work together harmoniously or effectively.  Think "matching set" or "complete system."

~
特价
特价 (tèjià) implies a significantly reduced price, usually for a limited time. It's similar to "special offer" or "sale price."

~
前头
前头 (qiántou) can mean either the physical front or a previous point in time or a section of a text.  Context is essential to understanding its specific meaning.

~
拔
拔 (bá) denotes the action of pulling something out, often with some force.  It's different from 拿 (ná - take) or 提 (tí - carry), which are more general ways of holding or moving something.

~
构建
构建 (gòujiàn) refers to constructing something abstract, such as a theory, system, or framework. It's different from 建造 (jiànzào - build) or 建设 (jiànshè - construct), which typically refer to physical structures.

~
亏
亏 (kuī) can express several seemingly contradictory meanings. It can refer to a financial loss, but also express the idea of "fortunately" or "luckily," especially when followed by 得 (de). The context is crucial to discern its meaning.

~
焦点
焦点 (jiāodiǎn) represents the center of attention or the most important aspect of something. It's different from 中心 (zhōngxīn - center), which can be a more general or physical center.

~
配置
配置 (pèizhì) suggests the arrangement or deployment of resources or personnel to achieve a specific purpose.  It often implies strategic allocation.

~
争夺
争夺 (zhēngduó) emphasizes intense competition or struggle for something limited or desirable.  It has a more forceful connotation than 竞争 (jìngzhēng - compete), which can be more general or less intense.

~
租金
租金 (zūjīn) refers specifically to the money paid for renting something, like an apartment or a car. It's different from 费用 (fèiyòng - fee) or 价格 (jiàgé - price), which have broader meanings.

~
他们
他们 (tāmen) is the third-person plural pronoun, specifically referring to a group of males or a mixed-gender group.  Use 她 们 (tāmen) for a group of females only.

~
暴力
暴力 (bàolì) refers to physical force used to harm or intimidate others.  It's different from 力量 (lìliàng - strength) or 势力 (shìli - power), which are more general and not necessarily negative.

~
回收
回收 (huíshōu) often involves collecting something for reuse or reprocessing, such as recycling materials.  It differs from 收到 (shōudào - receive) or 收集 (shōují - collect), which are more general.

~
见到
见到 (jiàndào) emphasizes the successful act of seeing someone or something, often after searching or waiting. It's different from 看见 (kànjiàn - see), which is more general and implies simply observing something within one's field of vision.

~
铁路
铁路 (tiělù) specifically refers to railroad tracks or the railroad system itself. It's different from 火车 (huǒchē - train), which refers to the vehicle that travels on the tracks.

~
造
造 (zào) often implies creating something new or substantial, often through manufacturing or construction. It differs from 做 (zuò - do) or 制作 (zhìzuò - make), which are more general terms.

~
快活
快活 (kuàihuo) is a more traditional and somewhat literary word for happiness.  It expresses a sense of carefree joy.  快乐 (kuàilè) is more commonly used in modern spoken Chinese.

~
酸奶
酸奶 (suānnǎi) specifically refers to yogurt.  While 牛奶 (niúnǎi) means "cow's milk," 酸奶 is fermented milk.

~
对外
对外 (duìwài) specifically means "towards the outside" or "foreign," relating to interactions or policies directed towards other countries or entities.  It's different from 外面 (wàimiàn - outside), which simply refers to the external environment.

~
煤
煤 (méi) specifically refers to coal, a fossil fuel. It is not a general term for fuel.

~
好听
好听 (hǎotīng) describes something pleasant to listen to, usually referring to music or someone's voice. It differs from 悦耳 (yuè'ěr - pleasing to the ear), which is more formal and poetic.

~
一时
This word is tricky because it has two almost opposite meanings. It can mean "for a short time," but it can also mean "at the same time."  Be careful to consider the context.

~
排除
There is no difference between the use of 排除 in Chinese and "eliminate, remove, exclude" in English.

~
老年
老年 (lǎonián) refers to the later years of life.  It emphasizes the stage of life itself, not necessarily the frailty or weakness sometimes associated with aging.  A similar word, 老年人 (lǎoniánrén), refers specifically to elderly people.  And 老头 (lǎotóu, old man) and 老太太 (lǎotàitai, old woman) are informal terms for elderly individuals, but can be considered disrespectful depending on the relationship.

~
血液
There is no difference between the use of 血液 in Chinese and "blood" in English.

~
做饭
做饭 (zuòfàn) is a general term for cooking a meal. It encompasses the entire process.  If you want to be more specific, you can use 炒菜 (chǎocài) which specifically refers to stir-frying, a common Chinese cooking technique.

~
慌忙
慌忙 (huāngmáng) implies a hurried and flustered state of mind, often due to nervousness or anxiety.  A related word, 匆忙 (cōngmáng) simply means "in a hurry" without necessarily suggesting a flustered state of mind.

~
诸位
诸位 (zhūwèi) is a formal and respectful way to address a group of people. It is similar to "ladies and gentlemen."  A less formal equivalent is 大家 (dàjiā), which means "everyone."

~
虽
虽 (suī), meaning "although" or "even if," is usually paired with a conjunction like 然 (rán, nevertheless), forming 虽然…但是/可是/却… (suīrán…dànshì/kěshì/què…).  Using 虽 without 然 is grammatically correct, but less common.

~
作废
作废 (zuòfèi) means to officially invalidate something, often a document or agreement. It implies a formal process.  A related word, 取消 (qǔxiāo), means "to cancel," but can be used in a wider range of situations, both formal and informal.

~
通讯
通讯 (tōngxùn) has two main meanings. One refers to communication in a general sense, like correspondence or telecommunications. The other refers specifically to a news report or dispatch, often sent from a remote location.

~
处分
处分 (chǔfèn) primarily refers to disciplinary action, usually in a formal setting like a school or workplace.  It implies a penalty or punishment for wrongdoing.  It can also mean "to deal with" or "to handle" a matter, but this usage is less common.

~
不幸
不幸 (bùxìng) carries a sense of gravity and is usually reserved for significant misfortunes, such as accidents, serious illnesses, or death.  A less formal word for unfortunate events is 倒霉 (dǎoméi), which implies bad luck.

~
为主
以…为主 (yǐ…wéizhǔ) indicates that something is the main focus or dominant element.  It's often used to express a primary strategy, method, or characteristic.

~
体积
体积 (tǐjī) refers to the three-dimensional size or bulk of an object.  A related word, 面积 (miànjī), refers to the area of a two-dimensional surface.

~
上线
上线 (shàngxiàn) in the internet context specifically means "to go online," referring to a website, system, or application becoming available online.  上网 (shàngwǎng) means to go online in the sense of connecting to the internet.

~
货
货 (huò) can mean both "goods" and "money," particularly in slang or dialect.  In standard Mandarin, using 货 to mean "money" is less common.  货物 (huòwù) is the standard term for "goods."

~
美容
美容 (měiróng) primarily refers to cosmetic treatments and procedures aimed at improving one's appearance.  It often involves specialized services like facials, skincare, and makeup.  打扮 (dǎban) refers to the general act of dressing up and making oneself presentable.

~
请客
请客 (qǐngkè) means to treat someone to a meal or entertainment, often as a gesture of hospitality or celebration.  It implies covering the expenses for the other person.

~
典礼
典礼 (diǎnlǐ) refers to a formal ceremony, often grand and public, marking an important occasion.  A more general word for ceremony is 仪式 (yíshì).

~
排水
排水 (páishuǐ) means to drain or discharge water, typically from a system or area.  It can also refer to draining in a more metaphorical sense, like draining resources or energy.

~
间
间 (jiān) has multiple meanings and uses. As a measure word, it counts rooms or spaces between things. It can also mean "between," "among," or "within a certain time or space."

~
制订
制订 (zhìdìng) means to formulate or create a plan, policy, or regulation. It emphasizes the process of drafting and developing something new.  A related word, 规定 (guīdìng), refers to established rules or regulations.

~
依靠
依靠 (yīkào) emphasizes dependence and reliance on someone or something for support, both materially and emotionally.  A similar word, 依赖 (yīlài), often implies a stronger sense of dependence, sometimes even to the point of helplessness.

~
好学
好学 (hàoxué) describes someone who is eager to learn and enjoys studying.  It suggests a genuine interest in acquiring knowledge.

~
生活费
生活费 (shēnghuófèi) encompasses the essential expenses needed for daily living, such as food, housing, and transportation.  It refers to recurring costs.

~
摄影师
There is no difference between the use of 摄影师 in Chinese and "photographer" in English.

~
绿色
绿色 (lǜsè) can sometimes be used metaphorically to refer to environmentally friendly practices or products.

~
巴士
巴士 (bāshì) is a loanword and is generally interchangeable with 公共汽车 (gōnggòng qìchē), the more formal term for "bus."

~
模特儿
模特儿 (mótè'ér) is a loanword. The shorter form, 模特 (mótè), is more commonly used.

~
会长
会长 (huìzhǎng) is the title for the president or chairman of an organization, club, or association.  It usually refers to a leadership role within a non-profit or community group.

~
率领
率领 (shuàilǐng) implies leading a group of people, often in a formal or organized manner. It suggests guidance and command.  带领 (dàilǐng) is a more general term for leading or guiding.

~
鸭子
鸭子 (yāzi) has a slang meaning of "male prostitute," particularly in some regions.  Be mindful of the context to avoid misinterpretations.

~
扮演
扮演 (bànyǎn) emphasizes the act of portraying or impersonating a character, often in a theatrical or dramatic context.  A more general word for "to play a role" is 饰演 (shìyǎn), which can refer to both acting and fulfilling a role in real life.

~
大赛
大赛 (dàsài) refers to a large-scale competition or contest, often of national or international importance.  It implies a significant and prestigious event.  比赛 (bǐsài) is a more general term for competition.

~
近视
近视 (jìnshì) specifically refers to nearsightedness or myopia.

~
游泳池
There is no difference between the use of 游泳池 in Chinese and "swimming pool" in English.

~
兴旺
兴旺 (xīngwàng) describes a state of prosperity and flourishing, often used to describe businesses, economies, or families.  It suggests growth and success.

~
要不然
要不然 (yàoburán) is used to introduce an alternative or consequence, often implying a warning or threat. It is stronger than 否则 (fǒuzé), which simply means "otherwise."

~
大多
大多 (dàduō) means "mostly" or "for the most part."  It indicates that something applies to the majority of cases.

~
监督
监督 (jiāndū) implies oversight and monitoring to ensure compliance with rules or standards.  It suggests a more authoritative role than 观察 (guānchá), which means to observe.

~
海外
Relates words include 国外 (guówài), which is more common in spoken Chinese.  海外 is more literary.  Additionally, 海外 has a stronger connotation of being across a body of water, whether or not it's an ocean.

~
活力
A similar word is 生命力 (shēngmìnglì, vitality; viability). 活力 describes the energy of a person, a group, or an endeavor/movement.  On the other hand, 生命力 describes the inherent capacity for something to survive or thrive. It's more intrinsic.

~
灭
When referring to putting out a fire, 灭 is less common than 熄灭 (xīmiè).

~
治病
More commonly, people say 看病 (kànbìng).  治病 is more formal and implies a more long-term solution or cure.  看病 is more about dealing with symptoms, getting some medicine, etc.  If you have a cold, you go 看病. If you have cancer, you go 治病.

~
测试
A more colloquial way to say this is simply 考 (kǎo).

~
此致
This is very formal and old-fashioned.  It might appear in a very formal business letter, but it's not used very often.

~
公路
Relates words include:
* 道路 (dàolù) refers to roads in general, including both urban and rural, paved and unpaved.
* 马路 (mǎlù) refers specifically to urban, paved roads.
* 街道 (jiēdào) refers to streets within a city or town.

~
泪水
This is more formal/poetic than 眼泪 (yǎnlèi), which is much more common.

~
看出
This means to "see" in the sense of "find out" or "discover". You can 看出 the flaws in someone's argument, or 看出 that your friend is unhappy, but you can't 看出 a bird.  For that, just use 看见 (kànjiàn) or even just 看 (kàn).

~
晴天
A more generic and common word for a nice day is 好天 (hǎotiān).  This can also refer to days which are clear and crisp, but a bit cold.

~
不值
不值 can also be used in the context of something not being worth some amount of money (like the English, "not worth a dollar").  不值得 (bù zhídé) means "not worth it", and means that something is not worth one's time or effort.

~
眼里
In the sense of "within one's vision", this is more poetic/literary than using 看得见 (kàndéjiàn) or 看到 (kàndào).

~
升级
This word doesn't necessarily refer to technology or computing.  It can refer to any kind of advancement or escalation.

~
乐曲
A more general and common word is simply 音乐 (yīnyuè), which refers to music in general.  乐曲 refers to a specific musical composition or piece.

~
靠近
This can also refer to a relationship or feeling between people.  For instance, the two sentences below are both grammatically correct:
*  我靠近她。 (I got close to her, physically)
*  我跟她靠近了。(Our relationship got closer, emotionally)

~
大脑
This word has a stronger literary feel.  If you're talking to your doctor, you should probably just say "脑子" (nǎozi).

~
各地
A more colloquial equivalent is 到处 (dàochù).

~
政党
More common word is simply 党 (dǎng).

~
减轻
A related word is 减弱 (jiǎnruò).  减轻 refers specifically to making something lighter - whether it's a physical object or something more abstract like a sentence or a punishment.  减弱 refers to making something weaker, or reducing the strength/intensity of something.

~
顺
顺 has many meanings.  When it means "along" or "with", the most natural translation is usually just 沿着 (yánzhe).  When it means "obey" or "listen to", the best translation depends on the context.  It could mean 听 (tīng), 按照 (ànzhào), or something else.

~
海浪
A more straightforward synonym is simply 海波 (hǎibō).

~
最终
Ultimately 最终 means "finally", "in the end", or "ultimately". This doesn't necessarily imply "the best" or something supremely important - unlike "ultimate" in English.  If I want to describe "the ultimate vacation", the word I need is probably something like 至尊 (zhìzūn) or 终极 (zhōngjí).

~
瓜
Be careful when ordering food.  西瓜 (xīguā) means watermelon, not just any melon.

~
到期
A related phrase is 过期 (guòqī).  到期 means that something is due - it's just reached the required or planned amount of time.  过期 means that it is past due or expired.  If you're talking about something undesirable like a visa or milk, you almost always mean 过期.

~
孙女
This distinguishes a "granddaughter through one's son" from one's 外孙女 (wàisūnnǚ), or granddaughter through one's daughter.  In modern Mandarin, this distinction is increasingly uncommon.  Just 孙女 is becoming more usual.

~
是不是
In many cases, this can simply be replaced with the word "吗" (ma) at the end of the sentence.  是不是 is used when there are some special nuances that "吗" can't capture, but this is probably beyond the HSK 6 level.

~
账
Although 账 is most often used for financial accounts and debts, it can also be used figuratively, in much the same way as the English word "account".  One can keep someone's faults "on account", e.g. "I'm keeping tabs on you" or "I haven't forgotten what you did".  Here are some examples:

*  这笔账我迟早要跟你算。(zhè bǐ zhàng wǒ chízǎo yào gēn nǐ suàn, lit. Sooner or later, I'm going to settle this account with you.)
*  新仇旧恨一起算。(xīn chóu jiù hèn yīqǐ suàn, lit. Let's settle old and new accounts all together.)


~
认
认 can have other uses, like 认错 (rèncuò, to admit one is wrong) or 认输 (rènshū, to admit defeat).

~
杯
Remember that 杯 can be used as a measure word.  一杯水 (yībēishuǐ) means "a cup of water".

~
楼道
This refers specifically to a corridor or hallway, unlike 走廊 (zǒuláng) which can refer to an outdoor passageway as well.

~
针
This can also be used as a measure word, e.g. 一针 (yīzhēn), or "one injection".

~
实际上
实际上 and 事实上 are quite similar, and choosing the right one depends on nuance.  实际上 means "in practice/in reality", suggesting that the real situation may be different from what seems or what is theoretically expected.  事实 means "truth" or "fact", so 事实上 highlights something that may not be immediately evident or commonly known.

~
涨价
This is intransitive.  The price goes up on its own.  If *I* put the price up, I would use 提价 (tíjià).

~
智能
智能 is used specifically for mental/cognitive ability, especially in contexts where AI is involved.

~
游玩
A more formal equivalent is simply to use the word 游 (yóu), as in the word 旅游 (lǚyóu).

~
分组
分 is the verb that means "to divide" or "to separate".  组 is the noun that means "group".  So 分组 literally means to divide into groups.

~
放到
The most common meaning of 放到 is to emphasize the destination or location where something is put.  A different but related phrase is 放进 (fàngjìn) which is used for putting something inside or into a container, and often follows the word "把".

~
部
部 is a very general classifier and can be used for a wide variety of things. It's a good "default" classifier to use if you're not sure which one is appropriate.

~
烤肉
This also refers to grilling or BBQing.  A similar word is 烧烤 (shāokǎo).  These are mostly interchangeable, but 烧烤 is perhaps a little more general as it includes both grilling and roasting.

~
奶 (nǎi)
While 奶 can mean "breast," it's more commonly used to refer to "milk" or "dairy products."  When referring to a woman's breast, 胸部 (xiōngbù) or 乳房 (rǔfáng) are more appropriate, though less direct.  As a verb, it means "to breastfeed."  It's also a term of address for a woman's mother or a woman who provides childcare.

~
请教 (qǐngjiào)
This is a polite and humble way to ask for advice or guidance. It emphasizes the speaker's respect for the other person's knowledge or expertise.

~
打 (dǎ)
This is a highly versatile verb with a broad range of meanings. Pay attention to the context to determine the correct meaning. Its many uses make it essential for learners to master.

~
主持人 (zhǔchírén)
Refers to someone who hosts or presents a program, event, or ceremony.  It's commonly used for TV or radio presenters, event emcees, or meeting facilitators.

~
宫 (gōng)
While it can mean "palace" or "temple," in a medical context, it specifically refers to the "uterus."

~
规划 (guīhuà)
This implies a more long-term, strategic plan, often used for urban development, career paths, or large-scale projects.  It carries a more formal tone than 计划 (jìhuà), which refers to a more general plan or schedule.

~
将近 (jiāngjìn)
Similar to 差不多 (chàbuduō), but slightly more formal.  It emphasizes that something is very close to a specific number or time.

~
特 (tè)
Often used as a prefix to indicate something special, unique, or distinct. It can also mean "especially" or "very" when used as an adverb.

~
中外 (zhōngwài)
This term is a set phrase referring to both China and other countries. It’s often used in contexts discussing international relations, cultural exchange, or comparative studies.

~
节假日 (jiéjiàrì)
This refers to public holidays, including both traditional festivals and national holidays.

~
没想到 (méi xiǎngdào)
Expresses surprise or unexpectedness. Similar to "I didn't expect..." or "To my surprise..."

~
不停 (bùtíng)
Emphasizes continuous or unceasing action.  It can be used with various verbs to indicate ongoing activity.

~
特有 (tèyǒu)
Highlights something unique or specific to a particular person, place, or thing.  It emphasizes distinctiveness.

~
心疼 (xīnténg)
This primarily expresses feeling distressed or sorry for someone, often due to their hardship or suffering. It can also indicate regret or reluctance to spend money. The romantic connotation of "loving dearly" is less common.

~
年前 (nián qián)
Can be ambiguous.  Clarify whether it refers to "before the New Year" (within the current year) or "years ago."

~
答 (dá)
More formal than 回答 (huídá) and usually used in written language, especially in exams, questionnaires, or official documents.

~
以后 (yǐhòu)
Refers to a time after a specific point.  Can indicate a general future time or a time following a particular event.

~
正义 (zhèngyì)
A more formal and abstract term for "justice" or "righteousness" often used in legal, philosophical, or political contexts.

~
队长 (duìzhǎng)
This refers to the leader of a team, group, or squad, often in a sports, military, or work setting.

~
高大 (gāodà)
Describes something tall and imposing, often used for buildings, trees, or people.  Emphasizes both height and stature.

~
融合 (rónghé)
Implies a blending or merging of different elements into a harmonious whole. It's often used in cultural, artistic, or technological contexts.

~
领取 (lǐngqǔ)
Refers to receiving or collecting something officially, often involving a formal process or documentation.

~
走私 (zǒusī)
Specifically refers to the illegal import or export of goods, often to avoid customs duties or trade restrictions.

~
程度 (chéngdù)
Indicates the level, extent, or degree of something. It's often used with adjectives or adverbs to specify intensity.

~
热量 (rèliàng)
Refers to the amount of heat energy, often used in scientific or nutritional contexts. It's the equivalent of "calories" in discussions about food.

~
船只 (chuánzhī)
A more formal term for "ships" or "vessels," often used in official or technical contexts.

~
适用 (shìyòng)
Means suitable or applicable for a particular purpose or situation. It often implies practicality and effectiveness.

~
夺取 (duóqǔ)
Implies taking something by force or through struggle, emphasizing the effort or conflict involved.

~
乘 (chéng)
Besides meaning "to ride," it can also mean "to take advantage of" or "to multiply." Its multiple meanings require careful attention to context.

~
昏 (hūn)
Can refer to a loss of consciousness or a state of being muddle-headed.  It can also mean "dusk" or "twilight."

~
前进 (qiánjìn)
Emphasizes moving forward with purpose and determination, often towards a goal.

~
骑车 (qíchē)
Refers to riding a bicycle or motorcycle.  Context determines which vehicle is being used.

~
差异 (chāyì)
Indicates a noticeable difference or discrepancy between things.  It's often used in comparisons or analyses.

~
预测 (yùcè)
Implies making an educated guess or estimation about future events, often based on data or trends.

~
血管 (xuèguǎn)
Refers to blood vessels in the body, including arteries, veins, and capillaries.

~
干吗 (gànmá) or  干嘛 (gànmá)
Informal way of asking "why?" or "what are you doing?" Similar to 为什么 (wèishénme), but more colloquial.

~
工夫 (gōngfu)
Can refer to time, skill, or effort, depending on the context. It's important to discern the correct meaning based on the surrounding words.

~
医学 (yīxué)
Refers to the study and practice of medicine as a scientific field.

~
有效 (yǒuxiào)
Means something is effective, valid, or produces the desired result. It's often used for documents, medicines, or methods.

~
指责 (zhǐzé)
Implies criticizing or blaming someone, often in a strong or accusatory manner.

~
联赛
联赛 is short for 联盟赛 (liánméngsài).

~
园地
This word is more literary (书面).  A more colloquial synonym is 场地 (chǎngdì).

~
设想
This word is somewhat formal (书面).  A more colloquial synonym is 想象 (xiǎngxiàng).

~
残疾
This word is the most neutral way to refer to a disability.  A more sensitive term is 残障 (cánzhàng).

~
陆军
This word is part of a set: 陆海空三军 (lù hǎi kōng sān jūn), which refers to the army, navy, and air force.

~
照耀
This word is more literary (书面). More colloquial synonyms include:  照亮 (zhào liàng) and  照射 (zhào shè).  照耀 is more poetic and often implies warmth and positive connotations.


~
交警
This word is an abbreviation of 交通警察 (jiāotōng jǐngchá).

~
觉
The most common meaning of this word is "sleep".  The most common measure word for it is 场 (chǎng) e.g. 睡了一觉 (shuì le yī jiào).


~
双手
This refers to *both* hands *together* in most contexts, not each hand individually.

~
同行
In the sense of "peer", this word emphasizes that the other person is in the *same industry* as you.

~
收看
This is somewhat formal (书面).  More colloquial synonyms include 看 (kàn).

~
中学
The measure word for 中学 is 所 (suǒ).

~
保密
This has stronger connotations of secrecy due to national security or strategic considerations than the English word "confidential".

~
原
This word has many meanings and uses.  When it means "former", the previous position/role must follow directly after the word 原. E.g. 原校长 (yuán xiàozhǎng) means "former principal".

~
主流
This implies widespread acceptance or dominance within a field, not just what's currently popular.

~
外头
This is more colloquial than 外面 (wàimiàn).

~
隐藏
This implies something is being deliberately concealed.

~
暗示
