This implies indirect communication, but it doesn't necessarily mean the speaker has malicious intent.

~
老乡
This refers to someone who comes from the same village, town or general area as you. It creates an instant bond of familiarity and connection.

~
实施
This implies a plan or policy is being put into action, not just any activity.

~
保安
This refers specifically to a security guard, not the broader concept of safety.

~
今后
This is more formal (书面). More colloquial synonyms include 从今以后 (cóngjīn yǐhòu).


~
只
Only is the most common meaning. When it means "single" or "lonely", it often appears as a reduplicated form 只只 (zhī zhī).
As a measure word, it's common for animals but can also be used poetically for other things.


~
中等
This describes something average, in the middle of a scale, not necessarily good or bad.


~
工作日
This refers specifically to weekdays (Monday-Friday), excluding weekends and public holidays.


~
情形
This is somewhat formal (书面). More colloquial synonyms include 情况 (qíngkuàng).


~
民警
This term refers to general police officers, including patrol officers and investigators, but excluding specialized police like traffic police or armed police.


~
剑
While 剑 (jiàn) refers to a double-edged straight sword, 刀 (dāo) is a single-edged, often curved, blade.


~
剩下
This emphasizes what remains after something else has been used or taken away.


~
参展
This specifically refers to participating in an exhibition, usually to showcase products or services.


~
搞好
This emphasizes achieving a good outcome or result, often through effort and careful planning.


~
闭幕式
This is the specific term for a closing ceremony, often marking the end of a major event.


~
今年
This is straightforward in meaning, referring to the current year.


~
小组
This refers to a small group of people, usually formed for a specific task or purpose.


~
灾
This refers to a large-scale disaster or calamity, often natural but can also be man-made.


~
健全
This describes a system or organization that is complete and functioning effectively, often in terms of regulations and procedures.


~
晚报
This refers to a newspaper published in the evening, often containing the latest news.


~
首脑
This term can refer to a leader of a group, organization, or country, and is often used in formal contexts.


~
西医
This term differentiates Western medicine from traditional Chinese medicine (中医 - zhōngyī).

~
先进
When referring to technology, 先进 translates to "advanced" or "sophisticated." When referring to deeds, it translates to "meritorious" or "exemplary."

~
船长
This word can refer to the captain of any boat, not just a ship.

~
炮
This word has many meanings, including "cannon," "gun," "firecracker," "artillery piece," and various cooking methods involving heating. Be aware of the context to determine the correct meaning.

~
看待
This word emphasizes the subjective perspective or attitude one holds towards something, rather than simply observing it objectively.  It often carries the nuance of "considering" or "regarding" something in a particular way.

~
叹气
This word can imply disappointment, frustration, resignation, or weariness, depending on the context.  It often suggests a sense of helplessness or powerlessness.

~
无法
This word expresses a stronger sense of inability than 不能 (bùnéng). It implies that something is impossible or beyond one's control.

~
时事
This term refers specifically to current events of political or social significance, not just any current trend or topic.

~
列为
This phrase indicates a formal classification or categorization, often by an official body or authority.  It implies a deliberate and systematic process of assigning something to a specific category.

~
等级
This word can refer to a hierarchical level or a specific grade within a system. It often carries connotations of social status or importance.

~
明日
While this word simply means "tomorrow," it is slightly more formal than 明天 (míngtiān).

~
以往
This word usually refers to a period of time leading up to the present, rather than a specific point in the past.  It emphasizes the contrast between the past and the present.

~
食品
This word encompasses any edible substance, including prepared dishes, while 食物 (shíwù) refers to more basic food ingredients.

~
课题
This word suggests a specific area of study or research, often within an academic or scientific context.  It implies a more focused and in-depth investigation than just a general topic.

~
安置
This word implies not only placing something somewhere but also ensuring its stability and suitability within that location.  It can also refer to arranging for someone's accommodation or resettlement.

~
半天
This word has multiple meanings, including "half a day," "a long time," and "midair." Pay attention to the context to determine the correct interpretation.  When used to mean "a long time," it usually implies a sense of impatience or frustration at how long something is taking.

~
交给
This word emphasizes the transfer of responsibility or ownership that occurs when something is handed over to someone else.

~
围
This word can refer to the act of encircling, the surrounding area, or the perimeter of something.

~
打败
This phrase implies a decisive victory or overcoming significant resistance, not just winning a simple competition.

个体
This word refers to a single, distinct entity, often in contrast to a larger group or system. It emphasizes individuality and separateness.

阻碍
This word suggests a significant obstacle or impediment that hinders progress or prevents something from happening.

This term refers specifically to a faster mode of transportation, such as an express train or bus, not just any fast vehicle.

深深
This word intensifies the adjective it modifies, emphasizing the depth or profoundness of the feeling or quality.

微博
While Weibo is a specific social media platform, it can also refer to microblogging in general.

This word refers specifically to fine grains of rock, while 沙 (shā) can refer to sand in general, including coarser varieties.

This word emphasizes the reciprocal or two-way nature of an action or relationship. It means that both parties are involved equally.

This word has various meanings related to protection, preservation, and guarantee. The specific meaning depends on the context.

看病
This phrase refers specifically to seeking medical attention for an illness or injury, not just visiting a doctor for a check-up or other reasons.

倡导

领袖
This word refers to a leader who inspires and guides others, often in a political or social context.  It carries a stronger connotation of authority and influence than simply "leader."

This word has multiple meanings related to ceremonies, rituals, etiquette, and gifts. The specific meaning depends on the context.

~
阴影
This word can refer to both a literal shadow and a figurative shadow, such as the lingering effects of a negative experience. It often carries a negative connotation.

~
暂停
Often used in collocation with other words, such as 暂停营业 (zánting yíngyè) - suspend business, or 暂停服务 (zánting fúwù) - suspend service.

~
生火
Can also mean to light a fire, or to start a fire. Similar words include 点火 (diǎnhuǒ), which specifically means to ignite or light a fire, and  起火 (qǐhuǒ), which refers to a fire starting, often unexpectedly or accidentally.

~
季度
When referring to a company's financial results, you should always use 季度. When referring to the four seasons of the year, you should usually use 春夏秋冬 (chūnxiàqiūdōng). When referring to a season in sports, use the specific term for that sport's season, such as 赛季 (sàijì).

~
景象
This word often refers to a grand or impressive scene, rather than just any everyday sight. It emphasizes the visual spectacle and can evoke a sense of awe or wonder.  A more common word for simply "scene" or "sight" is 景色 (jǐngsè).

~
实验室
The measure word 间 (jiān) is typically used for rooms.

~
杰出
杰出 is a more formal and literary term than words like  优秀 (yōuxiù, excellent) or  出色 (chūsè, outstanding). It implies a higher level of achievement or distinction.

~
物价
This term usually refers to the general price level of goods and services. It is often used in discussions of inflation or deflation. A related word is 价格 (jiàgé), which means price and refers to the cost of a specific item.

~
出汗
Be aware that this word is often used in a medical or physiological context.  For everyday conversation, the word 流汗 (liúhàn) is also common.

~
时而
Often paired with 时而 to indicate alternating states or actions.  It implies a sense of irregularity or unpredictability.

~
号召
This word has a strong connotation of a public or official call to action, often by a leader or organization, motivating people towards a collective goal.  A more neutral word for "call" would be  称呼 (chēnghu), or 叫 (jiào).

~
诗人
Can also be used more broadly to refer to someone who is poetic or romantic, not necessarily a professional poet.

~
前方
Often used in formal announcements or directions.  More colloquial terms include 前面 (qiánmiàn), which refers to the space directly in front of something, or  前面儿 (qiánmiànr), a more casual way of saying "up ahead."

~
读书
Depending on context, this phrase can mean "to read," "to study," or "to attend school." Pay attention to the context to understand the intended meaning.

~
楼房
Refers to a multi-story building, typically residential.  The measure word 栋 (dòng) is most commonly used for buildings.

~
中餐
When referring to "lunch,"  午餐 (wǔcān) is the more appropriate term.  中餐 specifically refers to a Chinese-style meal.

~
加
Has a wide range of meanings. In the context of mathematics, 加 means "plus" or "to add." In other contexts, it can indicate an increase, intensification, or application of something.

~
分为
Note that the object being divided comes before 分为, and the parts into which it is divided come after.

~
刚刚
Can also be used to soften a request or refusal, similar to "just" or "slightly" in English.

~
赏
Can have a more formal or literary connotation than other words for "give" like 给 (gěi). It can also mean "to appreciate" (beauty or art), similar to 欣赏 (xīnshǎng).

~
高等
Usually used in the context of education or biology. For general comparisons of height or level,  高 (gāo) is sufficient.

~
美
Has multiple meanings. It can describe physical beauty, a pleasant experience, or refer to the Americas or the USA (美国, Měiguó).  When used as a bound morpheme in 美洲 (Měizhōu, the Americas) or 美国 (Měiguó, USA), it doesn't carry the meaning of "beautiful."

~
不满
Implies a stronger sense of dissatisfaction than simply "not satisfied" (不满意, bùmǎnyì).  It suggests a degree of resentment or displeasure.

~
逃走
Emphasizes the act of escaping or fleeing, often from a dangerous or unpleasant situation.  More general words for leaving include  离开 (líkāi) or  走 (zǒu).

~
卧铺
Refers specifically to a sleeping berth on a train.  For other types of beds, use  床 (chuáng).

~
自学
Focuses on the independent nature of the study.  学习 (xuéxí) is a more general term for "study" or "learn."

~
为期
Indicates a set duration for an event or activity.  The length of time is usually specified after 为期.

~
摆脱
Implies freeing oneself from something undesirable or burdensome, such as a bad habit, a difficult situation, or an unpleasant person.

~
扎实
Describes something solid, firm, or well-founded, often in reference to skills, knowledge, or foundations.

~
强迫
Has a stronger connotation of coercion than  逼 (bī) or  迫使 (pòshǐ).  It implies using force or pressure to make someone do something against their will.

~
头脑
Can refer to both the physical brain and the mind.  It can also mean the gist of a matter or, informally, a leader or boss.

~
仅
A more formal and literary word for "only" than  只 (zhǐ).

~
全世界
A common term for "worldwide" or "the entire world."  全球 (quánqiú) is a synonym with a similar meaning.

~
兵
Has multiple meanings related to military contexts, including soldiers, weapons, and military affairs in general.

~
急
Has several meanings, including urgent, anxious, and rapid. The specific meaning depends on context.

~
外汇
Refers specifically to foreign currency exchange.  外币 (wàibì) is a more general term for foreign currency.

~
发电
Refers specifically to generating electricity.  It can also mean to send a telegram, but this usage is less common now.

~
不成
Can be used as a rhetorical question, implying disbelief or disapproval.

~
扎
Has various meanings, including "to tie," "to prick," and as a classifier for bundles of flowers or banknotes.  It is also used in the word 挣扎 (zhēngzhá, to struggle).

~
激情
Often used in the context of strong emotions related to love, art, or revolutionary ideals.  It can also refer to general enthusiasm or fervor.

~
踢
Can also be used colloquially to describe a butch lesbian.

~
推销
The word 推销 has a slightly negative connotation in Chinese, suggesting aggressive or unwelcome sales tactics.  A more neutral term would be 促销 (cùxiāo), which refers to sales promotion in general.  For personal selling, you could use  销售 (xiāoshòu).

~
只能
Be careful of the subtle difference between 只好 (zhǐhǎo) and 只能 (zhǐ néng).  Both imply a lack of choice, but 只好 emphasizes the speaker's reluctance or resignation, while 只能 simply states the limitation.

~
求
求 is stronger and more desperate than 请 (qǐng), which is the usual word for "request."  求 implies begging or pleading.

~
定价
定价 (dìngjià) specifically refers to the act of setting a price.  标价 (biāojià) refers to the price that's marked or listed.  价格 (jiàgé) is the general term for "price."

~
不通
不通 can mean both "blocked" (physically) and "doesn't make sense."  Context is essential to distinguish the meaning.  For "blocked," you can also use 堵塞 (dǔsè), which is more formal.  For "doesn't make sense," you might also use  说不通 (shuō bù tōng) or 没道理 (méi dàolǐ).

~
一代
一代 is often used to refer to a generation of people with shared characteristics, not just a time period. For example,  "the post-90s generation" would be  90后一代 (jiǔlíng hòu yīdài).

~
大胆
大胆 can be positive (brave, daring) or negative (reckless, audacious), depending on the context.

~
戒毒
戒毒 focuses on the process of quitting drug addiction.  If you want to talk about the state of being drug-free, you'd use  脱毒 (tuōdú).

~
杆
The appropriate measure word for 杆 depends on what it refers to.  For long, thin poles, 根 (gēn) is common.  For things like flagpoles or fishing rods, 支 (zhī) can also be used.

~
打包
Besides its literal meaning of "to pack," 打包 also means "to get a doggy bag" at a restaurant.

~
下课
下课 means "class is over," not "to leave the classroom."  To express the act of leaving the classroom, you'd use  离开教室 (líkāi jiàoshì).

~
亚运会
Remember the "会 (huì)" indicates it's a gathering or meeting, in this case, the games themselves.

~
汇款
汇款 refers specifically to remitting money.  If you're talking about transferring money between accounts within the same country, you might use  转账 (zhuǎnzhàng).

~
转化
转化 implies a more significant change than simply changing form.  It often suggests a qualitative shift.

~
上边
上边 can be literal ("on top") or figurative, referring to higher-ups in a hierarchy.

~
神
神 has a broad range of meanings, from "god" to "spirit" to "expression" (in someone's eyes).  Pay attention to context.

~
山区
山区 is the general term for a mountainous area.  山地 (shāndì) specifically refers to mountainous terrain, while  山脉 (shānmài) refers to a mountain range.

~
应急
应急 implies dealing with a sudden or unexpected situation.  It's not used for routine preparedness.

~
升值
升值 applies to currencies and assets appreciating in value.  For something becoming more valuable in a non-financial sense, you might use  增值 (zēngzhí).

~
跳
跳 can be used for various jumping motions, from small hops to large leaps.  If you want to emphasize a high jump, you might use  跃 (yuè).

~
边缘
边缘 can also be used figuratively to mean "on the edge of" something, like society or a breakdown.

~
摔
摔 implies an accidental fall.  If someone is deliberately thrown down, you'd use  扔 (rēng) or 摔倒 (shuāidǎo).

~
军人
军人 is a general term for military personnel.  士兵 (shìbīng) refers specifically to soldiers.

~
拿走
拿走 emphasizes taking something away from a location.  If you're simply carrying something, you'd use  拿着 (ná zhe) or  带着 (dài zhe).

~
远方
远方 evokes a sense of distance and often has a poetic or romantic connotation.

~
负担
负担 can be both a noun ("burden") and a verb ("to bear a burden").

~
变成
变成 describes a complete transformation.  If the change is gradual or partial, you might use  变得 (biànde).

~
少年
少年 is generally used for boys.  少女 (shàonǚ) is the equivalent for girls.

~
旁
旁 emphasizes being beside or next to something.  旁边 (pángbiān) is even more specific, meaning "beside" or "next to."

~
雨水
Besides being the general term for rainwater, 雨水 also refers to a specific solar term in the traditional Chinese calendar.

~
寸
寸 is an old-fashioned unit of measurement. While you might encounter it occasionally, 公分 (gōngfēn) or 厘米 (límǐ) are more common in modern usage.

~
场合
场合 emphasizes the social setting or appropriateness of behavior in a specific context.

~
研究生
研究生 includes both master's and doctoral students.  For a master's student specifically, you'd use  硕士研究生 (shuòshì yánjiūshēng), and for a doctoral student,  博士研究生 (bóshì yánjiūshēng).

~
电饭锅
Although literally "electric rice cooker," 电饭锅 is often used generically for cooking other things in it, too.

~
就是
就是 has many uses, including "exactly," "just," "even if," and simply for emphasis. Pay close attention to context.

~
入
Besides "enter," 入 can also be a component of other words and can have specialized meanings in classical Chinese.

~
运动会
运动会 usually refers to a track and field meet.  For other types of sporting events, more specific terms might be used.

~
自在
自在 describes a state of ease and comfort, often implying freedom from constraints.

~
沿着
沿着 implies following a path or line.  If you're simply going in a certain direction, you might use  往 (wǎng) or  朝 (cháo).



~
指着

The word 指着 (zhǐzhe) can function as a preposition, meaning "pointing at" or "referring to."  It indicates the target of a pointing action or a verbal reference.  For example:

* 他指着地图说：“我们要去那里。” (Tā zhǐzhe dìtú shuō: "Wǒmen yào qù nàlǐ.") - He pointed at the map and said, "We're going there."
*  她指着我说：“就是他！” (Tā zhǐzhe wǒ shuō: "Jiùshì tā!") - She pointed at me and said, "It's him!"

指着 can also be used adverbially to describe an action done by pointing. For example:

* 他指着告诉我怎么走。(Tā zhǐzhe gàosù wǒ zěnme zǒu.) - He told me how to get there by pointing.

Be mindful of the potential for 指着 to carry a negative connotation, especially when used with a strong tone of voice. It can imply accusation or blame.


~
费

费 (fèi) has several meanings, and context is essential to determine its correct usage.

* As a noun, 费 can mean "fee," "cost," or "expense." For example, 学费 (xuéfèi) means "tuition fee," and 费用 (fèiyòng) refers to "expenses" or "costs."

* As a verb, 费 can mean "to cost," "to spend," or "to take effort."  For example, 这本书费了我很多钱 (Zhè běn shū fèile wǒ hěn duō qián) means "This book cost me a lot of money."  费力 (fèilì) means "to exert effort" or "to be strenuous."

* 费 can also mean "wasteful" or "troublesome."  For example, 费事 (fèishì) means "troublesome" or "bothersome."

The pronunciation of 费 changes depending on its meaning and usage.  As a noun, it is pronounced with the fourth tone (fèi).  As a verb or adjective, it is pronounced with the second tone (féi).  Pay close attention to the context to pronounce it correctly.



~
…极了

极了 (jí le) is used to express an extreme degree of an adjective. It's similar to adding "-est" in English (e.g., "biggest," "smallest"). It always follows the adjective it modifies.


~
获奖

获奖 (huòjiǎng) specifically refers to winning a prize or award in a competition or contest. It doesn't simply mean receiving something.


~
构造

构造 (gòuzào) is used to describe the structure or composition of something, typically complex.  It often refers to physical objects, such as buildings or machines, but can also describe abstract concepts like the structure of a theory or an organization. It emphasizes the arrangement and interrelation of parts.


~
变为

变为 (biànwéi) means "to turn into" or "to change into," but it implies a more complete and irreversible transformation than simply changing.


~
遇见

遇见 (yùjiàn) means "to meet" or "to come across" unexpectedly or by chance.  It emphasizes the unplanned nature of the encounter.  For planned meetings, you would use 见面 (jiànmiàn).


~
汇

汇 (huì) has several meanings:

* "To remit money":  汇款 (huìkuǎn) means "to remit money."
* "To converge":  河流汇入大海 (héliú huìrù dàhǎi) - The rivers converge into the sea.
* "Collection":  汇集 (huìjí) - to gather; to collect.


~
松

松 (sōng) has a range of meanings, including "loose," "slack," "to loosen," "to relax," and "pine tree." The meaning depends heavily on context.  松 can also describe food that is light and fluffy.


~
歌星

歌星 (gēxīng) refers to a famous singer, a star. It is not used for just any singer.


~
抽样

抽样 (chōuyàng) refers specifically to the process of selecting a sample from a larger population for statistical analysis.  It's not just any kind of random selection.


~
气体

气体 (qìtǐ) refers to any substance in a gaseous state. It's a general term for gas.


~
笔记

笔记 (bǐjì) can refer to both "notes" taken during a lecture or class, as well as a specific genre of Chinese literature characterized by short, concise sketches or essays.


~
正版

正版 (zhèngbǎn) means "genuine" or "legal copy," particularly in contrast to pirated copies (盗版 dào bǎn).  It's often used in the context of software, books, or movies.


~
干涉

干涉 (gānshè) carries a negative connotation, suggesting unwanted or unwarranted interference or meddling in someone else's affairs.


~
小偷儿

小偷儿 (xiǎotōur) is a colloquial term for "thief," often used for petty theft.  A more formal term is 盗贼 (dàozéi).  The "儿" (er) is a diminutive suffix, adding a slight nuance of informality.


~
外衣

外衣 (wàiyī) refers to outerwear like coats and jackets, but it can also metaphorically refer to a superficial appearance or facade.


~
在场

在场 (zàichǎng) emphasizes physical presence at a location or event.


~
开幕

开幕 (kāimù) refers to the opening of a curtain, but it's often used metaphorically to describe the beginning of an event, like a ceremony or conference.


~
为难

为难 (wéinán) describes a feeling of awkwardness, embarrassment, or difficulty. It can be both transitive and intransitive.  It can mean "to make things difficult for someone" or "to feel embarrassed."


~
相应

相应 (xiāngyīng) emphasizes a reciprocal relationship or correspondence between two things.  It implies that one thing is done in response to or in accordance with another.


~
清醒

清醒 (qīngxǐng) means "clear-headed" or "sober," both literally (not intoxicated) and figuratively (mentally alert).


~
散

散 (sàn) has a wide range of meanings related to dispersion or separation. It can mean to disperse, scatter, break up, or distribute. It can also describe something as loose, scattered, or leisurely.  The specific meaning depends on the context.


~
道

道 (dào) has numerous meanings, including "road," "way," "path," "method," "skill," "principle," and "Tao" (in Taoism).  Pay close attention to the context to determine the correct meaning.  It also serves as a classifier for long, thin things.


~
基地

基地 (jīdì) refers to a base of operations, often military or industrial, but can also refer to a center for specific activities, like a research base.


~
袖珍

袖珍 (xiùzhēn) specifically means "pocket-sized," emphasizing smallness and portability.


~
当作

当作 (dàngzuò) means "to regard as" or "to treat as."  It implies a conscious decision to view something in a particular way.


~
表

表 (biǎo) has many meanings: "watch," "exterior surface," "table" (chart), "form," "meter," and "to express."  Context is crucial for understanding its intended meaning.


~
套餐

套餐 (tàocān) refers to a set meal, a combination of dishes offered at a fixed price. It's also used for bundled services or products.


~
担忧

担忧 (dānyōu) expresses worry or anxiety about something, often something in the future.


~
途径

途径 (tú jìng) means a way or path of achieving something. The word emphasizes methods and ways of passage. It suggests not only the path itself, but also the process of going through the path and taking action.


~
她们

她们 (tāmen) is the pronoun for "they" or "them," specifically referring to multiple females.


~
停留

停留 (tíngliú) implies a temporary stay or pause in a journey.


~
统计

统计 (tǒngjì) refers to the collection, analysis, interpretation, presentation, and organization of data.  It encompasses the entire field of statistics.


~
童话

童话 (tónghuà) specifically refers to fairy tales or children's stories with fantastical elements.


~
去掉

去掉 (qùdiào) means to remove or eliminate something unwanted or unnecessary.


~
往年

往年 (wǎngnián) refers to previous years or past years in general.


~
栏目

栏目 (lánmù) refers to a specific section or column in a newspaper, magazine, or website, or a regular segment on a radio or television program.


~
畅通

畅通 (chàngtōng) describes something that is unimpeded, free-flowing, or easily accessible. It can refer to smooth traffic flow, clear communication, or an unobstructed path.


~
园

园 (yuán) generally refers to a garden, park, or other enclosed area used for cultivation or recreation. It often appears as part of compound words for specific types of gardens or parks, like botanical gardens (植物园 zhíwùyuán) or kindergartens (幼儿园 yòuéryuán).

~
酒
Although 酒 can refer to any alcoholic beverage, it most commonly refers to strong alcohol like hard liquor.  If you want to specify wine (especially from grapes), use 葡萄酒 (pútáojiǔ).  For beer, use 啤酒 (píjiǔ).

~
有局限
This phrase is more natural when used with a subject.  For example, "This method has limitations" would be  这个方法有局限 (zhège fāngfǎ yǒu júxiàn).  You can also say "limited" with the word 有限 (yǒuxiàn).

~
太空
While 太空 technically can refer to any empty space, it overwhelmingly refers to outer space.  For other empty spaces, use 空地 (kōngdì) or 空房间 (kōng fángjiān).

~
整天
This word carries a slightly negative connotation, suggesting boredom, inactivity, or excessive engagement in a single activity.  It's like saying "all day long" in a slightly exasperated tone.  For a neutral "all day," use 一整天 (yī zhěng tiān).

~
集团
While 集团 can refer to any group, it's primarily used for large corporations or conglomerates.  For smaller, less formal groups, use 小组 (xiǎozǔ) or 团体 (tuántǐ).

~
污水
污水 specifically refers to wastewater or sewage.  For generally dirty or polluted water, use 脏水 (zāngshuǐ).

~
一块儿
While 一块儿 can mean "one piece" or a unit of currency, its most common meaning is "together."  It's similar to 一起 (yīqǐ), but slightly more colloquial.

~
部长
部长 can translate to various titles depending on context.  In government, it means "minister." In a company, it usually translates to "department head."

~
志愿
As a noun, 志愿 emphasizes a long-term aspiration or ambition.  As a verb, it means to volunteer.  For a simple "wish," use  愿望 (yuànwàng).

~
球
球 has multiple meanings, including "ball," "sphere," and even "ball game/match." Pay attention to the context to determine the correct meaning. The classifiers also change according to meaning.

~
车牌
车牌 specifically refers to a license plate for vehicles. Don't confuse it with 牌子 (páizi), which means "sign" or "brand."

~
电影院
While both 家 (jiā) and 座 (zuò) can be classifiers for 电影院, 家 is more common. 座 is generally used for larger, more impressive cinemas.

~
保卫
保卫 emphasizes defending something against attack or harm.  It's a more active defense than  保护 (bǎohù), which implies protection in a broader sense.

~
转向
转向 primarily refers to changing physical direction.  For changing a topic or opinion, use  转变 (zhuǎnbiàn).

~
乐趣
乐趣 suggests a deeper, more lasting pleasure than  快乐 (kuàilè), which is more about happiness or enjoyment in the moment.

~
艺人
艺人 has a broader meaning than just "actor." It encompasses various performing artists, including singers, dancers, and comedians.  For actors specifically, you can use  演员 (yǎnyuán).

~
不久
不久 emphasizes the shortness of the time period. It means "soon" or "not long after." Don't confuse it with 不久前 (bùjiǔ qián), which means "not long ago."

~
百分点
百分点 is specifically "percentage point," not just "percent" (百分之百).  It's used to express changes or differences in percentages.

~
眼
眼 can have several figurative meanings, including "small hole" and the "crux" of a matter. Pay attention to the context.

~
钻
钻 has many meanings, both literal (to drill, bore) and figurative (to delve into a subject, curry favor). Be mindful of the context.

~
生成
生成 suggests a natural process of formation or creation.  It differs from  制造 (zhìzào), which implies making something through human effort.

~
职位
职位 is a formal word for "position" or "post," often used in professional contexts.  For a more general term for "job," use  工作 (gōngzuò).

~
绿茶
Be aware of the slang meaning of 绿茶, referring to a seemingly innocent but manipulative girl. This usage is common online.

~
进来
进来 is specifically "come in."  For other directions of motion (e.g., "go in"), use  进去 (jìnqù).

~
弹
弹 has a wide range of meanings, including playing stringed instruments, flicking something, and even accusing someone. Pay attention to the context.

~
终止
终止 is a more formal word for "to stop" or "to terminate."  For more common usage, use  停止 (tíngzhǐ).

~
罢工
罢工 refers specifically to a labor strike.  For a general work stoppage, use  停工 (tínggōng).

~
集
集 has many meanings, including gathering, collection, and even "episode" (of a TV show).  The context is crucial for understanding its meaning.

~
糟
糟 carries a strong negative connotation, suggesting something is messy, ruined, or in a bad state.

~
工艺
工艺 refers to the techniques and skills involved in crafting or manufacturing something, especially traditional arts and crafts. It's not a general term for "technology."

~
接到
接到 emphasizes the act of receiving something, often a physical object or a communication.  For simply "to receive," use  收到 (shōudào).

~
峰会
峰会 specifically refers to a high-level meeting, often between heads of state or international organizations.

~
执行
执行 emphasizes putting a plan or decision into action, often in a formal or official context.  For a more general "to do" or "to carry out," use  做 (zuò).

~
那儿
那儿 is a more colloquial way to say "there."  In formal writing,  那里 (nàlǐ) is preferred.

~
小学
小学 refers to elementary school.  Don't confuse it with  中学 (zhōngxué), which means middle school and high school.

~
同一
同一 emphasizes complete sameness or identity.  For a more general "same," use  一样 (yīyàng) or  相同 (xiāngtóng).

~
脸色
脸色 refers to facial expression and complexion. It can indicate someone's mood or health.

~
阴谋
阴谋 carries a strong negative connotation, suggesting a secret and malicious plot.  It's not simply a "plan."

~
此后
此后 is a more formal way to say "after that" or "hereafter."  In casual conversation,  以后 (yǐhòu) is more common.

~
融入
This word emphasizes a gradual process of integration or assimilation. It implies becoming an accepted and harmonious part of something larger. It often describes cultural assimilation or the blending of different groups.

~
前边
前边 (qiánbian) means "in front of" or "ahead." It refers to the space or position before something or someone.  Note that 前面 (qiánmiàn) has the same meaning and is more commonly used.  There's no significant difference, but 前边 sounds slightly more colloquial.

~
委托
委托 (wěituō) emphasizes the act of entrusting a task or responsibility to someone. It often implies a formal or official arrangement.  It's a more formal word than 交给 (jiāogěi), and often implies a more significant or complex task than 交给.

~
犯规
犯规 (fànguī) is commonly used in sports contexts to describe a violation of the rules. It carries a sense of wrongdoing or illegality.

~
手段
手段 (shǒuduàn) can refer to both positive and negative methods. It can be a neutral term for "method," but it often carries a negative connotation of trickery or manipulation, especially when used without further qualification.

~
种植
种植 (zhòngzhí) usually refers to planting crops or cultivating land for agricultural purposes.  It implies a larger scale or more systematic approach than just "planting" something small.

~
过来
过来 (guòlái) implies movement towards the speaker or a designated point. It can also mean "to recover" (from illness or a difficult situation). Finally, when used after a verb, it indicates successful completion or mastery of a task:  e.g., 想过来 (xiǎng guòlái) - to figure something out;  做过来 (zuò guòlái) - to have done something before.

~
雨
It's useful to know the following measure words for 雨:
* 阵雨 (zhènyǔ): shower
* 一场雨 (yī cháng yǔ): a rain event

~
大伙儿
大伙儿 (dàhuǒ'er) is a colloquial term for "everybody."  It is similar to  大家 (dàjiā), but 大伙儿 has a warmer and more informal feel, suggesting a closer relationship among the group.

~
协议
协议 (xiéyì) implies a formal written agreement between parties, often involving legal or official matters.  It's a more formal and legally binding term than simple agreements.

~
春季
春季 (chūnjì) is a more formal and literary term for "spring" than 春天 (chūntiān), which is more colloquial.

~
走过
走过 (zǒuguò) emphasizes the act of passing by or traversing a location. It often implies a more intentional or purposeful movement than just walking past something incidentally.

~
缺陷
缺陷 (quēxiàn) refers to an imperfection, fault, or shortcoming in something. It implies a more significant problem than a minor flaw.  It can refer to deficiencies in physical things, abstract concepts like character, or even economic structures.

~
影迷
影迷 (yǐngmí) is a more dedicated and enthusiastic fan than just someone who likes movies.  It implies a deeper passion and engagement with cinema.

~
专辑
专辑 (zhuānjí) is often used in the music industry.  It carries the connotation of "album", a collection of musical recordings usually sold as a single item.

~
色
色 (sè) can mean color, but also has many other meanings which are not directly related.  It means sexual desire (好色, lustful).  It can mean facial expression (脸色，complexion). It can also be used to mean "quality" or "grade", as in 上色 or 下色.

~
当天
当天 (dāngtiān) specifically emphasizes that something happened on the same day as another event. It stresses the immediacy or simultaneity of the action.

~
拨打
拨打 (bōdǎ) is specifically used for making phone calls.  It is more specific than 打电话 (dǎ diànhuà), emphasizing the act of dialing a number, and thus is usually only used with phone numbers and rarely with names.

~
消毒
消毒 (xiāodú) means to disinfect and sterilize, primarily using chemicals. It implies the elimination of bacteria and other harmful microorganisms.

~
声明
声明 (shēngmíng) is a formal public statement, often issued to clarify or announce something officially. It carries more weight than a casual remark or an informal explanation.

~
夺剑
夺剑 (duójiàn) can be a literal act of seizing a sword, but it can also be used metaphorically to represent seizing power or control from someone.

~
东部
东部 (dōngbù) can refer to a general eastern area, or to the Eastern part of a specific region. The context will usually determine the reference and extent.

~
马路
马路 (mǎlù) generally refers to larger streets or roads designed for vehicle traffic, particularly in urban areas. It can encompass wider avenues but not typically small lanes or alleyways.

~
特地
特地 (tèdì) implies going out of one's way to do something.  It emphasizes the deliberate and intentional nature of an action, often taken for a specific reason.

~
考场
考场 (kǎochǎng) is not just any room where an exam might be held.  It refers specifically to a designated examination hall or room within a larger testing center.

~
对付
对付 (duìfu) implies handling a situation or person in a makeshift or less-than-ideal way. It often suggests dealing with something difficult or unpleasant, managing it with a temporary measure or compromise.

~
低于
低于 (dīyú) compares two things based on quantity or value. It indicates that one is less than the other in a measurable way.

~
长处
长处 (chángchù) focuses on inherent abilities or skills that someone excels in.  It refers to natural talents or strengths.

~
过度
过度 (guòdù) implies exceeding a reasonable or healthy limit. It suggests something being done to an excessive or extreme degree, often with negative consequences.

~
波动
波动 (bōdòng) implies a fluctuation of rise and fall.  It refers to variability or instability, as well as a wavelike or undulating motion.

~
全力
全力 (quánlì) means exerting all of one's strength or effort into achieving something. It indicates complete dedication and commitment to a task.

~
右
右 (yòu) is frequently used in directional terms like 右边 (yòubian), 右手 (yòushǒu), 向右 (xiàng yòu).

~
招呼
招呼 (zhāohu) has a broader meaning beyond simply greeting.  It includes gestures, calls, or other signals to attract attention, as well as taking care of someone's needs.

~
日语
日语 (rìyǔ) can refer to both the spoken and written forms of the Japanese language.

~
得出
得出 (déchū) implies arriving at a conclusion or result after a process of reasoning or calculation.  It suggests a logical deduction.

~
讲话
讲话 (jiǎnghuà) can refer to both formal speeches and informal conversations. It covers a broader range than just making a speech.

~
识字
识字 (shízì) means to recognize characters.  This is different from 认字 (rènzì), which implies a deeper understanding and ability to use those characters.

~
资本
资本 (zīběn) generally refers to financial capital.  It's often used in business and economic contexts to describe assets used for investment and production.

~
小朋友
小朋友 is specifically used to refer to young children, typically under the age of 10.  While 孩子 can also mean "child," it's a more general term and can refer to older children as well. 小朋友 carries a more affectionate and diminutive connotation.

~
领先
领先 implies being ahead of others in a competition, ranking, or progress.  It emphasizes the act of leading or being in the forefront.  This is different from simply being "in front" spatially.

~
面对面
While 面对面 literally translates to "face to face," it can also be used metaphorically to describe direct, personal interaction or confrontation, as in "a face-to-face meeting" or "a face-to-face conversation."

~
太阳能
This term specifically refers to energy derived from the sun.  It's distinct from other forms of renewable energy.

~
车上
车上 can refer to being *on* a vehicle as well as *in* a vehicle.  Context is usually enough to resolve this ambiguity.

~
秋季
秋季 is a more formal term for "autumn" than 秋天.

~
扑
扑 has diverse meanings.  Pay attention to the specific context to determine whether it refers to a physical action like pouncing or flapping, or a more abstract action like devoting oneself to something.

~
酷
酷 is borrowed from English "cool" and retains its slang meanings of fashionable, stylish, or impressive.  It's important to distinguish this from its other meanings related to cruelty or harshness.

~
动员
动员 carries a sense of rallying or mobilizing people for a specific cause or task.  It often implies a collective effort.

~
清洁工
清洁工 is a more formal and respectful term than some other words for "cleaner" or "garbage collector."

~
商场 and 店
商场 refers to a large shopping complex or mall, while 店 is a more general term for a shop or store.  A 商场 contains many 店.

~
皮包
皮包 specifically refers to bags made of leather or imitation leather.

~
可乐
可乐 can refer to any cola-flavored beverage, not just Coca-Cola.

~
不够
不够 can be used for both tangible things like "not enough money" and intangible things like "not good enough."

~
旋转
旋转 emphasizes circular motion around an axis, as opposed to other types of movement.

~
据
据, when used to mean "according to," often suggests a source of information that might not be entirely confirmed.  It carries less certainty than 根据.

~
直线
直线 can also be used figuratively to describe a sharp increase or decrease, as in "a straight line upward."

~
多方面
多方面 emphasizes the various angles or perspectives of a situation or issue.

~
伙
伙 can be used as a classifier for groups of people, especially those working together.

~
喷
The slang usage of 喷, meaning "to criticize scathingly online," is becoming increasingly common.

~
增多
增多 emphasizes an increase in quantity or number, while other words for "increase" might refer to size, intensity, etc.

~
调料
调料 specifically refers to seasonings and spices added to food, not other ingredients.

~
岁月
岁月 refers to a period of time, often with a nostalgic or reflective connotation.

~
部位
部位 typically refers to a specific part of the body, a plant, or an object, highlighting its distinct function or location.

~
政权
政权 refers specifically to political power or a ruling regime.

~
快要
快要 indicates an action that is about to happen imminently.

~
留下
留下 can mean both "to stay behind" and "to leave something behind."  Context is crucial for understanding the intended meaning.

~
以内
以内 means "within" or "less than" a specified limit. It is inclusive of the limit.

~
眼光
眼光 can also mean "foresight" or "vision," referring to one's ability to anticipate future trends or judge situations accurately.

~
带领
带领 emphasizes guiding and leading a group of people.

~
人数
人数 specifically refers to the number of people.

~
收听
收听 is specifically used for listening to radio broadcasts.

~
出名
出名 can mean both "to become famous" and "to be famous."

~
歌词
歌词 refers specifically to the words of a song.

~
敢于
敢于 emphasizes boldness and courage in taking action.

~
旅店
旅店 is a more general term for a place to stay while traveling, often smaller and less luxurious than a hotel (宾馆).

~
动摇
动摇 can refer to both physical shaking and wavering in one's beliefs or resolve.

~
远离
远离 emphasizes maintaining a distance, both physically and emotionally.

~
更新
更新 implies replacing something old with something new and improved, often in the context of technology or information.

~
对应
This word can also mean "to deal with" in certain contexts, particularly when talking about customer service or technical support.  For example, the phrase "专门对应客户投诉" (zhuānmén duìyìng kèhù tóusù) means "specifically responsible for dealing with customer complaints."

~
歌曲
While 歌曲 is a general term for "song," it often refers to more formal or artistic songs.  For everyday popular music, you might hear people use 流行歌曲 (liúxíng gēqǔ) - "popular song" - or simply 歌 (gē).

~
便利
便利 as an adjective means "convenient." As a verb, it means "to facilitate" or "to make convenient." Note that when used as a verb, it's usually used with a direct object. For example, "这趟火车便利了旅客的出行" (zhè tàng huǒchē biànlì le lǚkè de chūxíng) means "This train facilitated the passengers' travel."

~
西边
Note the difference between 西边 (xībian) and 西方 (xīfāng).  西边 refers to the west side or western part of a specific area or location. 西方 is a more general term, referring to "the West" as a geographical or cultural concept (similar to "Western countries").

~
必修
Often paired with 选修 (xuǎnxiū) - "elective."

~
迟
迟 also carries the connotation of "slow to react" or "slow-witted."

~
四周
Can also refer to the four weeks of a month. Context will usually make this clear.

~
用户
This word specifically refers to users of a service, system, or product, especially in a technical or online context.  For a more general word for "customer," use 顾客 (gùkè).

~
发动
Has a broader meaning than just "to start" an engine. It can also mean "to launch" an initiative, "to unleash" a force, "to mobilize" people, or "to arouse" emotions. For example, 发动战争 (fādòng zhànzhēng) means "to launch a war".

~
盒
Measure word for boxes.  For example, 一盒饼干 (yī hé bǐnggān) - "one box of biscuits."

~
提出
Be aware of the many meanings of this word. When followed by a physical object, it means "to take out" or "to withdraw."  For example,  从银行提出钱 (cóng yínháng tíchū qián) - "to withdraw money from the bank".

~
指头
While generally referring to fingers, 指头 can also refer to toes.  If you need to be specific, use 手指 (shǒuzhǐ) for fingers and 脚趾 (jiǎozhǐ) for toes.

~
一带
Used to indicate an approximate area or region.  For example, "长江一带" (Chángjiāng yīdài) - "the Yangtze River area/region."

~
品牌
Be mindful of the tone; it's often mispronounced.

~
请坐
A polite way to invite someone to sit down. In casual situations, simply saying 坐 (zuò) is sufficient.

~
原告
The opposite of 被告 (bèigào) - defendant.

~
端
This word has multiple meanings, including the "end" or "extremity" of something, a "port" in computing, and to "carry" something level with both hands. Pay attention to context.

~
多样
多样 (duōyàng) emphasizes variety within a single category, whereas 多种多样 (duō zhǒng duō yàng) emphasizes variety across multiple categories.

~
东边
Note the difference between 东边 (dōngbian) and 东方 (dōngfāng).  东边 refers to the east side or eastern part of a specific area or location. 东方 is a more general term, referring to "the East" as a geographical or cultural concept.

~
小型
Note the differences between 小型，小，and 微型. 小型 just means “small-sized” or “small-scale,” and is the most neutral of the three options. 小 is more subjective and just means “small” generally, e.g. 小房子 (xiǎo fángzi) just means “small house,” and has a certain subjectivity to it. 微型 (wēixíng) emphasizes how small something is.

~
全球
全球 is often used interchangeably with 全世界 (quánshìjiè), but 全世界 is slightly more colloquial.

~
踏实
Aside from meaning steady, steadfast and free of anxiety, this word can also mean "down-to-earth."

~
大学
Remember that 大学 also refers to one of the Four Books of Confucianism. The context should make it clear which meaning is intended.

~
午饭
Can be used interchangeably with 中饭 (zhōngfàn).

~
很难说
This phrase implies uncertainty and the possibility of different outcomes.

~
公正
Implies fairness and impartiality, especially in legal or official contexts.

~
跟前
Can also imply closeness or intimacy, especially in relationships.

~
胆
Has both a literal and figurative meaning (courage/gall vs. gallbladder).

~
不在乎
Can also imply indifference or a lack of concern.

~
搭档
Usually implies a close working relationship or partnership.

~
定然
More emphatic than 一定 (yīdìng) or 必然 (bìrán).

~
做法
Can refer to a specific method or recipe, especially in cooking.

~
残疾人
Use this term respectfully; avoid using terms like 残废 (cánfèi) which are considered offensive.

~
计算机
计算机 is a more formal and technical term than 电脑 (diànnǎo).

~
用得着
Implies necessity or usefulness.  Often used in questions to inquire about the need for something.

~
刷子
Measure word is 把 (bǎ).

~
网页
Measure word is 个 (gè).

~
医药
Encompasses both medicine and medical treatment.

~
体检
Short for 体格检查 (tǐgé jiǎncház).

~
认定
Implies a firm belief or judgment based on evidence or reasoning.

~
牌 (pái)
Can be used as a quantifier for certain objects like tablets, signs, and medals.  Note the specific measure words used: 片 (piàn), 个 (gè), 块 (kuài).

~
雄伟 (xióngwěi)
Often used to describe architecture, mountains, or other large structures, emphasizing their grandeur and magnificence.  It carries a stronger connotation than just "big."  Think "awe-inspiring."

~
华语 (huáyǔ)
More formal term for "Chinese language" compared to 中文 (zhōngwén).  Often used in official contexts or when discussing the Chinese language as a subject of study.

~
日夜 (rìyè)
Implies continuous activity without rest.  Similar to "around the clock."

~
短片 (duǎnpiàn)
Specifically refers to short films or video clips, not just any short piece of writing.

~
悬 (xuán)
Has a wide range of meanings. Pay attention to context.  The anxiety meaning often implies a sense of uncertainty or something unresolved.

~
加热 (jiārè)
Specifically means to apply heat to something, usually with the intention of raising its temperature.

~
扩展 (kuòzhǎn)
Implies an increase in scope, range, or influence, often referring to abstract concepts like knowledge, business, or territory.

~
区域 (qūyù)
Refers to a specific geographic area, often with defined boundaries or characteristics.

~
排名 (páimíng)
Refers to the act of assigning ranks or the resulting order itself.

~
毛笔 (máobǐ)
Specifically refers to traditional Chinese writing brushes.

~
投 (tóu)
Has many meanings, so pay attention to context. The meaning shifts depending on the following verb or noun.

~
圆珠笔 (yuánzhūbǐ)
Specifically refers to ballpoint pens.

~
操作 (cāozuò)
Often refers to the process of operating machinery or equipment, or performing a specific task or procedure.

~
后头 (hòutou)
More colloquial than 后面 (hòumian). Often used in spoken Mandarin.

~
采纳 (cǎinà)
Implies formally accepting a suggestion, proposal, or opinion. More formal than 接受 (jiēshòu).

~
午睡 (wǔshuì)
Specifically refers to a nap taken during the afternoon or midday.

~
发病 (fābìng)
Refers to the onset or occurrence of an illness.  Focuses on the beginning of the sickness.

~
有人 (yǒurén)
Can mean both "someone" and "there's someone/people present," depending on the context.

~
增长 (zēngzhǎng)
Refers to an increase in quantity, size, or degree. Often used for statistics or measurable growth.

~
邮票 (yóupiào)
Specifically refers to postage stamps.

~
级 (jí)
Used as a classifier for levels, ranks, or grades in a hierarchical system.

~
英勇 (yīngyǒng)
Describes bravery and courage, often in the face of danger or adversity.

~
冒 (mào)
Has a wide range of meanings, so context is crucial. Pay attention to the verb or noun that follows.

~
忽略 (hūlüè)
Implies unintentional disregard or oversight, whereas 忽视 (hūshì) suggests intentional disregard.

~
上衣 (shàngyī)
Refers to jackets, coats, shirts, or other garments worn on the upper body.

~
放下 (fàngxià)
Can have both literal and figurative meanings, such as putting down an object or letting go of a feeling or burden.

~
夺 (duó)
Often implies taking something by force or through competition.

~
四处 (sìchù)
Means "everywhere" or "in all directions."  Similar to 到处 (dàochù).

~
电话 (diànhuà)
Can refer to both the telephone itself and a telephone call. Note the different measure words used: 部 (bù) for the device, and 通 (tōng) for a call.

~
两边 (liǎngbiān)
Refers to both sides of something.

~
分行 (fēnháng)
Specifically refers to a branch of a bank or company.

~
凡是 (fánshì)
Emphasizes that something applies without exception.  Similar to "all" or "every."

~
偏 (piān)
Can describe a physical slant or tilt, as well as a biased or prejudiced viewpoint.

~
再次 (zàicì)
A more formal way of saying "once again."

~
宏大 (hóngdà)
Describes something grand and impressive in scale or scope, often used for plans, projects, or buildings.

~
知足 (zhīzú)
Means to be content or satisfied with what one has. Often used in the phrase 知足常乐 (zhīzúchánglè), meaning "contentment is happiness."

~
排行榜 (páihángbǎng)
Specifically refers to ranked lists, often used for things like music charts or best-selling products.

~
开头 (kāitóu)
Refers to the beginning or start of something.

~
办学 (bànxué)
Specifically refers to the act of running or managing a school, including aspects like administration, curriculum, and finances.

~
埋
This word is also used in the expression 埋怨 (mányuàn), which means "to blame" or "to complain."

~
珍贵
A similar word is 宝贵 (bǎoguì).  珍贵 emphasizes rarity and uniqueness, while 宝贵 emphasizes value and importance, often in a more abstract sense.  Something 宝贵 might be common, but still highly valued (like time, or life).  Something 珍贵 is usually rare, like a rare gem or an endangered animal.

~
鉴定
This can also be used to mean "authenticate" or "verify". For example, you can 鉴定 a piece of art.

~
处罚
This word carries a more formal and official tone than simply saying "punish." It often implies punishment by an authority or institution.

~
点名
This can mean to call roll, to mention someone by name, or to single someone out (for praise or criticism). The context usually makes it clear which meaning is intended.  For example, the sentence "老师点名批评了他" (lǎoshī diǎnmíng pīpíng le tā) means "The teacher criticized him by name."

~
管
The "particle similar to 把" usage is quite complex and is a grammar point that learners grapple with for a while. It is used to mark the object of the verb that follows. The object is then further described or acted upon. For example:

我把房间管干净了 (wǒ bǎ fángjiān guǎn gānjìng le) - I managed to get the room clean. / I took charge of getting the room clean.

~
补习
This word usually refers to supplemental lessons outside of regular school hours, like tutoring or cram school. It doesn't usually refer to simply reviewing material.

~
安乐死
This is a sensitive topic in Chinese culture, just as it is in many other cultures.

~
唱
Besides singing, 唱 can also be used for other vocalizations, such as shouting slogans or chanting prayers.

~
胶带
This term is broader than just "adhesive tape."  It can also refer to magnetic tape.

~
咳
This character represents the sound of a cough, a sigh, or an interjection like "oh," "damn," or "wow."

~
事后
This emphasizes looking back at an event *after* it has occurred, often to analyze or learn from it.

~
承办
This term emphasizes taking on the responsibility of organizing and managing an event or project.

~
脚印
Can also be used metaphorically, as in leaving one's mark on the world.

~
上演
This can be used for both stage plays and movies being shown in theaters.

~
眼看
Implies watching something happen with a sense of helplessness or inevitability, often something negative.

~
国庆
Refers specifically to the National Day of the People's Republic of China, celebrated on October 1st.

~
纯
Can also mean "skillful" or "practiced," often in the context of a craft or skill.

~
野
Can also mean "out of office" (e.g., 野鸡大学 - diploma mill).

~
内地
Specifically refers to mainland China (excluding Hong Kong, Macau, and Taiwan).

~
方针
Refers to guiding principles or policies, often related to government or organizational strategies.

~
窗口
Can also metaphorically refer to an opportunity or platform.

~
突破
Often implies overcoming significant challenges or barriers.

~
旅馆
A more modest term than 酒店 (jiǔdiàn), generally referring to smaller or simpler hotels.

~
重建
Often implies rebuilding after destruction or significant damage.

~
如
When used as "if," often followed by 果 (guǒ) to form 如果 (rúguǒ).

~
无边
Evokes a sense of vastness and limitlessness.

~
岛
Can refer to islands of various sizes, from small islets to large landmasses.

~
丰收
Usually refers to a bountiful harvest of crops, but can be used metaphorically for other kinds of success.

~
缘故
More formal than 原因 (yuányīn), often used in written language.

~
房屋
Refers to buildings in general, including houses and other structures.

~
举动
Refers to actions or behaviors, often with a focus on their outward manifestation.

~
违规
Implies violating established rules or regulations.

~
山峰
Specifically refers to the peak or summit of a mountain.

~
多媒体
Refers to the use of multiple forms of media, such as text, audio, and video.

~
高手
Implies a high level of skill or expertise in a particular area.

~
垃圾
Can also be used figuratively to describe something of poor quality or worthless.

~
单
As an adjective, can also mean "thin" or "weak," usually describing something flat or flimsy.

~
特大
Emphasizes exceptionally large size or magnitude.

~
水灾
Specifically refers to flooding or flood-related disasters.

~
再生
Can also mean "recycled", in the context of 再生纸 (recycled paper), 再生水 (recycled water), etc.

~
背后
Saying something 背后 means to say it out of earshot, i.e. when the person you're talking *about* can't hear you. If you're talking *to* someone, and someone else can't hear you, then you would use 私下 (sīxià).

~
熟
When used to mean "familiar", 熟 is usually paired with other characters. For example, 熟悉 (shúxī) means "to be familiar *with*". This word can also mean "ripe" or "cooked". Note that if something requires a lot of cooking, like a stew, then you would say that it is 熟烂 (shú làn).

~
莫言
莫言 is a relatively common name, but capitalized it refers to the Nobel-prize winning author.

~
皮
Has the colloquial meaning of "naughty", referring to children.

~
一齐
This word is more literary (书面) than 一起 (yīqǐ).

~
指标
Often used in economics contexts to mean economic indicators.

~
句
Note that there is no measure word for single-character words, only for sentences, which is 句.

~
轨道
Figuratively, this means "on the right path" or "on track."

~
户
This word is used as a measure word for families.

~
先锋
Also means "avant-garde", especially when used in relation to art.

~
座谈会
This kind of meeting involves lots of back-and-forth discussion. The usual way to translate meeting, 会议 (huìyì) is usually more one directional.

~
刚好
刚好 can also mean "by chance" or "coincidentally".

~
算
Has the colloquial meaning of "OK, nevermind", or "just forget about it", implying that the speaker is giving up on something.

~
试验
As a noun, 试验 is a more academic way of saying 实验 (shíyàn), although the dictionary definitions are the same.

~
罪
Often paired with other characters. For example, 犯罪 (fànzuì) means to commit a crime.

~
你们
This is always plural, unlike "you" in English.

~
两岸
Usually used to refer to the relationship between mainland China and Taiwan.

~
毕业生
Just means "graduate", but note that this refers to college graduates in mainland China, since secondary school is also called 毕业 (bìyè).

~
层次
Often used to refer to someone's social standing.

~
上周
Can also mean "the week before last."

~
花园
This word means a place with flowers, not necessarily a meticulously cultivated area.

~
穿上
This can only be used for clothing or armor. You can't use it to put on glasses, for example.

~
剪子
Note the 子 (zi) on the end. This character means "child," so 剪子 (jiǎnzi) literally translates to "scissors-child." Many tools in Chinese end with the character 子.

~
从不
Stronger than 不会 (bú huì), which means "won't".

~
走路
This word can also mean to leak information, or to travel on foot.

~
热水器
More formally called 热水器 (rèshuǐqì).

~
占据
Usually implies illegally occupying something.

~
贪钱
贪 (tān) can be applied to other things besides money. For example, 贪吃 (tān chī) means gluttonous, 贪玩 (tān wán) means addicted to playing, and 贪睡 (tān shuì) means to oversleep.


~
有用
有用 can also mean "effective."

~
平台
Colloquially means an online forum or bulletin board.

~
怨
As a verb, 怨 usually takes a direct object, such as the person who is being blamed. It's almost always followed by another clause.

~
向上
This word has seen a resurgence in official contexts in the 21st century, where it often signifies optimism or ideological purity. For example, the official response to COVID-19 has been described as "negative," while unapproved foreign vaccines are labeled as "positive."

~
深处
This can mean either a remote place, or figuratively, deep within someone's heart.

~
不能不
This is very strong, and almost like a command.

~
落实
Implies not only putting a policy into effect, but also following through and verifying that it worked.

~
涉及
Implies accidentally becoming related to or entangled with something.

~
西餐
This is usually eaten with a knife and fork. Note that some foods eaten in China, like hamburgers, aren't considered 西餐, since they can be eaten without utensils.

~
洗衣机
More formally 洗衣机 (xǐyījī).

~
开学
It can also mean "to begin a semester".

~
那边
那边 (nàbian) is often paired with 这边 (zhèbian), meaning "this side".  Together, they create a contrast, like "here" and "there".  You can also use 那边 independently to refer to a more distant or less specific location.  For example, 你把那个东西放那边吧 (nǐ bǎ nàge dōngxi fàng nàbian ba) - "Put that thing over there".

~
抄写
While 抄写 (chāoxiě) can mean simply "to copy", it often implies handwriting, as opposed to photocopying or digitally copying.  It can also carry a connotation of tedious or repetitive work, particularly when copying large amounts of text.

~
传达
传达 (chuándá) suggests conveying not just information, but also the underlying meaning or spirit of something.  It often involves interpretation or explanation.  For instance,  传达会议精神 (chuándá huìyì jīngshén) means "to convey the spirit of the meeting."

~
内在
内在 (nèizài) often contrasts with 外在 (wàizài) - "external" or "outward".  It refers to qualities that are inherent or intrinsic, rather than superficial.  For example,  内在美 (nèizài měi) means "inner beauty".

~
吉祥
吉祥 (jíxiáng) is often used in formal or traditional contexts, such as wishing someone a happy new year (吉祥如意 - jíxiáng rúyì).  It carries a stronger sense of good fortune and prosperity than simply "lucky".

~
一身
一身 (yīshēn) can have several meanings depending on context. It can refer to clothing (e.g., 他穿着一身黑 - tā chuānzhe yīshēn hēi - "He's wearing all black"), or one's whole body (e.g., 弄得一身汗 - nòng de yīshēn hàn - "To get covered in sweat"). It can also mean "alone" or "by oneself."

~
赛场
While 赛场 (sàichǎng) can refer to any competition venue, it is most commonly used for sporting events.  Think of it as a place where skills are tested and winners are determined.

~
非得 (fēiděi)
This implies a strong necessity or obligation. Often, the consequence of not doing the action is implied rather than stated outright. It can come off as pushy or demanding, so use carefully.  For example,  你非得现在走吗？ (nǐ fēiděi xiànzài zǒu ma?) - "Do you absolutely have to leave now?" The implied consequence is some sort of problem arising from the person leaving.


~
闭 (bì)
闭 (bì) is a more formal way to say "close" or "shut" compared to 关 (guān).  It's often used for eyes, mouth, or more abstract concepts like closing a meeting (闭幕 - bì mù).

~
完了 (wán le)
完了 has two main usages: indicating completion (e.g., 我吃完了 - wǒ chī wán le - "I've finished eating") or expressing a sense of despair or doom (e.g., 完了！我把钥匙丢了! - wán le! wǒ bǎ yàoshi diū le! - "Oh no! I've lost my keys!"). Pay attention to the context to distinguish the meaning.

~
仍 (réng)
仍 (réng) is more formal than 还是 (háishi) when expressing "still".  It's often used in writing or formal speeches.

~
之内 (zhī nèi)
Make sure to use 之内 after a phrase specifying the range, not directly after a number. For example,  三天之内 (sān tiān zhī nèi) - "within three days".

~
没用 (méiyòng)
没用 can be used before or after a noun. When used before, it means "useless". When used after, it means "it's no use" or "it won't work".  For example,  说也没用 (shuō yě méiyòng) - "It's no use talking."

~
成品 (chéngpǐn)
成品 specifically refers to a finished product, ready for sale or use, as opposed to raw materials or work-in-progress.

~
各位 (gèwèi)
各位 is a polite and formal way to address a group of people.  It's often used in speeches or formal announcements.

~
潮流 (cháoliú)
潮流 refers to a prevailing trend or current fashion, often implying something popular or stylish.

~
一番 (yīfān)
一番 can indicate a period of time or an instance of an action. It often suggests effort, experience, or a specific process.  For example,  一番努力 (yīfān nǔlì) - "a period of hard work."

~
心里 (xīnlǐ)
心里 emphasizes emotions and feelings, while 心中 (xīnzhoōng) is more about thoughts and ideas.  心里 is closer to "in one's heart", while 心中 is closer to "in one's mind".

~
名牌儿 (míngpáir)
名牌儿 specifically refers to a well-known or prestigious brand, implying high quality and status.

~
航空 (hángkōng)
航空 generally refers to all aspects of air travel and the aviation industry, including aircraft, airlines, and airports.

~
各个 (gège)
各个 emphasizes individuality and separateness, while 每个 (měige) focuses on every single member of a group.

~
新郎 (xīnláng)
新郎 is paired with 新娘 (xīniáng) - "bride".  Together they refer to the newlywed couple.

~
弯曲 (wānqū)
弯曲 describes something that is not straight, and can be used for both roads and objects.

~
不同 (bùtóng)
不同 is often followed by 的 (de) to indicate the specific aspect of difference.  For example,  不同的地方 (bùtóng de dìfang) - "different places."

~
大都 (dàdū)
大都 means "mostly" or "for the most part." Be careful not to confuse it with the ancient capital city also written as 大都.

~
支援 (zhīyuán)
支援 implies providing substantial help or support, often in a difficult or critical situation.  It can involve sending resources, personnel, or financial aid.

~
胡子 (húzi)
胡子 can refer to both a mustache and a beard. To specify, use 鬍鬚 (húxū) for mustache and 鬍子 for beard. However, in colloquial speech, 胡子 is commonly understood as beard.


~
挨 (āi)
挨 has two distinct meanings: to be next to/close to (e.g., 挨着坐 - āizhe zuò - "to sit next to each other") and to suffer/endure (e.g., 挨饿 - āi è - "to suffer from hunger").  Context is crucial for understanding the intended meaning.

~
患者 (huànzhě)
患者 is a more formal and medical term for "patient" compared to 病人 (bìngrén).

~
避 (bì)
避 implies actively avoiding something unpleasant or dangerous.

~
汉字 (hànzì)
汉字 refers specifically to Chinese characters, not just any Chinese writing.

~
无关 (wúguān)
无关 is often followed by 与 (yǔ) or 和 (hé) to indicate what something is unrelated to.  For example,  无关紧要 (wúguān jǐnyào) - "unimportant" or "irrelevant".

~
平坦 (píngtǎn)
平坦 describes a surface that is flat and even, often used for roads or land.

~
一路 (yīlù)
一路 can mean "all the way" (e.g., 一路平安 - yīlù píng'ān - "have a safe journey") or describe things of the same kind (e.g.,  一路货色 - yīlù huòsè - "goods of the same kind").

~
没事儿 (méishìr)
没事儿 can be used as a response to an apology ("it's okay"), to indicate having free time ("I'm free"), or to downplay a situation ("it's nothing").

~
之外 (zhīwài)
之外 means "outside of" or "besides." It is often used with 除...之外 (chú... zhīwài), meaning "except for..."

~
外科 (wàikē)
外科 specifically refers to surgical departments or the surgical branch of medicine.

~
空儿 (kòngr)
空儿 is a colloquial term for free time or spare time, similar to 空闲时间 (kòngxián shíjiān).

~
科技 (kē jì)
科技 is a shortened form of 科学技术 (kēxué jìshù), referring to science and technology as a unified concept.

~
这样 (zhèyàng)
这样 can mean "like this", "this way", or "in this manner." It can also be used to introduce a suggestion or conclusion.

~
智力
智力 is more often used to refer to intelligence as a measurable quantity, like on an IQ test.  For general intelligence or cleverness, 聪明 (cōngming) is more common.

~
记
As a verb, it can mean "to take notes" or "to write down."  It can also mean "to memorize." Be aware of the different contexts.  As a noun, it can mean a mark or symbol.

~
延伸
This emphasizes extending in space or length.  It can be concrete or abstract, referring to, say, a road or influence.  It can be distinguished from 延长 (yáncháng), which focuses on making something *longer* in time or space.  It's also different from 扩展 (kuòzhǎn), which is about expanding in scope or influence, often outward in multiple directions.

~
一行
一行 (yī xíng) specifically refers to a group of people traveling together, often for a specific purpose like a business trip or diplomatic mission. It doesn't refer to a line of text.  A more general word for a group would be 一群 (yī qún).

~
直到
直到 emphasizes the duration up to a specific point. It often pairs with 才 (cái), highlighting that something *only* happened at that point.  For example, 我直到十点才睡觉 (Wǒ zhídào shí diǎn cái shuìjiào) means "I didn't sleep until 10 o'clock," emphasizing that 10 o'clock was the point at which sleep finally occurred.

~
盗版
盗版 literally translates to "pirate edition", implying that it's illegal.  The legal equivalent is 正版 (zhèngbǎn).

~
故乡
This carries a stronger emotional connotation than just 家乡 (jiāxiāng). It refers to one's birthplace and often evokes feelings of nostalgia and longing.

~
电车
Depending on the context, this can refer to either trams/streetcars or trolleybuses.  In some regions, it might even refer to light rail. Pay attention to the local usage.

~
侵犯
侵犯 is a more serious violation than 违反 (wéifǎn). It implies encroaching upon someone's rights or territory.

~
开展
This suggests a dynamic and ongoing process of development or expansion, like unfolding a plan.  It's often used with activities or campaigns.  This is in contrast to 发展 (fāzhǎn), which refers to growth or progress more generally.

~
发射
Besides its literal meaning, 发射 can also refer to the launching of a project or program.

~
音像
音像 (yīnxiàng) refers to both audio and video recordings.  It's more encompassing than just "audio" or "video" individually.

~
带动
This implies a driving or pulling force that leads to movement or progress in something else.  It suggests that one action stimulates another.

~
出门
This specifically means to leave one's house or place of residence.  It doesn't just mean to go outside within, say, a gated community.

~
路上
Besides its literal meaning, 路上 can also mean "on the way" figuratively, as in "on the way to achieving something."

~
示范
示范 goes beyond simply demonstrating. It implies setting an example or serving as a model for others to follow.

~
一口气
This can also refer to doing something without a break or pause, in a single continuous effort.  For example, reading a book in one sitting.

~
水泥
水泥 specifically refers to cement.  混凝土 (hùnníngtǔ) is the word for concrete.

~
室
This character has multiple meanings, including "room," "work unit," even "grave." Pay close attention to the context.

~
尖脸
尖脸 isn't necessarily a negative description.  It simply means a pointed or narrow face shape.

~
国内
This refers to matters within a country's borders.  It is the opposite of 国外 (guówài), meaning "overseas" or "abroad."

~
宝宝
While it means "baby," it's often used as a term of endearment for loved ones, not just infants.

~
起诉
This specifically means to initiate legal proceedings.  It's distinct from 控告 (kònggào), which means to accuse or report someone to the authorities, not necessarily in a formal court setting.

~
生
When used with dates, 生 means to be born.  For example,  1990 年生 (yī jiǔ jiǔ líng nián shēng) means "born in 1990".

~
齐全
齐全 emphasizes everything being present and accounted for, not just a general sense of completeness.

~
收购
This implies a complete takeover or acquisition, often of a company or a large quantity of goods. It carries more weight than just buying something.

~
机构
机构 refers to a more formal organization, often with a specific function, like a government agency or a research institute. It differs from 组织 (zǔzhī), which can refer to any organized group of people.

~
相声
相声 is a traditional Chinese comedic performance involving two performers engaging in witty banter and wordplay. It relies heavily on cultural references and puns.

~
送行
This refers to the act of seeing someone off, often at the beginning of a journey.

~
止
Be aware that this character is used in words with opposing meanings, such as 停止 (tíngzhǐ, "to stop") and不止 (bùzhǐ, "not limited to"). Context is crucial.

~
要么
要么…要么… presents two mutually exclusive options.  It emphasizes a choice between the two.

~
环
Besides its meanings related to circular shapes, 环 can also be used in words related to the environment, such as 环境 (huánjìng, "environment").

~
品质
品质 refers to the inherent nature or character of something, often suggesting high quality or moral standards.  It goes deeper than just the superficial characteristics.

~
天堂
While it literally means "heaven," it can also be used more metaphorically to describe a place of great beauty or happiness.

~
城区
城区 is the main built-up area of a city, distinct from surrounding suburbs or rural areas.

~
会员
会员 specifically denotes membership in an organization or group.

~
男子
男子 generally refers to an adult male, not a boy.

~
复苏
复苏 implies a revival or recovery from a weakened or dormant state. It often describes economic recovery or the return of something lost.

~
深厚
This describes something profound, deep-rooted, or substantial. It can refer to knowledge, feelings, or even physical things like a thick layer of snow.

~
托
托 (tuō) has many meanings, but the most common meaning is to hold something up from underneath. Be careful not to confuse this with 托 (tuō) meaning "to entrust", which has a different tone.

~
延续
延续 (yánxù) emphasizes the *uninterrupted* continuation of something.  It suggests that something carries on without a break or interruption, often for a significant duration. Think of things like traditions, legacies, or processes that persist over time.  It's different from 继续 (jìxù) which just means to continue.

~
比方
比方 (bǐfang) introduces an *analogy* or *figurative example*.  It's used to explain something complex by comparing it to something more familiar or easily understood. Think of it as similar to saying "for instance" or "let's say" in English.

~
充足
充足 (chōngzú) describes something *more than sufficient*, an *abundance*. It goes beyond merely meeting the requirements; there's a sense of ample supply.  It's stronger than 够 (gòu) which only means "enough".

~
解说
解说 (jiěshuō) specifically refers to an *oral explanation*, often accompanying a demonstration, performance, or exhibit. Think of a museum guide, sports commentator, or someone explaining a procedure.

~
股东
A 股东 (gǔdōng) is specifically a *shareholder in a company*. It is different from other more general terms that might be translated to "member."

~
职能
职能 (zhínéng) emphasizes the *specific duties and powers* associated with a particular position or role.  It refers to the inherent capabilities and responsibilities of a job or an organ within a system.  This is different from 职责 (zhízé) which is more generally responsibility.

~
全新
全新 (quánxīn) emphasizes that something is *completely new, from beginning to end*.  It suggests a fresh start or a total renovation, not just a minor update.

~
这边
这边 (zhèbiān) is best translated as "over here" or "on this side". It has a more specific spatial meaning than simply "here".

~
父女
父女 (fùnǚ) refers specifically to the relationship between a *father and daughter*, not just any parent-child relationship.

~
紧紧
紧紧 (jǐnjǐn) describes something held or done *very tightly or closely*, with a sense of firmness and urgency.

~
心中
心中 (xīnzōng) refers to one's *innermost thoughts and feelings*, often private or unspoken.  It's more evocative than simply saying "in mind".

~
猛
猛 (měng) is often used to describe something done with sudden, intense force or ferocity.  It can refer to physical actions as well as sudden changes.  If something is 猛烈 (měngliè), it is powerful and intense.

~
迷信 (míxìn) emphasizes *irrational* belief, often involving supernatural or unfounded ideas.

~
梅花 (méihuā) can refer to both the *plum blossom* and the *wintersweet flower*.  Context is important to determine the specific meaning. Also, unlike the plum blossom which appears in the early spring, the wintersweet flower appears in the middle of winter. Also, it can refer to the suit of "clubs" in cards.

~
风 (fēng) has many meanings beyond just "wind", including *style, custom, manner, atmosphere*. Pay attention to context.

~
宝石 (bǎoshí) refers specifically to a *precious stone* used in jewelry, not just any rock.

~
录 (lù) has several meanings, from "record" and "copy" to less common uses like "to carve wood". Context is crucial.

~
usb
USB is generally written as "优盘" (U-disk) or just U盘 for short. The former is usually used for describing the technology as a whole while the later is specifically a physical USB flash drive.

~
利 (lì) covers a broad spectrum of "advantage" or "benefit", from sharpness to profit and interest. Context will dictate the specific nuance.

~
随意 (suíyì) suggests a lack of constraint or formality, doing things *as one pleases*, rather than simply "random".

~
心脏病 (xīnzàngbìng) refers specifically to *heart disease*, not just any medical condition affecting the chest area.

~
棉 (mián) is a generic term for cotton or kapok, used in various contexts from clothing to padding.

~
院子 (yuànzi) is a general term for an enclosed outdoor space, typically a *courtyard* or *yard*, attached to a house.

~
震惊 (zhènjīng) implies a profound and unsettling shock, often due to unexpected or disturbing news.

~
报警 (bàojǐng) specifically means to *report something to the police* or to sound an alarm, not just any kind of warning.

~
收藏 (shōucáng) emphasizes the careful *collecting and preserving* of valuable items, beyond simply putting something away.

~
愁 (chóu) is a feeling of *worry, anxiety, or sadness*, often related to specific concerns.

~
产业 (chǎnyè) refers to a specific branch of *economic activity or production*, like the tourism industry or the manufacturing industry.

~
从中 (cóngzhōng) means "from within" or "from among," highlighting the origin of something from a larger group or body.

~
若 (ruò) can function as both "if" and "like/as", sometimes making its meaning ambiguous.  Pay close attention to the sentence structure.

~
面向 (miànxiàng) describes something *oriented towards* or *intended for* a particular group or purpose.

~
同 (tóng) can mean both "same" and "together." Context is key to understanding its usage.  Also, note that 同 is a component of some more complicated words like 衚衕/胡同 (hútòng), an alleyway or lane.

~
左 (zuǒ) can also mean "east," "unorthodox," or even "wrong" in certain contexts, besides its primary meaning of "left."

~
漫长 (màncháng) specifically emphasizes the *tedious or seemingly endless duration* of something, rather than just its length.

~
薯条 (shǔtiáo) specifically refers to *french fries*, not just any type of potato dish.

~
儿女 (érnǚ) refers to *sons and daughters* collectively, not children in general.


~
早饭 (zǎofàn) specifically means *breakfast*.

~
毫升 (háoshēng) is a unit of volume, specifically *milliliters*.

~
提交 (tíjiāo) implies formally *presenting or submitting something for review or consideration*, often a document or proposal.

~
知名

知名 (zhīmíng) is more formal than "famous".  A better translation might be "well-known" or "renowned".  It's often used in formal contexts, like news reports or academic writing.  For everyday conversation,  有名 (yǒumíng) is more common.

~
没什么

没什么 (méishénme) is a versatile phrase.  While it can mean "it's nothing" or "you're welcome", it can also be used to downplay one's own accomplishments or possessions when complimented. This is similar to saying "it's not a big deal" or "it was nothing special".

~
修养

修养 (xiūyǎng) refers to self-cultivation,  specifically the cultivation of one's moral character and personal refinement. It goes beyond simply having good manners and encompasses inner qualities like patience, integrity, and humility.  It implies a conscious effort to improve oneself ethically and spiritually.

~
空军

空军 (kōngjūn) specifically refers to the air force as a branch of the military.  While it can technically encompass all air-related military operations, it doesn't include civilian aviation or other non-military uses of aircraft.

~
繁殖

繁殖 (fánzhí) is generally used for biological reproduction in animals and plants.  While it can sometimes be used metaphorically,  it's not typically used for things like copying documents or data.  For those contexts,  复制 (fùzhì) or  拷贝 (kǎobèi) are more appropriate.

~
客气

客气 (kèqì) is often used in situations where English speakers might say "you're welcome" or "don't mention it". It can also express humility, like when someone downplays a compliment.  Overusing 客气 can sometimes sound insincere.

~
来源

来源 (láiyuán) emphasizes the origin or source of something, often information or resources. It suggests a point of origin that can be traced back.  For example, you might ask about the 来源 of a news story or the 来源 of funding for a project.

~
交易

交易 (jiāoyì) generally refers to a business transaction or exchange of goods or services for money.  It implies a more formal or official exchange than simply buying something at a store.

~
母鸡
